401 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Petty v. Crowell


NO. 5-98-0766


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


306 Ill. App. 3d 774; 715 N.E.2d 317; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 555; 239 Ill. Dec. 872



August 4, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Union County. No. 98-L-21. Honorable D.D. Bigler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Union County (Illinois) which dismissed his negligence claim against the defendants, city and driver, and determined that the defendants had immunity from liability for a court-ordered community service participant's injuries that resulted from an employee's negligence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a negligence action seeking damages for injuries he sustained when he was struck by a vehicle owned by defendant city and driven by its employee, defendant driver. Defendants filed a dismissal motion and argued that both were immune from liability for plaintiff's injuries because plaintiff was allegedly injured while performing court-ordered community service. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss, from which plaintiff appealed. The court held that the plain language of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-7 clearly provided a municipality and its employee immunity from liability for injuries caused or sustained by court-ordered community service participants, absent allegations of wilful, wanton misconduct, or gross negligence. The court held that the statute barred the plaintiff's negligence claim. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which dismissed plaintiff's negligence claim because defendants were entitled to immunity from liability for injuries caused or sustained by court-ordered community service participants, absent allegations of wilful, wanton misconduct or gross negligence.

 

402 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Malchow


No. 2-98-0576


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


306 Ill. App. 3d 665; 714 N.E.2d 583; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 529; 239 Ill. Dec. 664



July 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 24, 1999. Released for Publication August 24, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 97--CF--3372. Honorable George Bridges, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that convicted him of failing to register as a sex offender as required by the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by indictment with unlawful failure to register as a sex offender, as required by the Sex Offender Registration Act (Act), 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq. The trial court denied defendant's motion to declare the Act unconstitutional and to dismiss the charges against him. Pursuant to a stipulated bench trial, the trial court found defendant guilty, imposed sentence, and denied defendant's motion for a new trial. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the Act. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, rejecting defendant's ex post facto, cruel and unusual punishment, right to privacy, double jeopardy, due process, equal protection, and single-subject rule arguments. With respect to defendant's sentence, however, the appellate court reversed and remanded. The trial court's failure to impose the mandatory minimum period of confinement in the county jail, as required by § 10 of the Act, rendered defendant's sentence void and illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction; the court reversed defendant's sentence and remanded for sentencing only, on the ground that the sentence imposed by the trial court was illegal and void.

 

403 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. Kirksey


No. 1-98-4759


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 912; 715 N.E.2d 669; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 521; 239 Ill. Dec. 915



July 19, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Kathy M. Flanagan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a mother on behalf of herself and her injured daughter, appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion of defendants, a city and a crossing guard, to dismiss all allegations against them in the personal injury action brought by plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, a mother on behalf of herself and her daughter, brought a personal injury action against defendants, a city and a crossing guard. Plaintiffs alleged that the daughter was injured when a vehicle struck her while she crossed a street manned by defendant crossing guard. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss all allegations against them. On appeal, plaintiffs contended that the trial court erred in finding that defendants' conduct was immunized under § 4-102 of the Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat.10/4-102 (1996). Defendants contended that § 4-102 granted them immunity from precisely that type of cause of action. The court held that the plain language of § 4-102 stated that a municipality and its employees could not be liable for their failure to provide adequate police protection or service and found this language controlling. Therefore, plaintiffs' allegations fell within the police protection services that were part of the common law "public duty" rule and that were codified in § 4-102. Therefore, because the trial court properly dismissed plaintiffs' complaint, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiffs' complaint for personal injury because defendants, a city and a crossing guard, could not be held liable under the Tort Immunity Act for their failure to provide adequate police protection or service.

 

404 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Board of Managers of Weathersfield Condo. Ass'n v. Schaumburg Ltd. Pshp.


No. 1-98-1053


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


307 Ill. App. 3d 614; 717 N.E.2d 429; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 516; 240 Ill. Dec. 336



July 16, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended on Denial of Rehearing September 30, 1999. Released for Publication October 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable David Lichtenstein, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting defendants' motions to strike and dismiss plaintiffs' fourth amended complaint pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-615 (1996).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, board of managers of a condominium association, alleged that defendants, limited partnerships, owed plaintiffs a fiduciary duty to budget, collect and set aside reasonable reserves for capital expenditures and deferred maintenance for the repair or replacement of common elements, and that defendants failed to establish reasonable reserves for the replacement of capital improvements. Defendants should have known that plaintiffs' obligations could not be met without an adequate contribution of reserve funds. Plaintiffs adequately pled damages; the facts established that the money plaintiffs had in reserve was an unreasonably small amount in relation to their needs, and what constituted reasonable reserves should have been determined by the trier of fact. Plaintiffs sufficiently alleged a cause of action under the Consumer Fraud Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/1 et seq. (1996). Defendants had a fiduciary and statutory duty to maintain adequate reserves and to disclose the status of the reserve account.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded; defendants had a duty to assess a particular amount to establish a certain level of reserves, defendants owed a fiduciary duty to plaintiffs, it was equitable to allow current owners or the plaintiffs to recover for defendants' alleged failure to accumulate reserves.

Woodstock Hunt Club v. Hindi


No. 2-98-1327


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


305 Ill. App. 3d 1074; 713 N.E.2d 824; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 505; 239 Ill. Dec. 293


April 15, 1999, Assigned; June 28, 1999, Submitted  
July 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 96--CH--375. Honorable Michael T. Caldwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which denied their motion to dissolve a permanent injunction and to dismiss the plaintiff hunters' claim. Plaintiffs alleged that defendants interfered with the plaintiffs' goose hunt contrary to the Hunter Interference Prohibition Act, (Act) 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 125/2.


OVERVIEW: The defendants used various noisemakers to stop the plaintiffs, hunt club members, from hunting geese. The plaintiffs, under the authority of Hunter Interference Prohibition Act, (Act) 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 125/2, obtained a permanent injunction against the defendants. The injunction prohibited the defendants from interfering with hunters engaged in the lawful taking of wild animals. The defendants moved to dissolve the injunction and to dismiss the plaintiffs' claim. They argued that the remaining portion of the statute was an unconstitutional infringement on speech. The court affirmed the permanent injunction and found the Act was constitutional because the statute was a reasonable restriction on the time, place, and manner of protected speech; that the restriction was content neutral; and that there were alternative methods of communication available.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the defendants' motion to dissolve a permanent injunction and to dismiss the plaintiffs' claim because it found that the hunter interference act was constitutional.

Goodwin v. McHenry County Sheriff's Office Merit Comm'n


No. 2-98-1604


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


306 Ill. App. 3d 251; 713 N.E.2d 818; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 507; 239 Ill. Dec. 287


February 24, 1999, Assigned  
July 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 98--CH--435. Honorable Terrence J. Brady, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sheriff appealed an order from the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion for reconsideration and ordered that its stay over defendant merit commission's proceeding regarding disciplinary charges against plaintiff employee would remain in effect until the disposition of the related criminal case pending against plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sheriff filed disciplinary charges against plaintiff employee seeking her removal. Plaintiff was also indicted in a related criminal case for felony theft charges. Plaintiff filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, sheriff and merit commission, seeking to enjoin defendant merit commission from hearing the disciplinary charges. She also filed a motion for preliminary injunction. The trial court entered an order prohibiting the merit commission from hearing the matter until further order. It then denied defendants' motion for reconsideration and ordered that its stay would remain in effect until the disposition of the criminal case. Defendant sheriff appealed. The court held the trial court abused its discretion in granting the stay because plaintiff had not exhausted her administrative remedies and had not requested a stay asserting privilege against self-incrimination. Furthermore, there was no absolute prohibition against simultaneous administrative disciplinary proceedings and related criminal proceedings. Thus, the order was reversed and the matter was remanded with instructions to dismiss the complaint.


OUTCOME: Order staying defendant merit commission's proceedings on defendant sheriff's disciplinary charges against plaintiff employee was reversed and the matter was remanded with instructions to dismiss plaintiff's complaint because plaintiff failed to exhaust her administrative remedies, she had not requested a stay, and there was no absolute prohibition against simultaneous disciplinary and related criminal proceedings.

 

407 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


DeWoskin v. Lowe's Chicago Cinema


No. 1-98-1971


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 504; 714 N.E.2d 1047; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 504; 239 Ill. Dec. 750



July 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE THOMAS P. QUINN and LESTER A. BONAGURO, JUDGES PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from the judgment of Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), dismissing his complaint and determining that the Cook County (Illinois) Amusement Tax Ordinance was not an occupational tax, prohibited by Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e), and its exemptions were reasonable and did not violate the uniformity clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2, or the equal protection clauses, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer purchased a movie ticket and paid the required amusement tax, thereby establishing standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Cook County (Illinois) Amusement Tax Ordinance. Defendant county officials moved to dismiss plaintiff's subsequent complaint for lack of standing and failure to state a claim under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. §§ 5/2-615 and 5/2-619. Plaintiff was found to have standing, but the complaint was dismissed. Plaintiff appealed. In affirming in part, the court ruled that the tax imposed was not an occupational tax that was prohibited by Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e), and the exemptions to the tax scheme did not violate the equal protection clauses, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, since there was a rational basis for the exemptions. Also, those exemptions that were granted for patrons of non-commercial organizations that served the community were reasonable and did not violate the uniformity clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2. In reversing and remanding with respect to the other exemptions, the court ruled that whether they were reasonable was a factual question that could not be disposed of by a § 2-615 motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the complaint was affirmed in part because the ordinance did not impose a tax on occupations; the tax scheme did not violate equal protection; and the exemptions for non-commercial organizations that served the community were reasonable and did not violate the uniformity clause. The judgment was reversed with respect to the other exemptions because a factual issue existed as to whether they were reasonable and justified.

Michigan Ave. Nat'l Bank v. County of Cook


No. 1-98-1974


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 392; 714 N.E.2d 1010; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 466; 239 Ill. Dec. 713



June 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 20, 1999. Released for Publication August 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Sophia H. Hall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendants' motion for summary judgment in plaintiff's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, as special administrator of the estate of the deceased, filed a medical malpractice lawsuit against the county, the county hospital, two doctors, and three nurses. Plaintiff alleged that defendants failed to order a mammogram, failed to diagnose decedent's condition of breast cancer, and failed to perform examinations on decedent. Defendants moved for summary judgment, contending that they were immune from liability under 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/6-105 (1992)(Tort Immunity Act). Two of the nurses were dismissed as defendants. The trial court granted summary judgment to the remaining defendants. Plaintiff appealed, arguing that defendants were not immune from liability. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in defendant's favor. The court found defendants were immune from liability under 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/6-105, because it provided immunity to local public entities and public employees who failed to make a physical or mental examination or failed to make an adequate physical or mental examination. The court disagreed with plaintiff that immunity was limited to preventive public heath examinations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in defendants' favor, agreeing that defendants, as public employees, were immune from the liability plaintiff was claiming in her complaint.

Houlihan v. City of Chicago


No. 1-97-1514


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 589; 714 N.E.2d 569; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 481; 239 Ill. Dec. 650



June 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 5, 1999. Released for Publication August 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in their action against defendant city alleging that the city failed to comply with the requirements of the Illinois Pension Code, 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-1-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Participants in the city of Chicago's municipal employee's pension funds brought suit as a derivative and class action against the city, alleging that the city failed to comply with the requirements of the Illinois Pension Code, 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-1-1 et seq., by not paying interest on money collected for the city's municipal pension funds. The city filed a motion to dismiss. The circuit court granted the motion to dismiss with prejudice. The court affirmed, holding that the pension code did not require the city to make interest payments to the pension funds when it contributed the statutory maximum under the statute. The court also found that the city did not have an obligation to exercise its home rule powers to raise additional monies when the city had already contributed the statutory maximum to the pension funds. The court also found the city did not violate plaintiffs' rights under the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of plaintiffs' complaint, disagreeing with plaintiffs that the city had an obligation to exercise its home rule powers to raise additional monies and that the city had an obligation to make interest payments to the pension funds. The court also found that the city did not violate plaintiffs' rights under the Illinois Constitution.

 

410 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kalwa


No. 1-97-1671


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 601; 714 N.E.2d 1023; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 485; 239 Ill. Dec. 726



June 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 19, 1999. Released for Publication August 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Cook of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of first degree murder and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and armed robbery and was sentenced to concurrent prison terms of one hundred years and thirty years, respectively. Defendant contended that he should have been granted a new trial because he was taking psychotropic medication during the trial, but never received a fitness hearing. He also contended that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the offense of armed robbery took place in Cook County, as charged in the indictment. The court held that the record proved that the trial court did everything that it possibly could to further investigate defendant's fitness for trial. The trial court ordered a fitness exam and defendant was found fit to stand trial. During numerous and protracted post-trial proceedings, the trial court repeatedly told defendant and defense counsel that there was no indication observed by the trial court or brought to its attention by any party that defendant was ever unable to cooperate with defense counsel or that defendant was unable to comprehend the nature of the proceedings. Thus, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court convicted defendant of first degree murder and armed robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling because there was no substantial evidence presented before the court to prove that defendant was unfit to stand trial.

 

411 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


KANNE v. BULKEY


No. 1-98-0597


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 1036; 715 N.E.2d 784; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 491; 240 Ill. Dec. 97



June 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 6, 1999. Released For Publication September 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Kathy M. Flanagan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion for summary judgment in medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed action against three physicians, alleging negligence in failing to diagnose prostate cancer. Plaintiff dismissed the claims against two defendants. The remaining defendant moved for summary judgment, stating that plaintiff filed his lawsuit after both the applicable statute of limitations and statute of repose expired. The circuit court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment. Plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed, finding that because the case was failure-to-diagnose, the omission was deemed to have occurred on the date defendant rendered his final treatment. Plaintiff testified that he never received any treatment from defendant after June of 1992. Therefore, plaintiff's claim was extinguished in June of 1996, two months before he filed his complaint. Thus, the trial court did not err in finding that the four-year statute of repose for medical malpractice actions barred plaintiff's complaint. The court also disagreed with plaintiff that the statute of repose, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212(a), was forbidden special legislation and violated state and federal constitutional rights, including access to the courts, equal protection, and due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant, because the claim was barred by the four-year statute of repose for medical malpractice actions.

 

412 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Zygmuntowicz v. Pepper Constr. Co.


No. 1-97-4636


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 182; 713 N.E.2d 777; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 447; 239 Ill. Dec. 246



June 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Walter J. Kowalski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant store appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that apportioned liability between it and co-defendant, general contractor, in a negligence action by plaintiff employee.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee slipped and fell while working at defendant store. Plaintiff filed a negligence action against defendants, store and general contractor. Defendant general contractor filed a third-party contribution action against plaintiff's employer. Plaintiff and defendant general contractor settled, and defendant general contractor filed a motion to apportion liability between it and defendant store. The lower court apportioned liability with 70 percent to defendant general contractor and 30 percent to defendant store. Defendant store appealed, alleging that the lower court lacked jurisdiction to apportion liability. The court agreed and reversed the apportionment order. The court held that the lower court did not have jurisdiction, nor the authority to apportion liability between these two defendants because defendant general contractor never cross-claimed against defendant store for contribution. The court held that without a formal pleading putting the question of liability between the defendants at issue, the court lacked the authority to apportion liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that apportioned liability between the defendants, store and general contractor, because defendant general contractor failed to file a cross-claim against defendant store for contribution; therefore the lower court lacked jurisdiction and authority to order any apportionment of liability.

Meza v. Lisa Rodriguez & Children's Home


No. 2-98-1140


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


305 Ill. App. 3d 777; 713 N.E.2d 764; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 452; 239 Ill. Dec. 233


April 15, 1999, Assigned  
June 25, 1999, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 97--AD--127, 97--F--148, 97--F--323. Honorable Patrick L. Heaslip, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) denying his motion to reconsider the dismissal of his complaint to establish parental relationship after executing a surrender, pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/0.01 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father executed a written surrender of parental rights as a response to consolidated proceedings filed by appellee mother intending to place the minor child of the marriage into adoption. In addition to the surrender, appellant completed a parental affidavit form indicating that he had read the surrender document and understood its content. Thereafter, appellant sought to void or revoke consent to the adoption. Appellees moved to dismiss appellant's complaint, arguing that appellant's surrender was irrevocable. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, appellant contended that his mental health prompted his alleged surrender. The court determined that appellant was informed that his surrender was irrevocable and that conformity of the document to the requirements of 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/0.01 et seq., strengthened the irrevocability of the surrender. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellees.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant's motion to reconsider the dismissal of his complaint to establish a parental relationship was affirmed because appellant's surrender of parental rights was irrevocable.

Van Harken v. City of Chicago


No. 1-98-0667


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


305 Ill. App. 3d 972; 713 N.E.2d 754; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 441; 239 Ill. Dec. 223



June 24, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing their complaint that the Chicago Municipal Code § 9-100-010 et seq., under which they were fined for parking violations, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff drivers received parking tickets pursuant to an ordinance promulgated by defendant city pursuant to Chicago Municipal Code § 9-100-010 et seq. Each of plaintiffs received a fine and, instead of seeking judicial review, plaintiffs filed a class action suit in federal court, seeking a declaration that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The federal claims were dismissed and plaintiffs brought a state claim, contending that the administrative process for reviewing parking violations improperly delegated a judicial function to private attorneys, thereby violating the Due Process Clause and the Separation of Powers Clause of the state constitution, Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. The trial court dismissed the claim. On appeal, the court determined that the administrative actions were subject to judicial review. Thus, the court held that the ordinance did not violate the constitution and affirmed the decision of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing plaintiff's complaint challenging a parking ordinance was affirmed because the ordinance did not violated the constitution because the administrative process was subject to judicial review.

 

415 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stork


No. 2-98-0667


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


305 Ill. App. 3d 714; 713 N.E.2d 187; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 424; 238 Ill. Dec. 941


May 17, 1999, Submitted  
June 18, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 22, 1999. Released for Publication July 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 98--CF--115. Honorable Christopher C. Starck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for unlawful entry of school property by a child sex offender in violation of 720 ILCS 5/11-9.2 from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a convicted child molester, entered a school for getting permission to distribute literature about his disk jockey business. Defendant was convicted of violating 720 ILCS 5/11-9.2, which prohibited entry of school property, by a child sex offender. Defendant appealed his conviction, and the court affirmed. Defendant challenged his conviction on both procedural and substantive due process grounds. The court disagreed that defendant's procedural due process rights were violated because there was no right, inherent or constitutional, to transact personal business on public school property. The court also found no violation of defendant's substantive due process rights because under that rational basis test, the law was reasonable related to the purpose of protecting school children from known child sex offenders. The court also dismissed defendant's argument that the law was vague as applied to him. A law was vague only when persons of normal intelligence must guess as to its meaning and differ as to its application.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for violating law which prohibited entry of school property by a child sex offender was affirmed because neither defendant's procedural or substantive due process rights were violated. Entry onto public school property to transact personal business was not a protected activity. Also, the law was a reasonable means of protecting the legitimate government interest of protecting school children from sex offenders.

 

416 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


E&E Hauling v. Ryan


No. 1-97-3174


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 131; 713 N.E.2d 178; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 415; 238 Ill. Dec. 932



June 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 30, 1999. Released for Publication July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 93 L 50050. The Honorable Joanne L. Lanigan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that an increase in paid-in capital from push-down accounting adjustments to plaintiff's balance sheet after a stock sale and a 26 U.S.C.S. § 338 election was a statutory increase in paid-in capital for franchise tax purposes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporation protested its payment of an assessment for franchise taxes following a stock sale between plaintiff's former and new sole shareholder that increased plaintiff's paid-in capital by nearly $ 58 million. The court affirmed the order, finding that an increase in paid-in capital from push-down accounting adjustments to a corporation's balance sheet after a stock sale and a 26 U.S.C.S. § 338 election was a statutory transfer to paid-in capital and subject to franchise tax under 806 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1.80(j) (1.80(j)) (1996). The court held that because there was an increase in paid-in capital, there was sufficient shareholder action to meet the 5/1.80(j) requirements. The court found that paid-in capital included amounts added or transferred into the paid-in capital account by internal transactions. The court noted that the uniformity clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970), was not violated because all domestic corporations paid franchise taxes, and therefore 5/1.80(j) applied to all corporations when determining the amount of paid-in capital. The court held that this was a rational system of capitalization and a proper basis to determine the franchise tax.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed that found an increase in paid-in capital from push-down accounting adjustments to plaintiff corporation's balance sheet following a stock sale and tax election was a statutory increase in paid-in capital for franchise tax purposes. The court ruled that the uniformity clause was not violated because the tax was applied to all corporations, and was a proper basis to determine the tax.

 

417 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Consolidated Freightways Corp. v. Human Rights Comm'n


No. 1-97-0919


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


305 Ill. App. 3d 934; 713 N.E.2d 148; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 388; 238 Ill. Dec. 902



June 9, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CH 10798. Honorable Aaron Jaffe, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County, (Illinois), which granted appellees, the Illinois Human Rights Commission and the Department of Human Rights, motion to dismiss appellant's complaint for injunctive relief in a Human Rights Act action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee employee filed a discrimination charge against appellant employer pursuant to the Human Rights Act. 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 1/1-101, et seq. Later appellee employee signed a settlement agreement. Appellee Illinois Human Rights Commission (IHRC) approved the agreement. Appellee employee later alleged that he signed the agreement under duress. Appellee Department of Human Rights (DHR) responded by withdrawing the agreement from appellee IHRC consideration. Appellant sought an injunction seeking to compel enforcement of the agreement and appellees filed a motion to dismiss. The lower court granted appellees' motion. The court affirmed, holding that the exhaustion doctrine only permitted a party to bypass administrative review when an administrative agency entered an order it had no authority to enter; and appellees IHRC and DHR's order was clearly within the scope of its authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant employer's request for injunction because appellees IHRC and DHR's order was clearly within the scope of its authority. The exhaustion doctrine only permitted a party to bypass administrative review when an agency entered an order without authority to do so.

 

418 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


CGE Ford Heights v. Miller


No. 1-97-2121 and 1-97-2384, Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 431; 714 N.E.2d 35; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 390; 239 Ill. Dec. 477



June 9, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing August 4, 1999. Released for Publication August 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 96 CH 2560 and 96 CH 12873, Consolidated. Honorable Robert Boharic, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, their complaint against defendants to prevent retroactive application of Public Act 89-448.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff partnerships filed two actions against defendant government agencies, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief to prevent an alleged retroactive application of Public Act 89-448 (Act), which was an amendment to the Retail Rate Law, 220 ILCS 5/8-403.1. The Act abolished subsidies for tire burning plants. As a result, plaintiffs, who burned tires, were no longer entitled to be paid the retail rate for electricity they generated. Plaintiffs argued that without the retail rate, their plants could not meet daily operating expenses. The lower court dismissed the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and vacated in part. The court held that the counts that were dismissed which sought to enjoin state action were improperly dismissed on sovereign immunity grounds. The court of claims, which the lower court found had jurisdiction, had no power to construe the constitutionality of a statute. The court affirmed dismissal counts that were premature.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's ruling dismissing plaintiffs' complaint to prevent retroactive application of Public Act 89-448, where the lower court had subject matter jurisdiction. The court affirmed the dismissal of those counts that were premature.

People v. Conley


No. 1-97-2740


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 1; 713 N.E.2d 131; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 381; 238 Ill. Dec. 885



June 7, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CR 12216. Honorable Michael Toomin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of four counts of attempted murder, three counts of aggravated battery with a firearm, and one count of aggravated discharge of a firearm and sentenced defendant to a total of 60 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of attempted murder, three counts of aggravated battery with a firearm, and one count of aggravated discharge of a firearm after he fired shots inside a restaurant at victims whom he believed smashed his car window. Defendant testified that he was fearful that two of the victims were going to shoot him, so he pulled out a revolver and started shooting. Three of the four people defendant confronted were shot. Defendant brought several errors. One contention was that the trial court erred by refusing to instruct the jury on the doctrine of transferred intent as it applied to defendant's self-defense claim against two of the victims. Defendant argued that he shot two victims in self-defense because he thought they were reaching for weapons. Defendant contended that the court should have instructed the jury to transfer defendant's self-defense intent to the unintended victims. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Assuming that the trial court should have given a transferred intent instruction, there was no prejudice because the jury rejected the defendant's theory of self-defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for attempted murder, aggravated battery with a firearm, and aggravated discharge of a firearm because it was not an error for the trial court to refuse a jury instruction on transferred intent. Defendant's remaining contentions were also without merit.

People v. Gill


No. 1-97-3437


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


304 Ill. App. 3d 23; 713 N.E.2d 124; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 720; 238 Ill. Dec. 878



June 4, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of March 19, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 150.



DISPOSITION: The case reversed and remanded for a new trial. The petition for rehearing denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted the him of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon in violation 720 Ill. Cons. Stat. 5/24-1.1 The trial judge found defendant guilty but mentally ill.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was on a school playground swinging an axe back and forth. Defendant was charged with unlawful use of a weapon by a felon. During trial, one expert testified that defendant was insane at the time of the alleged offense and was not fit to stand trial. In rebuttal, Plaintiff State of Illinois had an expert testify that that defendant had the ability to understand the nature of the criminality of his acts and had the ability to conform his behavior to the requirements of law. The trial court rejected defendant's insanity defense and found him guilty but mentally ill. Defendant appealed. Defendant argued that application of the newly amended insanity statute, which required defendant to prove insanity by clear and convincing evidence rather than by a preponderance, as was required under the prior statute, violated the ex post facto clause of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 10; Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 (1970). The court reversed the judgment. It was apparent from the record that defense counsel and the judge applied the amended statute when it was not in effect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial because the amended insanity statute, requiring a higher burden of proof, was not in effect at the time of trial and therefore application of the amendment constituted reversible error.

Nelson v. Industrial Comm'n (Village of Winnetka)


No. 1-98-0141WC


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION DIVISION


305 Ill. App. 3d 651; 713 N.E.2d 119; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 368; 238 Ill. Dec. 873



June 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 23, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joanne L. Lanigan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fire fighter sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied his claim for benefits under the Worker's Compensation Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 305/1 (1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellee village employed appellant fire fighter. Appellant sustained an injury during the course of his employment, and filed multiple applications for adjustment of his claim under the Worker's Compensation Act (Act), 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 305/1 et seq. (1996). The lower court denied the claims because they were barred as appellee enacted a statute under the authority of 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/22-306 (1996), which prevented appellant from seeking recovery under the Act. Appellant sought review, arguing that the amended version of 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/22-307 (1996) applied to his case. The amended statute would allow for appellant's claim under the Act. In affirming, the appellate court rejected appellant's arguments and held that the amendment was a change in the law, and not a clarification; thus, it had no application to the present case. The court found that 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/22-306 (1996) gave appellee the power to enact its statute limiting recovery by a fire fighter, and the legislative history surrounding the amendment to 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/22-307 (1996) revealed that the legislature sought to change the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's worker's compensation benefits. Amendments to the law that would allow appellee to also recover worker's compensation benefits were inapplicable because a former statute in effect at the time of appellant's claim, which limited his recovery, was controlling.

People v. McIntosh


NO. 5-97-1001


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


305 Ill. App. 3d 462; 712 N.E.2d 893; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 370; 238 Ill. Dec. 789



June 1, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County. No. 95-CF-192. Honorable E. Kyle Vantrease, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions from the Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois) of home invasion, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11 and criminal sexual assault, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-13, sentencing him to 10 years on each offense, to be served consecutively and requiring him to serve at least 85 percent of the sentence for criminal sexual assault prior to release, pursuant to the Illinois truth-in-sentencing requirements.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of home invasion and criminal sexual assault sentencing him to 10 years' imprisonment on each offense, the sentences to be served consecutively. The trial court also stated that defendant was to serve at least 85 percent of the sentence for criminal sexual assault prior to release, pursuant to the Illinois truth-in-sentencing requirements. Defendant appealed, arguing that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of criminal sexual assault. The court held actual penetration was not required and the evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of criminal sexual assault. Defendant further argued that his sentencing order must be amended to reflect that he was eligible for good-conduct credit, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3. The court held that the written judgment order under which defendant's sentence of imprisonment was entered contained no provision regarding truth-in-sentencing. Because the truth-in-sentencing provisions were unconstitutional, the trial court's verbal ruling applying the truth-in-sentencing provisions was void, but the rest of defendant's sentence remained valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentence of imprisonment, but modified the portion of defendant's sentence entered under the truth-in-sentencing provisions on the grounds that the trial court's verbal ruling applying the truth-in-sentencing provisions was void.

People v. Watts (In re K.P.)


Nos. 4-98-0931, 4-98-0932 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


305 Ill. App. 3d 175; 711 N.E.2d 478; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 363; 238 Ill. Dec. 375


March 10, 1999, Submitted  
May 27, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Adams County. Nos. 96JA34, 96JA35, No. 96JA36. Honorable Chet W. Vahle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents appealed from the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) decision to adjudicate their minor children wards of the state because of neglect, when petitioner sought to terminate respondents' parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the lower court decision that terminated respondents' parental rights in their minor children at petitioner state's request. The children had already been adjudicated neglected and made wards of the court because their environment was not clean or healthy, and one of them had unexplained bruises. Respondents argued that they had not been given 12 months to show reasonable progress in correcting the conditions requiring removal, as the applicable statute required at the time the children had been adjudicated neglected. The statute as amended after the adjudication applied, which gave nine months to show reasonable progress, because respondents had no vested right to improve. The evidence supporting the trial court's decision was clear and convincing, because subjectively reasonable efforts did not support a finding that the progress was objectively reasonable. The best interest of the children supported the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision because there was not enough of an improvement to find that the best interests of respondents' children disallowed termination of their parental rights. The statute as amended while the appeal was pending applied, because respondents had no vested right to improve the conditions mandating removal.

Segers v. Industrial Comm'n


NO. 5-98-0208


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


304 Ill. App. 3d 1060; 711 N.E.2d 450; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 335; 238 Ill. Dec. 347



May 19, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County. No. 96-MR-14. Honorable Loren P. Lewis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois) that denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and granted defendant company's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff's declaratory judgment action for death benefits under the Workers' Occupational Diseases Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 310/a (1996).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wife initiated a declaratory judgment action against defendant company for death benefits, based on the death of plaintiff's husband, pursuant to the Workers' Occupational Diseases Act (Act), 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 310/a (1996). The court denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and granted defendant company's motion for summary judgment because the court found that plaintiff's claim was barred by a lump-sum settlement agreement executed by plaintiff's husband and defendant company. The appellate court held that the court did not err in finding that it had primary jurisdiction because the matter involved a question of law, defendant commission's expertise was neither helpful nor necessary, and a potential to foreclose needless litigation by a court ruling existed. After considering the lump-sum settlement agreement and the Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 310/a (1996), the appellate court held that plaintiff's claim was not barred because the provision of § 9 of the Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 310/a (1996), that potentially barred the claim, was not invoked. Therefore, the decision was reversed, and judgment was entered for plaintiff.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for defendant company was reversed, and judgment was entered for plaintiff wife because plaintiff's death benefit claim was not statutorily barred or barred by a settlement agreement between plaintiff's husband and defendant company. The lower court had primary jurisdiction over the case because questions of law existed, needless litigation could be foreclosed, and defendant commission's expertise was not helpful or necessary.

People v. Cosby


No. 1-97-4569


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION

May 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 6, 1999.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion for a new trial and entered judgment convicting defendant of aggravated sexual assault, attempted murder, violation of the Firearm Owner's Identification Card Act, 430 Ill Comp. Stat. 65/2(a)(1) (1995), and armed violence. The court imposed consecutive sentences for each conviction.

When officers responded to the scene of the crime, defendant fled. Plaintiff State of Illinois brought charges against defendant, alleging that he was guilty of aggravated sexual assault, attempted murder, violation of the Firearm Owner's Identification Card Act (Act), 430 Ill Comp. Stat. 65/2(a)(1) (1995), and armed violence. Following a trial of the matter, defendant was convicted as charged and the lower court imposed consecutive sentences for each of the convictions. The court held that while defendant's convictions were supported by the evidence, defendant's sentence for his violation of the state firearm identification statute was improper, and remand was necessary for resentencing on that offense.

Anderson v. Department of Mental Health & Dev. Disabilities


No. 1-96-3112


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


305 Ill. App. 3d 262; 711 N.E.2d 1170; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 323; 238 Ill. Dec. 509



May 14, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 90-L-2504. Honorable Jennifer Duncan-Brice, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment for appellee conservator in appellant's action to enforce a lien to recover expenses of treatment. Appellant's hospital lien, which was filed pursuant to the Hospital Lien Act, 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 35/0.01 et seq. (1996), was adjudicated to zero.


OVERVIEW: After appellee conservator's ward jumped from a hospital window, he received medical and psychological treatment from appellant Department of Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities. When appellee obtained a settlement in a lawsuit he brought against the hospital on behalf of his ward, appellant filed a notice of lien pursuant to the Hospital Lien Act, 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 35/0.01 et seq. The trial court adjudicated appellant's lien to zero and entered judgment for appellee in appellant's action to enforce the lien. The appellate court affirmed the judgment, holding that the trial court did not err by requiring appellant to prove a causal connection between the ward's injuries from the fall, which resulted in the settlement, and the treatment provided by appellant. Because appellant had not differentiated between medical and psychiatric treatment in its billing, the court was unable to set a reasonable figure for the charges to which appellant might have been entitled for the medical treatment. Thus, appellant was not entitled to recover expenses through the imposition of a lien pursuant to the act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment entered in favor of appellee conservator in appellant Department of Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities' action to enforce a lien to recover expenses of treatment. The court also affirmed the adjudication of appellant's hospital lien to zero. Appellant failed to prove a causal connection between the treatment and the judgment to which the lien attached.

County of Kankakee v. Anthony


No. 3-98-0107


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


304 Ill. App. 3d 1040; 710 N.E.2d 1242; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 311; 238 Ill. Dec. 140



May 4, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 14, 1999. Released for Publication June 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 21st Judicial Circuit. Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 95--OV--973. Honorable Sheldon W. Reagan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois) in favor of appellee county in appellee's action that alleged appellants violated zoning laws by operating a private school in their garage without obtaining the proper permits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowners constructed and operated a private school in their garage without obtaining a variance and special use permit. Appellee county filed suit against appellants for violating zoning laws. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee, and the appellate court affirmed the judgment. The 1996 zoning code was void because it was not passed by a simple majority, as required by 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5--12014(b) (1996). Accordingly, the 1967 zoning code was applicable. Sufficient evidence supported the trial court's determination that appellants' school constituted an illegal use of their property. The principal use of appellants' property was as a single-family dwelling. The school was not an accessory use of the property because it was not clearly and customarily incidental to a single-family dwelling.


OUTCOME: Judgment in favor of appellee county was affirmed in its action that alleged appellant landowners violated zoning laws because, under the clear language of the zoning laws, the private school appellants operated in their garage was not an accessory use to appellants' single-family dwelling.

People v. Slater


No. 3-97-0351


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


304 Ill. App. 3d 489; 714 N.E.2d 9; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 308; 239 Ill. Dec. 451



April 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 96--CF--935. Honorable James T. Teros Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part as modified and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit Rock Island County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of two counts of attempted first-degree murder and two counts of aggravated battery with a firearm. Defendant appealed from the lower court's application of the truth-in-sentencing law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached a car occupied by two individuals and fired at least four shots into the car. Defendant was then charged and convicted of one count of attempted murder and one count of aggravated battery with a firearm as to each victim. Application of truth-in-sentencing law required defendant to serve 85 percent of his sentence. The court vacated the aggravated battery convictions based on one-act one-crime principles. The firing of the gun in rapid succession constituted a single act as to each victim. That act could be the basis for only one conviction per victim and, therefore, the aggravated battery convictions had to be reversed. Defendant's sentence was not subject to the truth-in-sentencing provisions. Ill. Public Act 89--404, which contained the truth-in-sentencing law, was found to be unconstitutional. The defects of the truth-in-sentencing law were not cured until after defendant committed his crimes, and therefore the curative legislation was inapplicable to defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for attempted murder, but vacated the aggravated battery convictions because they violated one-act one-crime principles. Defendant's firing of a weapon constituted a single act as to each victim and that act could be the basis for only one conviction per victim. The truth-in-sentencing law was inapplicable to defendant's sentence because the law was not constitutional when defendant committed his crimes.

People v. Edwards


No. 2-97-0976


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


304 Ill. App. 3d 250; 710 N.E.2d 507; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 286; 237 Ill. Dec. 877


April 6, 1999, Submitted  
April 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 97--CF--989. Honorable John R. Goshgarian, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Cause remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of armed violence in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33A--2, aggravated battery with a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12--4.2(a)(1), and aggravated discharge of a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24--1.2(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment for armed violence in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33A--2, aggravated battery with a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12--4.2(a)(1), and aggravated discharge of a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24--1.2(a)(2), after shooting the victim once in the leg. Defendant appealed. The court rejected defendant's argument that the victim had not suffered great bodily harm where the victim testified that she did not immediately feel pain after being shot, holding that it was for the trier of fact to determine whether the victim had suffered great bodily harm based on the nature of the injury. Because defendant only fired one shot causing injury to the victim, the court held that defendant could only be convicted of armed violence and vacated the convictions for aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated discharge of firearm because those convictions were based on the same physical act as the conviction for armed violence. Where the statute used to sentence defendant was found to be unconstitutional, the court remanded the case for resentencing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for armed violence was affirmed but her convictions for aggravated discharge of a firearm and aggravated battery with a firearm were vacated where they were based upon the same physical act as used to convict defendant of armed violence. The case was remanded for sentencing where the statute used to sentence defendant had been found to be unconstitutional.

 

430 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


City of Charleston v. Witmer


NO. 4-98-0438


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


304 Ill. App. 3d 386; 709 N.E.2d 998; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 287; 237 Ill. Dec. 529


January 19, 1999, Oral Argument Held  
April 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Coles County. Nos. 97OV2389, 97OV2390, 97OV2454, 97OV2460. Honorable Teresa K. Righter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois) in an action for violating a city ordinance, where defendants were found guilty of placing billboards in areas where signage was prohibited by the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendants placed billboards in areas where signage was prohibited by a city ordinance. Plaintiff city filed complaints, and defendants were found guilty of ordinance violations. Defendants argued on appeal that the ordinances were void, that plaintiff city failed to comply with statutory notice requirements, that the ordinance was invalid because it lacked an ordaining clause, and that the fines assessed were unconstitutional. The court reversed and held that the ordinance was invalidly enacted and, therefore, plaintiff city could not enforce it against defendants. The purpose of notice was to give all parties an opportunity to support or oppose a matter at issue. Notice setting forth the time and place of a hearing to zone property was mandatory and jurisdictional and any amendment passed in contravention thereof was void. The original published notice, while adequate to notify interested persons of a public hearing, did not serve to provide notice of a subsequent public hearing where no meeting of the zoning board was opened. Thus, the billboard ordinance was passed in contravention of the notice requirements of 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-13-14 and was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of guilty against defendants in an action where they had been prosecuted for placing billboards in areas where signage was prohibited by a city ordinance because the notice requirements required by statute were not met, rendering the ordinance void and unenforceable against defendants.

Toothman v. Hardee's Food Sys.


NO. 5-97-1034


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, restaurant chain and managers, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Saline County (Illinois), which found that appellants committed the tort of false imprisonment by strip searching appellee employees on the disappearance of $ 50 and was liable for compensatory and punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, two store managers and restaurant chain, were counting money in a safe, when they discovered that $ 50 was missing. Appellants accused appellees, four restaurant employees, of taking the money and forced them to submit to a strip search. The money was later discovered missing due to a bank error, and appellees brought suit against appellants for false imprisonment. Appellant moved for motion to dismiss, or in the alternative that appellees could proceed only under the Workers' Compensation Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 305/1 et seq. (1996). The trial court denied both motions, and a jury verdict resulted in appellees' favor, awarding compensatory and punitive damages. The court also stated that appellees proved the intentional tort of false imprisonment. The court affirmed the jury verdict in appellees' behalf, concluding that both the compensatory and punitive damages was reasonable and was not based upon passion or prejudice.
