People v. Jones


Nos. 2-97-0525 & 2-97-0544 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


306 Ill. App. 3d 793; 715 N.E.2d 256; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 243; 239 Ill. Dec. 811


November 24, 1998, Submitted; October 30, 1998, Assigned  
April 14, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing August 6, 1999. Released for Publication September 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. Nos. 96--CF--524, 95--CF--2604. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of two orders by the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted the state's motion to revoke defendant's probation for domestic battery, and a second decision convicting defendant of first-degree murder. Defendant argued it was error to admit evidence of defendant's other crimes against the victim and error to sentence defendant as a Class 4 felon for his conviction of felony domestic battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed two orders of the trial court: the first granting the state's motion to revoke defendant's probation for domestic battery of a victim, and a second decision convicting defendant of first-degree murder of the same victim. The court held that it was not an abuse of discretion to admit evidence of the previous acts of abuse defendant committed against the victim because the probative value of that other crimes evidence was not outweighed by its prejudicial impact. The reported incidents occurred within several months of the murder. In each of the incidents defendant committed an act of violence upon the victim or engaged in obsessive behavior. The court held that a second conviction of domestic battery was not required to enhance defendant's sentence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12--3.2(b) (1996). Qualification for an enhancement under the statute simply required that defendant had committed a "violation" of the domestic battery statute. Therefore, the court held it was not error to enhance defendant's sentence based upon the three prior occasions where defendant was charged with, but not convicted of domestic battery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments as modified. It was not an abuse of discretion to admit evidence of other crimes defendant committed against the victim because the probative value of that evidence was not outweighed by its prejudicial value. Statutory enhancement of defendant's sentence for domestic battery was properly based upon the prior occasions where defendant was charged with but not convicted of domestic battery.

 

433 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Zeitz v. Village of Glenview


No. 1-97-4323


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


304 Ill. App. 3d 586; 710 N.E.2d 849; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 225; 238 Ill. Dec. 52



April 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1999. Released for Publication June 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Albert Green, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners and plaintiff development corporation appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment in favor of defendants in an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from zoning ordinances enacted by defendant village. Plaintiffs also sought damages for inverse condemnation and improper taking.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners and development corporation presented a development plan to defendant village to build 10 homes on a 10-acre property. Defendant village later rezoned the property to limit the number of homes allowed on the property to five. Plaintiffs filed suit, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from the zoning ordinances. Plaintiffs sought to have defendant village's re-zoning of the land declared invalid, and alleged damages for inverse condemnation and improper taking of the property. Following a bench trial, the trial court entered judgment for defendants. Plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed the finding that no party had a vested right in the continuation of a zoning ordinance. The court held that plaintiffs did not satisfy the criteria for invoking the estoppel doctrine against defendant village. The court, after reviewing the La Salle and Sinclair factors, determined that plaintiffs failed to establish by clear and convincing evidence that the zoning classification at issue was arbitrary and capricious. The court further held that plaintiffs did not prove that the zoning ordinance deprived them of all economically viable uses for the property.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of defendants in plaintiffs' action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from zoning ordinances was affirmed. The court held that plaintiffs failed to establish by clear and convincing evidence that the zoning ordinance was arbitrary, unreasonable, and without any substantial relation to the health, safety, comfort, morals, or general welfare of the public.

 

434 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Durham


No. 2-97-0368


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 763; 708 N.E.2d 1249; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 204; 237 Ill. Dec. 209



March 31, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 96--CF--880. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which denied his motion in limine, regarding the testimony of a deceased victim of gunshot wounds, naming defendant as his assailant. Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1), (a)(2) (1996), and aggravated battery with a firearm, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-4.2(a)(1) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a motion in limine regarding the testimony of a victim of gunshot wounds. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1), (a)(2) (1996), and aggravated battery with a firearm, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-4.2(a)(1) (1996). A police officer had presented a spread of photographs to the victim as he lay on his deathbed. The victim could not speak, but nodded affirmatively and began to cry when shown a photograph of defendant. The trial court admitted the victim's reaction as an excited utterance and a spontaneous declaration. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion, and that the victim's nod when shown a photograph of defendant was not the type of startling event that would cause an excited utterance under the exception to the hearsay rule. The error was harmless, however, where sufficient evidence, beyond the victim's testimony, existed to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also held that the imposition of consecutive sentences was proper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the convictions and sentencing of defendant for murder and aggravated battery with a firearm because the trial court's error in admitting the victim's identification of defendant was harmless where other evidence was sufficient to establish defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also held that the imposition of consecutive sentences was proper.

 

435 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Butler


No. 1-97-1633


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


304 Ill. App. 3d 750; 709 N.E.2d 1272; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 215; 237 Ill. Dec. 559



March 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96-CR-17568. Honorable William O. Maki, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/401, and sentenced defendant to 15 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was returning from a trip to Jamaica when she was arrested for possession of cocaine. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment after being convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/401. At trial, customs officials testified that defendant was carrying bottles of wine, which also contained cocaine. Defendant testified that she had been offered the trip for free and that the only catch was that she had to carry back some wine. Defendant testified that she did not know of the cocaine and thought it was legal to transport the wine. Defendant appealed her conviction and sentence. The court affirmed, holding that a rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant knew she was carrying contraband because the circumstances of the free trip were suspicious. Where defendant failed to show that her co-defendant's testimony would have been material to her defense, so that the outcome of the case would have been different, the court held that her constitutional right to offer testimony had not been violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court convicting defendant of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver was affirmed where there was evidence from which a rational trier of fact could have found that the suspicious nature of defendant's travel inferred that she knew she was carrying cocaine.

 

436 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. G.O. (In re G.O.)


No. 1-98-0956


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


304 Ill. App. 3d 719; 710 N.E.2d 140; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 219; 237 Ill. Dec. 717



March 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 1, 1999. Released for Publication May 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. 97 JD 12502. HONORABLE DANIEL P. DARCY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for first degree murder; defendant alleged that he was deprived of equal protection under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970), and that his confession was obtained illegally and improperly admitted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was convicted of first degree murder, in violation of 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-33(1.5). The court reversed and remanded the finding of delinquency because defendant's demand for a jury trial was denied, thus depriving him of equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970). The court held that defendant, because he had been charged with first-degree murder, was similarly situated as a violent juvenile offender or as a habitual juvenile offender. The court further held that because 405/5-33(1.5) did not preclude a jury trial, a trial by jury must have been granted if requested. The court found no rational basis or legitimate legislative goal was served by granting the right to a jury trial for two offenses and denying it as to a third. The court ruled that under the totality of circumstances, defendant's confession was improperly obtained because defendant had no advice from an adult, he was alone with police officers when interrogated, he was not a free agent after giving an exculpatory statement, he never signed a formal waiver of his rights, and his statements never were reduced to writing and given to him to review or sign.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case because when the trial court denied defendant juvenile's demand for a jury trial, it violated his right to equal protection, and no rational basis or legitimate legislative goal was served by it. The court also ruled that defendant's confession was improperly obtained because he had no advice and counsel, he was alone with police officers during interrogation, and he was not a free agent.

 

437 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Sampson v. Graves


1-98-0655


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


304 Ill. App. 3d 961; 711 N.E.2d 1118; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 221; 238 Ill. Dec. 457



March 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified May 26, 1999. Rehearing Denied May 24, 1999. Released for Publication June 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Robert V. Boharic, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a mayor, appealed the order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted motion filed by plaintiffs, city aldermen, for summary judgment on defendant's counterclaim that sought an order declaring that the city ordinance that allowed a committee member to hire independent counsel with the approval of the council, violated Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(f) by changing the form of the city's government without a referendum.


OVERVIEW: A city council passed an ordinance that granted the chairman of the finance committee (chairman), upon the request of an alderman, the exclusive right to hire an attorney, subject to the approval of the city council, and filed a complaint seeking the compliance of defendant, the mayor. Defendant filed a counterclaim seeking to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional, alleging that the ordinance unlawfully restricted his power, thus changing the form of the city's government without a referendum as required by Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(f). The trial court granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment on the counterclaim. On appeal, the court held that under 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-1-7(b), the corporate authorities had the power to hire attorneys as consultants. Because plaintiff and defendants were the corporate authorities as defined by 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-1-2(2)(c), and the chairman's right to hire an attorney was subject to the approval of the council, which was presided over by defendant pursuant to Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3.1-40-30, the ordinance did not change the form of the city's government and was not unconstitutional. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the motion of plaintiffs, city aldermen, for summary judgment on the counterclaim of defendant, the mayor, because the ordinance that allowed a committee member to hire independent counsel subject to the approval of the council merely allowed that member to recommended an attorney to the city authorities; thus, the city's form of government was not changed, and the ordinance was constitutional.

Plank v. A.M.P. (In re A.M.P.)


NO. 4-98-0826


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 907; 708 N.E.2d 1235; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 173; 237 Ill. Dec. 195


December 30, 1998, Submitted  
March 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 98MH24. Honorable Ann A. Einhorn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant moved to withdraw and sought review from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which granted appellee parents' petition for authorization of electroconvulsive therapy for their child.


OVERVIEW: Appellee parents wished to exercise their common law right to consent to electroconvulsive therapy (ECT) for their daughter. No statute prevented such consent. The trial court was asked to examine the parents' exercise of authority to ensure that the minor's liberty interests were protected. The trial court authorized the ECT, and on motion by respondent's appointed counsel, directed the clerk to prepare and file a notice of appeal. On appeal, the court determined that although there was a lack of statutory authority concerning consent for ECT, it was proper for the lower court to adopt the framework of similar legislation to guide its analysis in order to provide constitutional safeguard to the minor to protect her rights under the common law. The court determined that review of the record indicated that the minor's right of procedural due process was met and that her parents and physicians were acting in her best interest. The order was, therefore, affirmed and the motion to withdraw was granted.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court authorizing electroconvulsive therapy was affirmed and counsel's motion to withdraw was granted, because the record established that the lower court provided the minor with safeguards of procedural due process and ensured that her parents and physicians were acting in her best interests despite the absence of statutory guidance.

People v. Wanke


No. 2-97-0581


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 772; 708 N.E.2d 833; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 169; 237 Ill. Dec. 30


February 17, 1999, Submitted  
March 24, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 23, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of DeKalb County. No. 91--CF--323. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions on two counts of burglary in the Circuit Court of DeKalb County (Illinois), contending that the trial court erred by admitting statements that defendant made to police officers regarding the burglaries during supposed plea bargain negotiations, in refusing defendant's requests for different appointed counsel, and by allowing a guilty but mentally ill jury instruction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his burglary convictions, contending that the trial court erred by admitting statements that he made to police regarding the burglaries. Defendant claimed that the statements were allegedly inadmissible as part of a plea negotiation under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402(f), 134 Ill. 2d R. 402(f). Defendant also claimed that the trial court erred by refusing requests for different appointed counsel, and by allowing a guilty but mentally ill jury instruction. Upon de novo review, the court considered Rule 402(f), which stated that if a plea discussion did not result in a guilty plea, neither the plea discussion nor any resulting agreement, plea, or judgment were admissible against defendant. The court affirmed the trial court's admission of defendant's statements, concluding that the rudiments of a negotiation process were not present where the state and police made no comments about defendant making a plea. Defendant's other contentions of error were also unsuccessful, and the convictions were affirmed. Defendant's request for 25 days credit toward his sentence was granted because the trial court erred in not giving credit for time spent in custody before posting bond.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for burglary, but granted a credit for 25 days time served by defendant in custody before posting bond. The court found that defendant's statements were admissible because no police or state authority made a statement about defendant making a plea; the court also found no abuse of discretion in denying defendant's request to appoint different trial counsel where no ineffective assistance was proven.

 

440 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


No. 1-97-1405


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 949; 709 N.E.2d 609; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 161; 237 Ill. Dec. 354



March 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edward Fiala, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him for first-degree murder and attempted murder. Defendant asserted the out-of-court statements of two witnesses were not admissible hearsay, under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-10.2 (1996), where the statements lacked the requisite trustworthiness, and the state failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his convictions for first-degree murder and attempted murder, asserting the out-of-court statements of two witnesses were improperly admitted under § 115-10.2 of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-10.2 (1996), where the statements lacked the requisite trustworthiness, and the state failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held the hearsay statements of the first witness were not admissible under § 115-10.2, because they lacked trustworthiness where they were made long after the crime occurred, and the statements were not subject to meaningful cross-examination. The court held the hearsay statements of the second witness were not admissible under § 115-10.2, because they lacked trustworthiness where there were substantial and numerous inconsistencies in his statements, and the statements were not subject to meaningful cross-examination. The court held because there was only a disavowed statement from a third witness and no other evidence against defendant, the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction. Accordingly, the convictions were reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed because the out-of-court statements of two witnesses were not admissible hearsay where they were made long after the charged crime occurred, they contained numerous inconsistencies, and were not subjected to meaningful cross-examination. Thus, because there was only a disavowed statement from a third witness and no other evidence against defendant, the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction.

 

441 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dasaky


1-97-2027


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 986; 709 N.E.2d 635; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 162; 237 Ill. Dec. 380



March 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 1999. Released for Publication May 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 94-CR-6193, 94-CR-21344. THE HONORABLE LEO HOLT, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that the alleged sentencing agreement between the state and defendant was binding as to the state, and dismissed all charges against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a debriefing and consideration agreement with plaintiff state but during the proceedings, defendant was charged in another case in violation of the agreement with the state. Defendant filed a pretrial motion to dismiss pending indictments or, in the alternative, enforce the agreement between defendant and the state that he be given boot camp or probation. The trial court dismissed the indictments and the state appealed, arguing that the agreement was not binding on the state because no agreement actually existed. The court agreed with the state, noting that only defendant had argued that he was promised boot camp or probation in return for his testimony. Neither his former attorney nor the state alleged any promise of the kind. The court further noted that defendant had not complied with his part of the agreement not to pick up another case. The court held that because defendant showed no prejudice, even if there was a plea agreement, defendant had not yet pleaded guilty and therefore could not assert the argument. The court therefore reversed the dismissal and remanded the case back to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of defendant's charges was reversed because no agreement existed between plaintiff state and defendant to either offer probation or to send defendant to boot camp. The court found that defendant showed no prejudice to his case by the alleged agreement.

People v. Ruppel


No. 4-98-0411


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 885; 708 N.E.2d 824; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 151; 237 Ill. Dec. 21


January 12, 1999, Oral Argument Held  
March 22, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 2, 1999. Released for Publication April 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 97DT100. Honorable Michael Q. Jones, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted her of driving with a blood-alcohol concentration over .10 in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501(a)(1). Defendant argued that the state failed to show that it had probable cause to arrest her or to perform the blood test, and that the blood sample was not lawfully drawn.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her conviction of driving with a blood-alcohol concentration (BAC) over .10 pursuant to 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501(a)(1). Defendant contended that involuntary blood test results which indicated she had a BAC of .228 were inadmissible. The court concluded that defendant's blood contained evanescent evidence, which was her changing BAC. The test was performed in a hospital by medical personnel according to standard medical procedures. The officer had probable cause to stop defendant for driving while under the influence before he ordered the test. Defendant contended that the involuntary blood test was performed pursuant to § 11-501.6(b) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.6(b). The court concluded that § 11-501.6(b) did not apply because defendant was not receiving medical treatment. The court concluded that the blood test was authorized by § 11-501.2(c)(2) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.2(c)(2), and was ordered by the police officer as an investigatory tool, and was not used for any medical purpose. The judgment was affirmed where defendant's involuntary blood test results were admissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed convicting defendant of driving with a blood alcohol concentration over .10 where the state had probable cause to arrest defendant and to perform the blood test, the blood sample was lawfully drawn, and the state provided an adequate foundation for the blood test results.

Quantum Pipeline Co. v. Illinois Commerce Comm'n


No. 3-98-0131


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


304 Ill. App. 3d 310; 709 N.E.2d 950; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 142; 237 Ill. Dec. 481


September 10, 1998, Submitted  
March 12, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 30, 1999. Rehearing Denied May 17, 1999. Released for Publication May 17, 1999. As Corrected July 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Illinois Commerce Commission. ICC Docket Nos. 96--0001/96--0318.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed from a decision of the Illinois Commerce Commission rescinding petitioners' certificate authorizing construction of a common carrier pipeline and denying petitioners' request for eminent domain authority.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed an application with respondent commerce commission seeking authorization to build a pipeline. Respondent waived a hearing and granted petitioners' certificate of public convenience and necessity after finding that a public need existed. Due to an inability to obtain easements from all of the affected landowners, petitioners sought eminent domain power. After the time to petition for a rehearing on its grant of petitioners' certificate expired, respondent filed a report to reopen the proceeding. A decision rescinding petitioners' certificate was reversed and remanded. Petitioners, having complied with the provisions of the statute, acquired a property right to build the pipeline. Respondent had to afford procedural due process to petitioners. Petitioners were not provided the required notice. Respondent did not issue a written complaint charging any violation of its prior order granting petitioners' certificate, or any change in the law, or any factual change constituting a violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the rescission of petitioners' certificate because the procedure used by respondent violated petitioners' procedural due process rights by not giving petitioners the required notice.

People v. Jenkins


NO. 4-97-1104


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 854; 709 N.E.2d 265; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 124; 237 Ill. Dec. 279


January 7, 1999, Submitted  
March 11, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 97CF819. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) and appealed his life sentence, contending that the trial court failed to make a written finding as required by the habitual offender statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-2 (1996), and that he was not given a hearing prior to being ordered to reimburse the county for the cost of his defense, as required by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/113-3.1(a) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and sentenced as a habitual offender to life imprisonment. He filed an appeal, challenging his sentence because the trial court failed to make a written finding as required by the habitual offender statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-2 (1996), and to comply with 725 ILCS 5/113-3.1(a) (1996), by not conducting a hearing prior to ordering him to reimburse the county for the cost of his defense. He then filed a motion to reconsider sentence and to declare the sentencing statute unconstitutional. The court concluded that it had jurisdiction over the appeal in spite of defendant's filing of the posttrial motion to reconsider sentence. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. It held that defendant forfeited his argument that the trial court made no written finding under the habitual offender statute, because he did not raise the issue at the hearing or in a timely motion to reconsider sentence, and no exceptions to the forfeiture rule applied. It also held that the court did not hold the hearing required before ordering defendant to reimburse the county for the services of his appointed counsel, and remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, holding that defendant forfeited his argument that a written finding was not made under the habitual offender statute by failing to raise the issue at the hearing or on a motion to reconsider sentence. The court reversed in part and remanded for a hearing on defendant's ability to reimburse the county for the cost of his defense.

People v. A.T.


No. 2-98-0165


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 531; 708 N.E.2d 529; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 120; 236 Ill. Dec. 943


February 8, 1999, Submitted  
March 10, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 97--CF--583. Honorable Donald C. Hudson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a determination of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) that proceedings should be returned to juvenile court for disposition instead of remaining in criminal court for sentencing.


OVERVIEW: The state initiated delinquency proceedings under the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5--4, against 15 year old defendant. The state alleged that defendant committed offenses that included attempted first degree murder and aggravated discharge of a firearm, which were predicate offenses that gave rise to a rebuttable presumption to transfer a minor's case to criminal court. The state filed a petition to transfer defendant's case to criminal court, which was granted. Defendant tendered pleas of guilty to lesser charges. The trial court accepted defendant's pleas. Defendant then filed a petition to transfer his case back to juvenile court for disposition. The state filed a motion to retain jurisdiction in criminal court. The state argued that the legislature's intent was for the decision to transfer to stand throughout the proceedings and to have the minor sentenced as an adult on all the offenses of which he was convicted, even if none of those offenses were predicate offenses. The court held that it was appropriate to make a new determination of whether a minor's case should be returned to juvenile court for disposition, or retained in criminal court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination that proceedings should be returned to juvenile court. The court held that it was appropriate for the trial court to hold a new hearing on whether criminal court jurisdiction should be retained where the juvenile offender was convicted only of offenses that would not give rise to mandatory transfer or rebuttable presumption for transfer to criminal courts.

People v. Boatman


NO. 4-98-0212


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 589; 708 N.E.2d 520; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 115; 236 Ill. Dec. 934


December 30, 1998, Submitted  
March 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 9, 1999.
Appeal denied by People v. Boatman, 187 Ill. 2d 573, 724 N.E.2d 1270, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 25, 244 Ill. Dec. 186 (2000)
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Boatman, 187 Ill. 2d 573, 722 N.E.2d 1141, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 29, 243 Ill. Dec. 72 (2000)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by People v. Boatman, 312 Ill. App. 3d 340, 726 N.E.2d 1178, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 171, 244 Ill. Dec. 867 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2000)
Motion granted by, Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Boatman, 2015 IL App (4th) 130532-U, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 984 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 97CF1076. Honorable John G. Townsend, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), of attempted first degree murder of a peace officer, two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated battery with a firearm, and unlawful possession of a stolen vehicle. He challenged his sentences on several grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his sentences for attempted first-degree murder of a peace officer, aggravated sexual assault, aggravated battery with firearm, and unlawful possession of a stolen vehicle. The court affirmed the sentence for possession, which was extended due to conviction of the more serious offenses, holding that under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-2(a) (1996), imposition of extended terms on separately charged, differing class offenses arising from unrelated courses of conduct was proper whether they were prosecuted separately or consolidated. The court held void the 160-year sentence for attempted murder as unauthorized by 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-4(c)(1). The court reduced it and remanded for amendment of the sentencing order, and held that defendant was eligible for good-time credit under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3. The court rejected defendant's claim that the statutory amendment increasing the penalty for attempted first degree murder of a peace officer in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/8-4(c)(1) was unconstitutional under the single subject rule, holding that the provisions of the act were related.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence for possession of a stolen vehicle, holding that its extension due to conviction of the more serious offenses was proper whether those offenses were prosecuted separately or consolidated. The court reduced the 160-year sentence for attempted murder, as unauthorized by statute.

 

447 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Moran Transp. Corp. v. Stroger


No. 1-97-2061


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 459; 708 N.E.2d 508; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 117; 236 Ill. Dec. 922



March 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joanne L. Lanigan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff diesel fuel purchasers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed their complaints in an action seeking relief against enforcement of a municipal diesel fuel tax ordinance. Plaintiffs asserted they had standing to attack the constitutionality of the tax and that the tax violated Ill. Const. of 1970, art. IX, § 2. Defendants challenged the grant of class certification to plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff diesel fuel purchasers appealed the dismissal of their complaints in a case for declaratory and injunctive relief against enforcement of a municipal ordinance that imposed a tax on diesel fuel, asserting the trial court erred in finding that they lacked standing to attack the constitutionality of the ordinance and wrongly rejected plaintiffs' uniformity clause claim. Defendants challenged the grant of class certification to plaintiffs. The court held plaintiffs did have standing where they had paid money pursuant to the tax which they alleged to be violative of the uniformity clause, Ill. Const. of 1970, art. IX, § 2. The court held the ordinance was not violative of the uniformity clause where the tax classification was based on a real and substantial difference between the people taxed and those not taxed, and the classification was reasonably related to public policy. The court held the trial court erred in granting class standing where plaintiffs did not address the statutory requirements necessary to maintain a class action. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed, except as to the grant of class standing, and was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing plaintiff diesel fuel purchasers' complaints was affirmed because the diesel fuel tax ordinance was not unconstitutional where the tax classification was based on a real and substantial difference between the people taxed and those not taxed, and was reasonably related to public policy. The judgment granting plaintiffs class standing was reversed because they did not address the applicable statutory requirements.

 

448 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


County of Cook v. Village of Rosemont


No. 1-98-2847


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 403; 708 N.E.2d 501; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 118; 236 Ill. Dec. 915



March 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 31, 1999. Released for Publication April 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 97L50281. HONORABLE THOMAS P. QUINN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), granting appellee county's motion for summary judgment in its action alleging that appellant unlawfully passed an ordinance prohibiting the payment and collection of a valid county amusement tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellee county's ordinance created an amusement tax that was to be collected and remitted by owners and operators of amusement places. Appellant village, which was within the county and owned and operated amusement places, enacted an ordinance that provided appellant's patrons would not pay the tax, and appellant employees would not collect it. Appellee filed a complaint against appellant for mandamus, injunction, lack of constitutionality, and other relief. The circuit court granted appellee's motion for partial summary judgment on the grounds that appellant's ordinance was not a constitutional exercise of its home rule authority. The court also found that appellant's ordinance had extraterritorial effect because it prevented the imposition of the amusement tax on ticket purchases from third parties outside the village. The issue on appeal was whether enacting the ordinance exceeded appellant's grant of home rule power under article VII, section 6(a) of the Illinois Constitution of 1970. The court held that the ordinance was not for appellant's own government and affairs, but those of the county, and therefore, affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's grant of summary judgment to appellee county, holding that appellant village had exceeded its home rule authority in enacting an ordinance prohibiting the collection and payment of an amusement tax enacted by the county. The court affirmed the trial court's issuance of an injunction permanently barring enforcement of the ordinance.

People v. McDougle


No. 2--97--0475


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 509; 708 N.E.2d 482; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 112; 236 Ill. Dec. 896


February 9, 1999, Submitted  
March 3, 1999, Filed


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 75--CF--3064. Honorable Robert G. Coplan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) that denied his request for a transfer from the Department of Corrections so that he could receive additional psychiatric treatment. Defendant asserted the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act, pursuant to which he had been committed, violated his rights to due process and equal protection, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Ill. Const. of 1970 art. 1, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of a decision that denied his application, pursuant to the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act (Act), 725 Ill. Comp Stat. 205/9 (1996), seeking a transfer from the Department of Corrections (DOC) for additional psychiatric treatment, asserting the Act violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection. Because an individual could not be adjudicated sexually dangerous unless he had a mental disorder for more than one year and he demonstrated propensities towards acts of sexual assault or sexual molestation of children, the court held the legislature could prescribe a different manner of treatment for persons committed as sexually dangerous persons and those committed for other mental health issues. The court held the Act was not unconstitutional where it was rationally tailored to achieve its objective to provide treatment and to protect the public from sexual violence, and so did not violate equal protection, and where proceedings under the Act were reasonably related to the substantial public interest of protecting citizens from dangerous deviant sexual behavior, and so did not violate due process. Accordingly, the decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The decision denying defendant's request for a transfer of commitment facilities was affirmed because the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act (Act) was rationally tailored to achieve its objective to provide treatment and to protect the public from sexual violence, and where proceedings under the Act were reasonably related to the substantial public interest of protecting citizens from dangerous deviant sexual behavior.

People v. Wilson


No. 1-96-3655


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 1035; 710 N.E.2d 408; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 104; 237 Ill. Dec. 778



March 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1231. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 14, 1999. Rehearing Denied April 12, 1999. Released for Publication April 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John D. Brady, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of first-degree murder and aggravated discharge of a firearm, and imposed an extended sentence and a concurrent sentence, respectively. Defendant argued he was deprived of the right to a trial by an impartial jury, he was denied the right to effective assistance of trial counsel, and his extended-term sentence for murder was an abuse of discretion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of a judgment that convicted him of first-degree murder and aggravated discharge of a firearm, and imposed an extended-term sentence for the murder conviction. Defendant asserted the jury was not impartial, his trial counsel was ineffective, and his extended-term sentence was an abuse of discretion. The court held defendant had not been denied his right to a trial by an impartial jury where the trial court's questions and procedures employed in voir dire to gauge juror competency created a reasonable assurance that any prejudice or bias would be discovered, and defendant failed to show that any juror was partial. The court held the counsel's decision to not use a peremptory challenge against the suspect juror did not amount to ineffective assistance where it was not objectively unreasonable, and defendant failed to show that it was not tactical and a matter of jury selection strategy. The court held the sentence imposed by the trial court was unenforceable because defendant did not satisfy the criteria required to extend his sentence. Accordingly, the judgment of conviction was affirmed, and the sentence was reduced to the maximum for first-degree murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed where the trial court's questions in voir dire created a reasonable assurance that any juror bias would be discovered, and the counsel's decision to not use a peremptory challenge against a suspect juror did not amount to ineffective assistance. The extended-term sentence was reduced to the maximum sentence for first-degree murder where defendant did not meet the criteria required to extend his sentence.

 

451 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lee


No. 1-97-3045


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 356; 708 N.E.2d 457; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 107; 236 Ill. Dec. 871



March 2, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James P. Flannery, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Arguing that he was denied his constitutional right to a jury trial when the judge failed to respond to two notes sent by the jury during deliberations, defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of home invasion, residential burglary, aggravated battery of a senior citizen, and aggravated battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of home invasion, residential burglary, aggravated battery of a senior citizen, and aggravated battery. During his trial, the lower court failed to respond to two notes sent by the jury indicating that they were deadlocked because the notes were sent when the court and counsel were at dinner. On appeal, defendant contended that the failure to respond had the effect of coercing the deadlocked jury into reaching a compromise verdict, and that his constitutional right to be present at every critical stage was violated. The court rejected this argument, finding that the lower court's failure to respond to the jury notes did not coerce the jury to reach a unanimous verdict. The court noted that the length of deliberations were not excessive given the fact that defendant was charged with eight counts. The court also found that defendant was not denied the right to be present at a critical stage in the trial. Defendant's convictions were affirmed except for his conviction for aggravated battery, which was vacated, because it was a lesser-included offense of aggravated battery of a senior citizen.


OUTCOME: Defendant's jury convictions for home invasion, residential burglary and aggravated battery of a senior citizen were not coerced because the court failed to respond to notes from the jury, and were, therefore, affirmed, but his sentence on those counts was modified to allow for application of the good conduct credit.

Coles-Moultrie Elec. Coop. v. City of Sullivan


NO. 4-98-0271


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


304 Ill. App. 3d 153; 709 N.E.2d 249; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 281; 237 Ill. Dec. 263


October 13, 1998, Submitted  
March 2, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Moultrie County, No. 97CH9. Honorable Dan L. Flannell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electric cooperative appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Moultrie County (Illinois), which dismissed plaintiff's action to enjoin defendant city from providing electrical service to disputed areas outside defendant's corporate limits.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed an order dismissing plaintiff electric cooperative's suit seeking to enjoin defendant city from providing electrical service to disputed areas outside defendant's corporate limits. Plaintiff filed suit when defendant planned to provide electric service to areas outside its corporate limits without annexing them. Plaintiff's suit was dismissed and the court ruled that the agreement was clear and unambiguous that existing service territories did not have to be annexed before defendant could serve them. The court also held that under Illinois Municipal Code, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-117-1(2) (5/11-117-1) (1996), defendant could sell electric power to areas outside its corporate limits because the agreement was a waiver by plaintiff that relinquished its rights with respect to the disputed territories. Further, the court found that the agreement was not void for lack of approval by the Illinois Commerce Commission, because it did not come within the Electric Supplier Act (Act), 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. 30/1-16 (1996). The agreement was not a "service area" agreement, and defendant was not an electric supplier, electric cooperative, or a public utility under the Act.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing plaintiff electric cooperative's action to enjoin defendant city from supplying electrical service to disputed areas was affirmed because the agreement was clear that existing service territories did not have to be annexed, and it waived plaintiff's rights to the disputed areas. The court noted that the agreement was not subject to the Electric Supplier Act and did not need approval by the Illinois Commerce Commission.

People v. Williams


No. 2-97-0956


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


302 Ill. App. 3d 975; 707 N.E.2d 980; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 84; 236 Ill. Dec. 642



February 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 11, 1999. Released for Publication March 11, 1999. As Corrected March 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County. No. 97--CF--207. Honorable Charles R. Hartman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois) convicting him of armed violence based upon possession of a controlled substance, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33A--2 (1996), unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24--1.1(a) (1996), and unlawful use of a weapon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24--1(a)(9) (1996), and sentencing him to concurrent terms of 18 and 10 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted following a jury trial of armed violence based upon possession of a controlled substance, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33A--2 (1996), unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24--1.1(a) (1996), and unlawful use of a weapon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24--1(a)(9) (1996). The jury found defendant not guilty of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The trial court sentenced him to concurrent terms of 18 years' imprisonment for armed violence and 10 years' imprisonment for unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon. No sentence was imposed for the unlawful use of a weapon. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the conviction of armed violence, reversed the conviction of unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, and vacated the sentences, holding that the sentence for unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon violated the one-act, one-crime rule where the armed violence conviction was based on the same act, and Public Act 88-680, the statute increasing the minimum sentence for armed violence violated the single subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the armed violence conviction, reversed the unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon conviction, vacated the sentences, and remanded for resentencing, holding that the unlawful possession sentence violated the one-act, one-crime rule because the armed violence conviction was based on the same act, and the statute increasing the minimum sentence for armed violence violated the state constitution's single subject rule.

People v. Dennis D. (In re Dennis D.)


No. 1-98-1775


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 442; 707 N.E.2d 667; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 76; 236 Ill. Dec. 540



February 11, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Bernetta D. Bush, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, upon a jury verdict, found him subject to involuntary admission and ordered him hospitalized pursuant to the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-100 et seq.


OVERVIEW: A day prior to respondent's involuntary admission trial, respondent informed his counsel that he did not wish her to represent him. Counsel moved for leave to withdraw and informed the court that respondent intended to proceed pro se. At trial, counsel informed the court that respondent refused to cooperate, indicated he did not want representation, and disagreed with the trial strategy. Respondent informed the court he wanted to proceed without representation. The court refused the request. After voir dire, respondent made statements in court about not wanting representation. Respondent was escorted from the courtroom and the trial was held without his presence. The jury returned a verdict finding respondent subject to involuntary admission. Respondent was ordered hospitalized pursuant to the Mental Health Code, 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-100 et seq. Respondent sought review. The court reversed, finding that the trial court erred in denying respondent's request to represent himself without first ascertaining whether or not respondent had the capacity to make an informed waiver as required by the Mental Health Code, 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-805.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding respondent subject to involuntary admission was reversed because respondent suffered prejudice as a result of the trial court's failure to inquire whether respondent understood the consequences of waiving counsel before ruling upon his capacity to do so.

People v. McVeay


No. 2-97-0127


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


302 Ill. App. 3d 960; 706 N.E.2d 539; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 64; 235 Ill. Dec. 984



February 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 96--CF--1362. Honorable Robert G. Coplan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) that declared him to be a sexually dangerous person pursuant to the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 205/0.01 et seq. (1996).


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, appellant was declared to be a sexually dangerous person pursuant to the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act (Act), 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 205/0.01 et seq. (1996), and was committed to the custody of the director of corrections until appellant's recovery and release. Appellant sought review, presenting three issues on appeal: (1) whether the trial court erred when it refused to appoint an independent psychiatrist for him; (2) whether he was denied due process; and (3) whether he was denied equal protection of the laws. The court affirmed, holding that no statutory authority or case law existed to support defendant's request for an independent psychiatrist. The court reviewed appellant's constitutional claim under the plain error doctrine, because the constitutionality of the Act had never been called into question, and held that the statute did not deprive appellant of his due process or equal protection rights. The court noted that the Act applied to all persons coming within the classification of alleged sexually dangerous persons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, declaring appellant to be a sexually dangerous person under the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act (Act), because there were no violations of appellant's constitutional rights to due process or equal protection. The Act provided for the court to appoint two psychiatrists to examine appellant, and he was treated no differently than any other person charged with the same offense.

People v. Fiedler


Nos. 3-97-0895 & 3-97-0896 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


303 Ill. App. 3d 236; 707 N.E.2d 1247; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 67; 236 Ill. Dec. 677



February 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1999. Released for Publication March 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 91--CF--1208, 91--CF--1209. Honorable Ann Brackley Jorgensen, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty but mentally ill of first-degree murder pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9--1(a)(1) and attempted murder pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8--4(a), 9--1(a)(1), and she was sentenced to concurrent terms of natural life imprisonment and 25 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9--1(a)(1) and attempted murder pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8--4(a), 9--1(a)(1). Defendant appealed and argued that the cause must be remanded because her attorney failed to comply with a court rule. The rule required an attorney appointed in a postconviction proceeding to consult with defendant to ascertain her contentions of deprivations of constitutional rights, to examine the report of proceedings at trial, and, if necessary, to amend the petition to present adequately the defendant's contentions. The court held that a postconviction proceeding had three stages. The court held that the trial court's order revealed that it considered defendant's petition under the first stage of the proceedings. The dismissal order entered by the trial court mirrored the language to be employed during a first stage dismissal. The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and attempted murder because the trial court treated the postconviction petition as if it were in the first stage of the proceedings rather than the second stage.

People v. Reynolds


NO. 4-97-0757


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


302 Ill. App. 3d 722; 706 N.E.2d 49; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 29; 235 Ill. Dec. 789


April 8, 1998, Submitted  
January 22, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Douglas County. No. 97CF28. Honorable Frank W. Lincoln, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Circuit Court of Douglas County (Illinois) of violating an order of protection under the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-30 (1996), the order of protection having been entered pursuant to the Illinois Domestic Violence Act of 1986, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/101 et seq. (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating an order of protection under the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-30 (1996), and appealed, contending that the Illinois Domestic Violence Act of 1986 (Act), 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/101 et seq. (1994), was vague and overbroad and, therefore, violative of U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV, and Ill. Const. 1970 art. I, §§ 2, 4, that the state failed to prove him guilty, that the trial court erred in excluding certain evidence, and that the prosecutor's closing argument violated due process. In affirming, the court held that the Act's definition of harassment included knowing conduct not necessary to accomplish a reasonable purpose, and defendant should have known his conduct was not reasonable; hence, the Act was not vague. The court also held that the Act was not overbroad, and the element of expression in the definition of harassment was not constitutionally protected. The court found defendant's additional assignments of error to be without merit as the evidence was sufficient to convict him, the excluded evidence was irrelevant, and defendant failed to preserve the violation of due process issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of violating an order of protection, holding that defendant should have been aware that his conduct was not reasonable, his speech was not constitutionally protected, the evidence was sufficient to convict him, any evidence excluded by the trial court was irrelevant, and defendant failed to preserve the issue of violation of due process.

Raintree Homes v. Village of Kildeer


No. 2-98-0176


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


302 Ill. App. 3d 304; 705 N.E.2d 953; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 17; 235 Ill. Dec. 770



January 22, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 97--MR--148. Honorable John R. Goshgarian, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) dismissing their amended complaint for declaratory judgment requiring defendant to refund certain impact fees, contending that the trial court erred in holding that their cause of action was barred by the one-year statute of limitations pursuant to the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1-101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs engaged in building residential homes. Plaintiffs alleged defendant municipality adopted by ordinance a schedule of impact fees required to be paid as a condition of obtaining a building permit for a residential unit. Plaintiffs alleged that these fees were unconstitutional and beyond defendant's statutory authority. The trial court found that plaintiffs had pled a tort type action and that the action was time-barred under the one-year statute of limitations for civil actions filed against a local public entity. Plaintiffs contended that the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1-101 et seq., applied only to tort claims and was, therefore, inapplicable to their constitutional claims. Defendant responded that the Act extended to any civil action brought against a local public entity. 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-205 provided that all civil actions not otherwise provided for had be commenced within five years next after the cause of action accrued. Plaintiffs' constitutional claims fell under the five-year limitations period and were timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order dismissing plaintiffs' complaint, holding that the amended complaint challenged the constitutionality of ordinances that were in effect within the five years from filing of the original complaint and was filed within the applicable five-year period of limitations.

People v. Jenkins


NO. 4-97-1104


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 918


August 28, 1998, Submitted  
December 31, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 97CF819. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for one count of armed robbery entered in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois). Appellant argued that the sentence was improper because the trial court failed to make a written finding as required by the habitual offender statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of one count of armed robbery following a jury trial in the trial court. Defendant filed a posttrial motion, which was denied by the trial court at the sentencing hearing. Defendant was sentenced as a habitual offender to a term of natural life imprisonment. Appellant then filed a motion to reconsider sentence and to declare the sentencing statute unconstitutional. No hearing was held on that motion and the record did not reveal any disposition by the trial court. The unresolved motion postdated the notice of appeal. Appellant argued that the sentence was improper because the trial court failed to make a written finding as required by the habitual offender statute. Second, he argued that the trial court failed to comply with criminal procedure code in that he was not given a hearing prior to being ordered to reimburse the county for the cost of his defense. The court dismissed the appeal because it lacked jurisdiction due to the fact that a motion was pending in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal because it had no jurisdiction to hear an appeal when an otherwise timely posttrial motion was pending, even if the motion was filed after the notice of appeal.

People v. Logan


No. 3-97-0885


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


302 Ill. App. 3d 319; 705 N.E.2d 152; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 927; 235 Ill. Dec. 539



December 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 96--CF--1919. Honorable Thomas E. Callum, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of the unlawful failure to register as a sex offender, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/3 (1996), and sentenced him to 60 days' imprisonment and 30 months' probation.


OVERVIEW: After his motion to dismiss was denied, defendant was convicted of the unlawful failure to register as a sex offender. He appealed arguing that the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq. (Supp. 1997), and the Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 152/101 et seq. (Supp. 1997) were unconstitutional in that they violated the ex post facto clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The court rejected his argument concluding that the legislature did not intend to impose punishment with the enactment of the statutes, and that the statutes did not have a punitive effect. The court found that the purpose of the statutes was to protect the public. The court rejected defendant's argument that he was deprived of his right to due process because the statutes did not provide for a hearing. The court concluded that defendant failed to show that the statutes deprived him of a protected liberty or property interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the unlawful failure to register as a sex offender.

People v. Jones


No. 1-97-3747


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 892; 707 N.E.2d 192; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 932; 236 Ill. Dec. 347



December 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the effectiveness of his counsel and the constitutionality of his sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of two counts of aggravated battery with a firearm under the theory of accountability for the actions of a co-defendant.


OVERVIEW: At trial, defendant's attorney failed to object to the admission of a co-defendant's statements. Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery with a firearm under a theory of accountability for the actions of a co-defendant. Defendant sought review and argued that he was denied effective assistance of counsel as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI. The appellate court found that the elicitation of the co-defendant's statement constituted reasonable trial strategy in an effort to distance defendant from both the shootings. Similarly, counsel's failure to object to the co-defendant's statements included within defendant's custodial statement constituted a strategic choice. The appellate court modified defendant's sentence because the legislation that enacted the truth-in-sentencing provision was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, as modified, because defendant failed to establish that his trial counsel's actions fell below an objective standard of reasonableness and as such, he was not denied effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The appellate court modified defendant's sentence because the legislation that enacted the truth-in-sentencing provision, under which sentence was imposed, was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment and sentence, as modified, because defendant failed to establish that his trial counsel's actions fell below an objective standard of reasonableness; therefore, he was not denied the effective assistance of counsel.

People v. Mondragon


No. 1-97-3920


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 936



December 31, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Colleen McSweeney Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for aggravated battery of a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant severely beat his common law wife's five-year-old daughter. He was convicted of aggravated battery of a child and was sentenced to a term of 30 years in prison. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion because he based his decision on the evidence, the aggravating and mitigating factors presented, and the presentence investigation report in sentencing defendant to the maximum sentence possible. The court found that the truth-in-sentencing provision that was enacted in Pub. Act 89-404 was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule of the Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d), but that the subsequent amendment by 1996 Ill. Laws 588, which added the predatory criminal sexual assault of a child to the identical truth-in-sentencing provision was constitutional. Because defendant committed the crime after the truth-in-sentencing law was enacted, the court affirmed his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing a 30-year sentence. The court found that although Public Act 89-404 was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule, the subsequent reenactment of the truth-in-sentencing provision in 1996 Ill. Laws 588 validated the sentencing provision and applied to defendant.

In re Estate of Hall


No. 1-97-4654


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 829; 707 N.E.2d 201; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 937; 236 Ill. Dec. 356



December 31, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James W. Kennedy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner partner of decedent sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed her claim seeking a surviving spouse's share of her partner's estate, after respondent administrator of estate, argued that petitioner could not be a surviving spouse because the state did not recognize same-sex marriages.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner partner of decedent sought a surviving spouse's share of decedent's estate in probate court after decedent died intestate. Respondent administrator of the estate filed a motion to dismiss the claim asserting that petitioner could not be a surviving spouse because Illinois did not recognize same-sex marriages. The trial court granted the motion. Upon review, petitioner argued that the prohibition against same-sex marriages violated the equal protection provisions of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The court held that the issue was nonjusticiable and moot because it did not affect the actual controversy between the parties. In making the determination, the court held that it had to decide whether actual spousal status could be conferred upon petitioner and whether the relationship between decedent and petitioner could be construed as a valid marriage. The court held that the facts alleged did not meet the statutory requirements for a valid marriage and spousal status could not be conferred. Further, adjudicating petitioner's constitutional challenge would result in the same nonmarital status. The decision of the probate court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the probate court and determined that the issue was not justiciable because by declaring the same-sex marriage prohibition unconstitutional, petitioner partner of decedent would still not be conferred spousal status as to benefit under the Probate Act.

Mr. B's, Inc. v. City of Chicago


Nos. 1-97-2149 & 97-2279


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 930; 706 N.E.2d 1001; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 900; 236 Ill. Dec. 127



December 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the. Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 L 50040. Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ticket brokers appealed from a grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant holding that an amended amusement tax ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 4-156-020(F) (amended Nov. 15, 1995), was not an unconstitutional violation of Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e).


OVERVIEW: Ticket brokers contended that Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 4-156-020(F) (amended November 15, 1995), an amendment to the tax ordinance, was an unconstitutional service or occupation tax by the city. The amended amusement tax ordinance was not an unconstitutional service or occupation tax violating Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e). The main substance of the transactions between ticket brokers and their patrons was the purchase of a ticket as tangible property and any other services rendered were incidental. The tickets were tangible personal property, and therefore, the city's amended amusement tax ordinance did not constitute an occupational or service tax. The amusement taxes were within the category of items within home rule powers. The amended amusement tax was authorized by 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-42-1. The brokers did not provide an adequate record to review whether the city's amended amusement tax was an unconstitutional extraterritorial exercise of its home rule authority when applied to ticket brokers located outside the city.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed but was reversed and remanded for the purpose of resolving the material issue of whether the ordinance was being extraterritorially applied to the ticket brokers.

People v. Olsen


No. 1-97-2928


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of the unlawful use of weapons in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1(a)(7)(1992). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: An arson and explosives investigator was called to the scene of a metal railroad trestle bridge after a total of 21 red and blue plastic containers were found hanging from both sides. An advertisement for a fur store was painted on the sides of the bridge. The containers were plastic peanut butter jars. Each jar contained gasoline and a separate green hobby fuse inserted into the top with a metal plate underneath. Several of the fuses had been lit but had not ignited. Only one of the fuses had ignited and that device had not exploded but had only burned. Based on fingerprints on the jars, defendant was arrested. She testified that she had intended to illuminate the banners with the lit jars, which she called "lanterns," in order to protest the sale of furs. The investigator testified that he would classify the jars as incendiary devices, but they could be classified as explosives if they had the proper fuel-to-air ratios. Defendant was convicted. After judgment was entered, the appellate court found that the State had not shown under the applicable statute that the devices were "explosive" devices designed to detonate, and thus, the conviction was improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

People v. Hancock

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT
