DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) denied defendant's motion to suppress, and entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, unlawful possession of a controlled substance, unlawful use of weapons, and two counts of armed violence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant told police investigating defendant that he had been at defendant's apartment, that defendant sold cannabis to another individual, and that defendant offered to sell cocaine to the confidential informant. Based on this information, the police permitted the confidential informant to take part in a controlled purchase of drugs from the defendant. After the purchase was made, the police obtained a "no-knock" search warrant. The warrant was supported by a complaint that stated defendant had been involved in sales for at least ten days. Defendant left and drove off; he was subsequently arrested. Police then executed the warrant after they obtained a master key to defendant's residence. Defendant moved to suppress the money and cocaine that was found. After the trial court denied the motion and defendant was convicted, the appellate court found the "no-knock" search did not violated defendant's constitutional rights because defendant was absent when the search warrant was executed, no property was damaged in executing the warrant, and defendant had been involved in a continuing course of criminal activity.

In re Marriage of Charnogorsky


No. 1-97-4463 & 1-98-1523


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 649; 707 N.E.2d 79; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 896; 236 Ill. Dec. 234



December 18, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Lisa Murphy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father filed a petition to require petitioner mother to use the last name of each parent for their child, and the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, denied the petition. The father then filed a petition to change the child's name, pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/21--101 (West 1996), but the circuit court denied that petition, ruling that the father lacked standing. The father appealed from both rulings.


OVERVIEW: After the circuit court dissolved the marriage of the father and the mother, a daughter was born to the parties. The mother was given custody of the child, and the father was awarded visitation rights. The father claimed that he and the mother had agreed that their daughter would use both of their last names; however, the mother used only her own last name for the child. The father was unsuccessful in obtaining a court order requiring the mother to use both last names. On appeal, the appellate court held: (1) the circuit court did not err by dismissing the father's petition to require the mother to use both of their last names as their child's last name; (2) the father failed to show that the exclusion of two witnesses was reversible error; (3) the circuit court did not err in entering a directed finding that the parties did not enter an agreement that the child's last name would include both of the parties's last names; (4) the circuit court did not err in denying the father's petition to change the child's last name; and (5) the father failed to fulfill his burden of proof that an equal protection violation had occurred.


OUTCOME: The rulings were affirmed.

First Fin. Funding Corp. v. Rosewell (In re County Treasurer)


No. 1-97-3705


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 639; 707 N.E.2d 60; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 873; 236 Ill. Dec. 215



December 18, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. VTS-970179. Honorable Michael J. Murphy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation filed a petition to declare a tax sale to be in error pursuant to § 21-310 of the Property Tax Code, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/21-310 (1996). The corporation also sought reimbursement with interest. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, granted the petition, but declined to award interest. The corporation filed a petition for reconsideration, which was denied. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation bought the lien of the 1994 delinquent real estate taxes against a parcel of real estate at the annual Cook County tax sale, but it later sought to have the sale declared an error because the property was owned by a university and was not subject to taxation. Although the circuit court declared the sale in error, it refused to award the corporation interest because the failure to perform either a physical inspection of the property or a title inspection on the property would not be excused where it could be shown that a reasonable inspection would have disclosed the grounds on which the sale in error was declared to be erroneous. The appellate court held that the circuit court erred in defining the term "actual knowledge" as used in § 21-315(b)(iv) of the Property Tax Code, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/21-315(b)(iv) (1996), so broadly as to contemplate the existence of "actual knowledge" based solely upon the ability to obtain such knowledge. Also, the circuit court's determination that the corporation should be denied interest under § 21-315(b)(iv) was against the manifest weight of the evidence presented.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and remanded.

National Sch. Bus Serv. v. Department of Revenue


No. 1-97-3560


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 820; 706 N.E.2d 936; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 855; 236 Ill. Dec. 62



December 15, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John A. Ward, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bus service sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held in favor of appellee Department of Revenue (department) that the activities of the bus service did not fall within the definition of "rolling stock" under the Use Tax Act (Act), 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 105/3-55 (1992) so as to exempt the bus service from tax imposed under the Act.


OVERVIEW: A bus service that operated in-state school buses purchased 25 buses in order to supplement its income with charger trips for private groups, some of which required trips to other states. The bus service paid no use tax on the new buses, claiming they was exempted under § 3-55 of the Act, which excluded tax on "rolling stock" moving in interstate commerce. The department audited the bus service and on discovering less than 5 percent of its travelled miles involved interstate travel, denied the exemption and assessed back taxes and penalties. The lower court affirmed the department, and on appeal the court affirmed, holding that the department's interpretation of the Act was entitled to substantial deference, and that the department's requirement of regular and frequent use in interstate commerce for the exemption was reasonable. This did not create an unconstitutional classification by distinguishing rolling stock used regularly in interstate commerce from that used only irregularly, as the purpose of the statute was to avoid multistate taxation, which was reasonably served by the distinction. Moreover, denial of the exemption was not against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that the bus service was not exempt from taxation.

People v. DeLuca


No. 1-97-3857


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 454; 706 N.E.2d 927; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 850; 236 Ill. Dec. 53



December 14, 1998, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Daniel Weber, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to unlawful sale of a firearm by a liquor licensee, two counts of unlawful use of a weapon, and one count of theft. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) ordered defendant's weapon collection destroyed, and defendant challenged that order.


OVERVIEW: Police executed search warrants at defendant's home and business. They seized 138 guns. The trial court eventually ordered that the weapons be destroyed. Defendant argued that he was denied due process because the trial court ordered destruction of the weapons without a hearing. Defendant was not denied due process simply because he made the strategic choice to argue the legal merits based on stipulated facts. The trial court did not deprive defendant's wife of due process when it ordered the weapons destroyed. The weapons were subject to confiscation pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-6(a) (1994). It was undisputed defendant was guilty of illegal arms sales. The State demonstrated by a preponderance of the evidence that the guns were connected to illegal activity. The trial court could have reasonably inferred that the weapons stored at defendant's home represented the inventory necessary to carry out the illegal sales.


OUTCOME: The judgment ordering destruction of the weapons was affirmed.

Brandt v. Time Ins. Co.


Nos. 1-97-2913 & 1-98-0143 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


302 Ill. App. 3d 159; 704 N.E.2d 843; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 844; 235 Ill. Dec. 270



December 10, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE RICHARD E. NEVILLE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: No. 1-97-2913--Affirmed. No. 1-98-0143--Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured contested an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her claims against defendant insured for failure to state a claim in the insured's action to recover damages sustained as a consequence of the insurer's refusal to pay her claims under a health insurance policy. The insured alleged breach of contract, violations of 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/155 (1996) and 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/1 (1996), and fraud.


OVERVIEW: The insured signed a blank application for insurance coverage and gave it to her agent to complete and submit. The agent completed the application, indicating that the insured had not been treated in the past five years for diabetes, knowing that she had been diagnosed with Type II diabetes. Subsequently, the insured was diagnosed with terminal stomach cancer and the insurer rescinded the policy based on its discovery that the insured had been treated for diabetes. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the fraud counts but reversed the summary judgment, holding that a fact question remained as to whether the agent acted as the insurer's agent, and thus whether his knowledge of the misrepresentation was to be imputed to the insurer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the insured's claims against the insurer for fraud and violation of the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, but reversed the trial court's summary judgment on her claims for breach of contract and of the Insurance Code, concluding that there were factual issues to be determined concerning the insurer's imputed knowledge of the agent's misrepresentation.

Kaufman, Litwin & Feinstein v. Edgar


No. 1-97-2455


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


301 Ill. App. 3d 826; 704 N.E.2d 756; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 817; 235 Ill. Dec. 183



December 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted summary judgment in favor of defendant state officials and intervenor attorney in a declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiff law firm alleging that certain 1997 amendments to the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act (Act) were unconstitutional. The law firm appealed.


OVERVIEW: The law firm's attorneys practiced in the domestic relations area. The law firm alleged that certain amendments of Act violated the separation of powers doctrine and that all or certain of these amendments violated procedural and substantive due process, the contract clauses of the Illinois and United States Constitutions, and constituted special legislation. Most of the amendments complained of related to fees. The court affirmed. The court held that: (1) where the legislature grants a right that neither existed at common law nor was granted by the constitution, it was free to define the parameters of its purely statutory creature; (2) the legislature was entitled to remedy abuses of a statutory cause of action by enacting procedural rules more specific than those general remedies set forth in the supreme court rules; (3) the legislature had the authority to devise procedures to be followed in causes of action it creates, such as dissolution of marriage, and the power to amend such legislation; and (4) the challenged amendments did not involve the contracts clause because they did not impair the obligations of any existing contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Freed v. Ryan


No. 1-97-0612


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


301 Ill. App. 3d 952; 704 N.E.2d 746; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 809; 235 Ill. Dec. 173



November 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE THOMAS P. DURKIN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff student was cited for violating a city ordinance after he used another individual's driver's license to gain admission to a bar. Defendant, Secretary of State of Illinois, suspended his driver's license pursuant to § 6-206(a)(10) of the Illinois Vehicle Code (Code), 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-206 (1994). The student appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denying his petition for administrative review.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the student argued that § 6-206(a)(10), which authorized the suspension of driving privileges where a person used false identification, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Applying a rational-basis test, it held that the statute did not violate the student's due process rights. The Code's primary purpose was the safe and legal operation of motor vehicles and it evidenced an intent to prevent drunken driving and driving by persons under 21 years old who had consumed alcohol. These were legitimate governmental goals. The statutory declaration that suspension of driving privileges was a legitimate means of removing dangerous drivers from the highway was not irrational. Further, the legislature could rationally speculate that license holders under 21 years old could use false identification in an attempt to gain access to alcohol and that such conduct would lead to an increase in drunken driving or driving by persons under 21 years old who had consumed alcohol. Thus, the legislature could rationally seek to deter these offenses by providing for the suspension of the driving privileges of a license holder who used false identification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, denying the student's petition for administrative review of the secretary's order suspending his driver's license.

People v. M.G. (In re M.G.)


No. 1-97-1440


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


301 Ill. App. 3d 401; 703 N.E.2d 594; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 798; 234 Ill. Dec. 733



November 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 30, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 96 JD 15032. The Honorable Daniel Kelly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile challenged his adjudication, in the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), and mandatory disposition pursuant to the Illinois Violent Juvenile Offender Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-36, challenging the constitutionality of the statute and arguing various procedural deficiencies relating to notice.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Illinois Violent Juvenile Offender Act, a juvenile was placed in the custody of the department of corrections after his second adjudication involving a violent offense. He challenged the mandatory disposition provisions of the statute as violating Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, which called for proportional punishment, and the due process guarantee of the United States Constitution. The appeals court upheld the law as reasonably addressing the problem of youth violence, limiting a court's sentencing discretion only as necessary to protect this compelling interest. The appeals court then held that service was properly effected on the juvenile's incarcerated father by certified mail, and that notice of intent to seek adjudication as a violent offender was timely and properly served on the juvenile's counsel by fax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication and disposition.

 

477 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Exhibits, Inc. v. Sweet


No. 1-97-3636 & 1-97-3229 Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


303 Ill. App. 3d 423; 709 N.E.2d 236; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 799; 237 Ill. Dec. 250



November 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 9, 1999. Released for Publication April 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Lester A. Bonaguro, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which granted summary judgment in favor of the Illinois Department of Revenue. The company had sought to recover taxes paid under protest as a result of the Service Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.101 et seq. (1987). The company asserted the tax violated the commerce clause and thus was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The tax applied to persons engaged in the business of making sales of service. Although it was a tax on the service occupation, the tax was calculated at a percentage rate of the cost of tangible personal property transferred as an incident to the sale of service. The company was located in Illinois and provided the service of making trade show exhibits which it transported to trade shows by common carrier. It also assembled, maintained, and disassembled the exhibits at the trade shows. In the transactions at issue, the exhibits were sold to Illinois customers and initially delivered to the customers at trade shows outside Illinois for use at those locations. Following disassembly of the exhibits at the end of the trade shows, the exhibits were returned to Illinois for storage and reuse. The company denied that it was liable for any tax under the act and contended the exemptions were legitimate because the exhibits were delivered and first used out of state, notwithstanding the subsequent storage in Illinois. The appellate court held the statute did not impose multiple taxation and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

PEOPLE v. WORDEN


No. 2-97-0553


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 836; 702 N.E.2d 611; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 737; 234 Ill. Dec. 271



October 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County. No. 95--CF--386. Honorable Charles R. Hartman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Stephenson County (Illinois) which convicted defendant, after a guilty plea of aggravated criminal sexual assault in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14(b)(1), and sentenced him to six years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction, defendant appealed contending that he should have had the mittimus corrected to reflect that he was eligible for good-conduct credit without reference to the recently enacted truth-in-sentencing legislation. Specifically, on appeal defendant contended that he was not subject to the truth-in-sentencing provisions because the implementing legislation was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that defendant agreed to plead guilty in exchange for a six-year sentence and the State's agreement to dismiss two misdemeanor charges. Further, the appellate court found that although defendant's conviction was produced by a statute which had previously been ruled unconstitutional, 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 35/1 et seq., that fact did not affect the computation of defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, and modified to properly reflect defendant's appropriate sentence.

 

479 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mosley


No. 3-97-0014


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 725; 702 N.E.2d 280; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 741; 234 Ill. Dec. 114


September 10, 1998, Submitted  
October 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit. Peoria County, Illinois. No. 96-CF-385. Honorable Robert Barnes, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the Tenth Judicial Circuit of Peoria County (Illinois), which convicted defendant in a jury trial of first degree murder, under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1994), and which sentenced him to a term of 40 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a 17-year-old gang member who drove a fellow gang member to murder a competing gang member. Defendant testified that he joined the gang because he feared for his own life and for the life of his mother. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in striking his affirmative defense of compulsion. He wanted to introduce evidence to show that he had been compelled to participate in the murder because of the circumstances of his life. On motion of the state, the defense of compulsion was stricken. The court held that the defense of compulsion was unavailable in any murder prosecution. The fact that defendant was not eligible for the death penalty, due to his juvenile status, did not enable him to assert the compulsion defense. Defendant next contended that the truth-in-sentencing statute, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3 (1994), was enacted in violation of the "single subject rule" in the Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d). The court held that the constitutionality of the truth-in-sentencing law was not properly raised on direct review of a judgment of conviction but must instead be raised by way of an action for habeas corpus, mandamus, or declaratory judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder. The court found that the trial court did not commit error when it struck the affirmative defense of compulsion.

 

480 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Blanks


No. 3-97-0188


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 361; 701 N.E.2d 547; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 703; 233 Ill. Dec. 697



October 9, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 95--CF--5946. Honorable Amy Bertani, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pled guilty to aggravated criminal sexual assault. The defendant subsequently filed a post-conviction petition for a modification of his sentence on the ground that he received ineffective assistance of counsel in making his guilty plea. The 12th Judicial Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois) dismissed the petition as frivolous and patently without merit. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the defendant contended that his sentence had to be modified because it was imposed pursuant to the truth-in-sentencing statute, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3--6--3 (1995), and that statute was unconstitutional. The State argued that the defendant waived the issue on appeal because he failed to raise it in any prior proceeding. In reply, the defendant argued that a challenge to the constitutionality of a statute was not subject to waiver. The appellate court rejected the defendant's arguments. The court found that the defendant did not argue that the truth-in-sentencing law was unconstitutional in his post-conviction petition, only that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. Therefore, he waived the issue. Additionally, the truth-in-sentencing statute was collateral to the statutes under which the defendant was convicted and sentenced. Accordingly, an attack on the constitutionality of the truth-in-sentencing law was subject to waiver.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

481 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Alliance of Police v. Ill. State Labor Relations Bd.


No. 3-97-0865


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 377; 701 N.E.2d 825; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 704; 233 Ill. Dec. 760



October 9, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of an order of the Illinois State Labor Relations Board. No. S-VR-97-13.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police alliance (Alliance) petitioned for review of an order of the defendant labor relations board. In that decision, the board sustained a ruling by its Executive Director (Director) that denied the alliance's request for voluntary recognition certification of a proposed "bargaining unit" under the Illinois Public Labor Relations Act (Act) 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 315/1 et seq., (1996).


OVERVIEW:  5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 315/1 et seq. (1996) among other things, gave state employees the right to voluntarily join a union and to bargain collectively with their employer over issues concerning wages, hours of work, and other terms of employment. In order to be covered under the act, a union's bargaining unit must be certified by the labor relations board. The appellate court held that the act was inapplicable to the city that employed the police officers, as the city employed less than 35 employees. Having held that the act was inapplicable to the city, the only other issue presented in the case at bar was whether the act was unconstitutional. 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 315/20(b) (1996) must be analyzed under the rational basis test. Under that test, the statute need only have a rational basis for distinguishing the class to which the law applied from the class to which the law did not apply. If any set of facts reasonably could have justified the classification, it should have been upheld. The court found that the act did not violate the equal protection clause and was therefore not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the labor relations board was affirmed.

 

482 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Farina v. Sensor


No. 2-97-1141


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 333; 701 N.E.2d 1147; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 696; 233 Ill. Dec. 873



October 5, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 95--FA--64. Honorable Sharon L. Prather, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), dismissing her petition for visitation with her granddaughter after determining that the doctrine of res judicata barred the petition.


OVERVIEW: After a paternity proceeding established that an individual was the father of plaintiff's child, the trial court granted visitation to the child's grandmother. Later, the visitation was terminated, and visitation was granted to the father, but only while in the home of the child's grandmother, with whom the father lived. Thereafter, the father moved from his residence with the grandmother, and she brought a petition for visitation. The trial court dismissed the petition, finding that the order terminating the grandmother's visitation barred her subsequent petition under the doctrine of res judicata. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that the termination order was not a final determination on the merits that visitation by the grandmother would not be in the child's best interests and therefore that res judicata did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

483 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nicholson


NO. 4-97-0378


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 256; 701 N.E.2d 517; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 673; 233 Ill. Dec. 667


July 14, 1998, Oral Argument Held, Submitted  
September 30, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 1998. As Corrected December 28, 1998. Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 96CF1171. Honorable G. Michael Prall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for three armed robberies, attempted armed robbery, and aggravated battery. Because the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), found that defendant had inflicted great bodily harm on a victim, defendant was required under "truth-in-sentencing" legislation, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(ii) (1996), to serve 85 percent of his sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed contending that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, that the "truth-in-sentencing" provision violated the "single subject rule" of Ill. Const. 1970, art. IV, § 8 (d), and that the truth-in-sentencing provision violated the equal protection clause.The court summarily rejected the contention that the truth-in-sentencing provisions deprived convicts of equal protection. The court also held that defense counsel was not ineffective in failing to seek a severance, and that although defense counsel should have objected to the prosecutor's request that defendant comment on the veracity of certain witnesses, defendant was not substantially prejudiced by the error. Additionally, defense counsel was not incompetent for failing to object to evidence properly admitted. Finally, the court held that the truth-in-sentencing provision was not unconstitutional and did not violate the "single subject rule" of the Illinois Constitution. Accordingly, defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

484 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Villareal ex rel. Villareal v. Peebles


No. 1-96-2713


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


299 Ill. App. 3d 556; 701 N.E.2d 145; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 637; 233 Ill. Dec. 502



September 24, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 94 D 651368. HONORABLE DENNIS DOHM, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother, on behalf of her child, filed a cause of action against defendant alleged father to establish the paternity of and support for the mother's child. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered an order finding the alleged father to be the natural father of the child. The trial court also entered orders of support and withholding. The alleged father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The blood tests the trial court ordered the mother, child, and alleged father to undergo resulted in a combined paternity index (CPI) of 2,582 to 1. The mother testified that in July, August, and September 1986, she engaged in sexual intercourse with the alleged father and no one else. The child was born in May 1987. The alleged father denied ever having sexual relations with the mother. The alleged father's expert witness testified that the CPI was not significant in this case. On appeal, the alleged father argued that 75 Ill. Comp. Stat. 11(f)(4) (1994) of the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984 was unconstitutional because it declared a CPI of 500 to 1 to be significant regardless of the laboratory protocol used by the testing facility. The court held that (1) the alleged father waived his constitutional challenge where he raised it for the first time on appeal, (2) the alleged father failed to promptly inform the attorney general under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 19, 134 Ill. 2d R. 19 concerning his constitutional challenge, and (3) that the alleged father had not presented sufficient evidence to rebut the statutory presumption of paternity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order finding the alleged father to be the natural father of the child. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in not ordering the mother to produce the examining physician, the physician who performed the blood tests. The court held the trial court did not need the testimony of the examining physician where the CPI of 2,582 to 1 was greater than the 500 to 1 statutory CPI.

People v. Dainty


No. 4-97-0221


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fulton County. No. 95--CF--280. Honorable Patricia A. Walton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed violence in the Circuit Court of Fulton County (Illinois). Defendant appealed on the ground that the single subject rule under Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) was violated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged on several counts and convicted of armed violence. Defendant argued that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33A-3(a-5)(1996), which increased the minimum sentence for armed violence, violated the single subject rule under the Illinois Constitution. The court held that the statute did violate the single subject rule and was unconstitutional in its entirety. The court reasoned that the law contained a multitude of provisions and created several new laws regarding unrelated matters, thereby violating the Illinois Constitution. The court remanded the case back for the trial court to sentence defendant in accordance with the old sentencing provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated his sentence and remanded the case back so that the trial court could sentence defendant in accordance with the old sentencing provisions.

People v. Powell


No. 1-96-3644


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


299 Ill. App. 3d 92; 701 N.E.2d 68; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 617; 233 Ill. Dec. 425



September 16, 1998, Decided; Nunc Pro Tunc June 30, 1998


NOTICE:   [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph J. Urso, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which sentenced defendant to 16 years' imprisonment on each count of attempted first-degree murder and armed violence of which he was convicted. Defendant was convicted of two counts of each offense, and his sentences were to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of two counts of attempted first-degree murder and two counts of armed violence. The trial court sentenced defendant to 16 years' imprisonment on each count. Defendant's sentences were to run concurrently. On appeal, defendant contended that his sentence for armed violence violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution of 1970 because the penalty for armed violence was disproportionate to the penalty for the predicate offense of aggravated battery. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that: (1) the authority defendant relied on was unpersuasive in support of his argument that aggravated battery with a firearm was a more serious offense than aggravated battery based on great bodily harm, there was no reason to interfere with the sentencing procedures developed by legislature in relation to the offenses at issue in the case; (2) defendant's constitutional rights had not been violated and his convictions for armed violence and aggravated robbery were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which sentenced defendant to 16 years' imprisonment on each count of attempted first-degree murder and armed violence of which he was convicted.

People v. Jones


No. 4-97-0388


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 739; 702 N.E.2d 984; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 624; 234 Ill. Dec. 330


February 10, 1998, Submitted  
September 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 25, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 96--CF--561. Honorable Clark E. Erickson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment entered in the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him for aggravated battery of a police officer and charged by traffic citations with illegal sound amplification, reckless driving and disobeying a police officer. Defendant was sentenced to five years incarceration for aggravated battery and assessed court costs on all other convictions.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant because of the excessive volume emitting from his car radio. Refusing to comply with the officer's request for his license and insurance card, defendant sped off while the officer's arm was caught in the car window in an attempt to unlock the door. The officer hung on to the car as the defendant reached speeds in excess of 70 miles per hour. On appeal, defendant contended that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-611 was unconstitutional because it was content-based and was overbroad in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I. While the court agreed that the state had a substantial interest in protecting its citizens from unwelcome noise on city streets, it failed to provide a compelling reason for discriminating between the amplification of commercial speech and non-commercial speech. Statements regarding the victim's occupation were made within the judge's discussion of the factual circumstances of the crime, and the record did not support defendant's contention that the judge improperly relied on the victim's occupation to enhanced the sentence, especially since the mid-range sentence of five years was well within the discretion of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings.

Maun v. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation


NO. 4-98-0096


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


299 Ill. App. 3d 388; 701 N.E.2d 791; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 763; 233 Ill. Dec. 726


August 18, 1998, Oral Argument Held, Submitted  
September 3, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rule 23 Order Redesignated Opinion nunc pro tunc and Ordered Published November 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 96MR0238. Honorable Robert J. Eggers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor challenged the decision of the from Circuit Court of Sangamon County, Illinois, which affirmed the suspension of his license to practice medicine for 18 months by defendant Illinois Department of Professional Regulation and its director, based on doctor's violation of § 22(A)(25) of the Medical Practice Act of 1987, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/22(A)(25) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Doctor was a plastic surgeon licensed to practice medicine in the state. A disciplinary complaint sought disciplinary action for charging too much for his services in violation of the Act. Department suspended his license and the circuit court affirmed. Doctor appealed, arguing that § 22(A)(25) was unconstitutionally vague; § 22(A)(25) was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority; because the Department had failed to promulgate rules defining certain phrases as set forth in § 22(A)(25), it could not enforce that section against him; and the Department's decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court found the terms in § 22(A)(25) were capable of sufficiently precise interpretation to serve as a guide to those who had to comply with that section. Doctor's noncompliance with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 341(e)(7) resulted in his forfeiting the argument that § 22(A)(25) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him. Further, there was proper delegation of legislative authority and the statute sufficiently outlined requirements. The record contained sufficient evidence to support the Department's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Brooks v. Cigna Prop. & Cas. Cos.


No. 1-97-4260


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


299 Ill. App. 3d 68; 700 N.E.2d 1052; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 595; 233 Ill. Dec. 344



September 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard E. Neville, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant insurer's motion to compel arbitration of plaintiff's uninsured motorist claim under § 143a of the Illinois Insurance Code, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/143a (1996), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 755a (1983).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insured filed a claim with defendant insurer under § 143a of the Illinois Insurance Code, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/143a (1996), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 755a (1983), after his injury by an uninsured motorist, and demanded arbitration. When the claim was not resolved, plaintiff filed an action for breach of contract. The circuit court granted defendant's motion to compel arbitration. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court denied plaintiff's motion to stay the appeal pending a decision on the constitutionality of § 143a in light of differences in the statutory provisions of the relevant version of § 143a. The court held that arbitration of claims under § 143a differed from contractual arbitration because it was compulsory and the statute did not merely provide for optional arbitration. The court found that when plaintiff filed his claim for uninsured benefits he voluntarily subjected himself to the mandates of § 143a, which required arbitration of the claim as to liability and damages. The court held that the mandatory arbitration under § 143a could not be waived and that defendant's conduct in not proceeding to arbitration did not amount to waiver or estoppel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted defendant insurer's motion to compel arbitration of plaintiff insured's uninsured motorist claim. The court held that the relevant statute required mandatory arbitration that could not be waived. The court remanded for a decision on plaintiff's claim for "vexatious delay."

People ex rel. Waller v. 1996 Saturn


No. 2-97-0570


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 96--MR--429. Honorable Henry C. Tonigan III, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which decided that the claimant's car was subject forfeiture pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/36-1.


OVERVIEW: The claimant had been convicted of burglary and his car was subject to forfeiture under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/26-1. On appeal, the court affirmed the forfeiture. The court did so because the inherent gravity of the offense was not greater than the fine imposed where the total fine available was $ 20,000 and the value of the claimant's vehicle was $ 17,000, the car was an integral part of the commission of the burglaries, and the criminal activity using the claimant's car was extensive in terms of time where the burglaries would have been much more difficult to accomplish without the use of claimant's car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment declaring that the claimant's car was subject to forfeiture for being used in the commission of burglaries.

People v. Wiggins


No. 1-97-0961


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


298 Ill. App. 3d 766; 700 N.E.2d 119; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 565; 233 Ill. Dec. 18



August 17, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CR 16543. Honorable Thomas M. Davy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of unlawful use of a weapon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1(a)(10) (1992). Defendant asserted that § 5/24-1 violated the single subject rule, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d)(2), and also that she was denied effective assistance of counsel because her attorney failed to raise the issue of her fitness for trial, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-21 (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a trial court of unlawful use of a weapon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1(a)(10) (1992). The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, finding that § 5/24 did not violate the single subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) (1970), because the provisions of the entire law of which that section was a portion were all germane to a single expressed purpose. Also, the court found that defendant had not received ineffective assistance of counsel when her attorney failed to raise the issue of her fitness for trial owing to her use of psychotropic medication because under the applicable law, such drug use did not render defendant presumptively unfit for trial, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-21 (1996).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

People v. Selby


No. 4-97-0960


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


298 Ill. App. 3d 605; 698 N.E.2d 1102; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 552; 232 Ill. Dec. 672


July 16, 1998, Submitted  
August 11, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 13, 1998.Released for Publication September 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. Nos. 97CF31, 97CF32, 97CF33. Honorable Charles E. Glennon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which dismissed its charges against defendants.


OVERVIEW: A grand jury returned indictments against defendants on four counts of official misconduct and one count of conspiracy. The trial court dismissed the indictments and the state appealed. The state claimed that the trial court erred by finding Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 120.50 constitutionally infirm. Defendants claimed that the court lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal because of the trial court's decision concerning § 120.50. The court held that (1) it had jurisdiction to hear the matter because trial court's ruling did not effectively invalidate any portion of the official misconduct statute; (2) the trial court erred in ruling that § 120.50 was indefinite and uncertain; and (3) the fact that § 120.50 failed to specifically identify the violation as a criminal offense did not require a dismissal of the charges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's dismissal of the charges.

Alencastro v. Sheahan


1-97-0772


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


297 Ill. App. 3d 478; 698 N.E.2d 1095; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 525; 232 Ill. Dec. 665



July 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied July 28, 1998. Released for Publication August 7, 1998.
Appeal denied by Alencastro v. Sheahan, 181 Ill. 2d 567, 706 N.E.2d 495, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1660, 235 Ill. Dec. 940 (1998)
Related proceeding at Alencastro v. State, 54 Ill. Ct. Cl. 457, 2001 Ill. Ct. Cl. LEXIS 28 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 95-L-14466. THE HONORABLE Joseph N. Casciato, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant sought review after the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the tenant's claim for illegal eviction against defendants, sheriff's deputies and bank. The trial court dismissed the tenant's civil rights claim against the sheriff based on sovereign immunity and dismissed the state law negligence claim for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The tenant claimed that the eviction was unlawful because she had not received notice of the foreclosure proceedings or the sale of the premises. The tenant alleged that the sheriff was liable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for maintaining a policy or procedure that allowed persons not named in a court order for possession to be summarily evicted and that the sheriff was statutorily liable for the negligence of his deputies under 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6016. The court held that (1) a sheriff's nondiscretionary, statutory duty to execute Writs of Assistance and other state court orders militated heavily in favor of recognizing that a sheriff acted as a state official in such a capacity; (2) the deputies were carrying out orders; (3) the sheriff had not had any part of the decision to evict; (4) the behaviour of the deputies was not illegal; (5) the sheriff could not be sued in his individual capacity because he was not individually involved in the eviction; and (6) the tenant had to bring an action against the state in the Court of Claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

People v. Rankin


NO. 4-97-0664


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


297 Ill. App. 3d 818; 697 N.E.2d 1246; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 502; 232 Ill. Dec. 316


June 23, 1998, Submitted  
July 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 95CF212. Honorable Charles E. Glennon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which denied his post-conviction petition filed under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1(a)(4) (1994), challenging his six-year extended-term sentence for unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) (1994).


OVERVIEW: After he received a six-year extended-term sentence for unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) (1994), defendant filed a post-conviction petition under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1(a)(4) (1994), challenging the sentence. The court reversed the denial of defendant's petition, holding that (1) the defendant did not forfeit his challenge to the extended-term sentence and he properly raised the issue in the post-conviction proceeding; (2) the trial court erred in using a prior felony conviction as both an element of an offense and a justification to impose an extended term; (3) one year of defendant's sentence was void as greater than that permitted by statute; (4) the extended-term sentence could only have been imposed on the most serious class of offenses of which the defendant was convicted; and (5) defendant's prior juvenile adjudication of delinquency could not be used to justify an extended term. The court directed the trial court to reduce defendant's sentence to five years on remand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment which denied defendant's post-conviction petition, and it remanded with directions.

 

495 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Orr v. Edgar


Nos. 1-98-1485, 1-98-1508


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


298 Ill. App. 3d 432; 698 N.E.2d 560; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 484; 232 Ill. Dec. 469



July 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Francis Barth, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, county clerk and voters, challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded summary judgment for defendants, governor and state board of elections, in plaintiffs' challenge to the constitutionality of Pub. Act 89-700 (Act), which abolished "one-punch" straight-party voting in Illinois. Plaintiffs claimed the Act violated the State Mandates Act, 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. 805/1 et seq. (West 1994).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, county clerk and voters, filed their complaints for injunctive and declaratory relief and alleged that Pub. Act 89-700 (Act), which abolished "one-punch" straight-party voting in Illinois, was unconstitutional and violated the State Mandates Act, 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. 805/1 et seq. (West 1994). Defendants, governor and state board of elections, claimed that the statute did not infringe upon the right to vote. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the legislation did not infringe upon the right to vote but only affected the manner in which citizens exercised their right to vote. The court ruled that the Act was rationally related to a legitimate government interest. The court held that the Act needed no supermajority for its passage in the legislature and that the governor's signature was timely. The court relied on the enrolled bill doctrine and rejected plaintiffs' argument that the legislature did not follow its own rules. The court held that the Act did not violate the State Mandates Act. The court determined that plaintiff clerk was without standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court held that the challenged legislation regulated only the manner in which the citizens exercised their right to vote and represented legislation that was rationally related to a legitimate government interest. The court affirmed the order of the trial court that awarded summary judgment to defendants, governor and board of elections, in the action for declaratory and injunctive relief filed by plaintiffs, county clerk and voters.

Northern Ill. Home Builders Ass'n v. City of St. Charles


No. 2-97-0847


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


297 Ill. App. 3d 730; 697 N.E.2d 442; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 454; 231 Ill. Dec. 888


May 7, 1998, Submitted  
July 6, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 29, 1998. Released for Publication July 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 92--MR--0013. Honorable R. Peter Grometer and Timothy Q. Sheldon, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) granted summary judgment in favor of the defendant city and against plaintiff builders in their action for a declaratory judgment that the city's ordinances, St. Charles, Ill. Municipal Code § 13.08.150 (1990) and § 13.08.135 (1992), which mandated electric service connection fees, were unconstitutional and invalid. The builders appealed.


OVERVIEW: A city operated its own electric utility system and through its ordinances, charged new customers fees for connecting the electric service. A group of builders contended that the fees were unconstitutional and invalid because 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. §§ 11-119-1 and 11-119-3 prohibited the city from charging connection fees to their electric utility systems. The city argued that the builders did not have standing to challenge the ordinances because they sold the homes they built and passed the costs of connection on to the homeowners. The court held that (1) the builders had standing to challenge the constitutionality and validity of the ordinances because the city failed to establish that the builders recouped the connection fees, (2) the city had the authority to enact the ordinances because the legislature granted the power to the city to own and operate an electric service and charge reasonable fees for its operation and maintenance, (3) §§ 11-119-1 and 11-119-3 did not prohibit the city from charging the fees because the issuance of bonds was not the only way to raise money to pay for improvements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the builders' complaint as it related to the old ordinance, but affirmed the dismissal of the counts that related to the new ordinance. The case was remanded for a disposition on the merits of the builders' challenge to the old ordinance.

HILLARD v. BAGNOLA


No. 1-96-1807 & 1-97-0094 (Consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


297 Ill. App. 3d 906; 698 N.E.2d 170; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 431; 232 Ill. Dec. 332; 14 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 331



June 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 6, 1998. Released for Publication August 14, 1998. The Name of this Case has been Corrected May 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edwin W. Berman & Lester D. Foreman, Judges Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed appellee police board's decision to discharge him.


OVERVIEW: The trial court affirmed appellant police board's decision to discharge appellant police officer. The court affirmed that order on appeal. The court found that an applicable version of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-107 (1997) did not require the joinder of individual board members to provide subject matter jurisdiction. The court also held that appellant was in the best position to judge the credibility of each parties' experts and that its ruling in that regard was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court further determined that appellant failed to cite to any relevant authority that held that the inadvertent loss of his urine samples amounted to an unconstitutional denial of due process and that there was no evidence that the specimens were intentionally destroyed or tampered with. The court also concluded that not obtaining a warrant before requiring appellant to take a drug test because his status as a police officer placed him into a "special needs" exception and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 10-1-18.1 (1991) did not require notice before conducting the test because precedent held that it was not an examination under that statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that affirmed appellant police board's decision to discharge appellant police officer. The court found that joining individual board members was not required for jurisdiction, that no relevant authority showed that losing appellant's urine samples was a due process violation, and that a warrant was not needed for his drug test because his job placed him into a "special needs" exception.

People v. M.P. (In re M.P.)


No. 1-96-3307


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


297 Ill. App. 3d 972; 697 N.E.2d 1153; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 444; 232 Ill. Dec. 223



June 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 14, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Christopher J. Donnelly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in proceedings pursuant to the Juvenile Court Act of 1987 (Act), 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-1 et seq. (1992), requiring that he remove tattoos from his arms.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a minor, was found following a bench trial to be delinquent based upon the charge of criminal trespass to a vehicle. The trial court sentenced defendant to one year probation and 100 hours of community service. It also ordered that as part of his probation that the defendant remove tattoos on his arms which symbolized an alliance to a street gang. Defendant appealed the order arguing that the trial court abused its discretion and that it was an intrusive and illegal condition of probation not prescribed by the Act. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment from the trial court. The court held that while the trial court is afforded a great deal of discretion in issuing conditions of probation, ordering tattoo removal was not a reasonable measure of rehabilitation for defendant and was therefore an abuse of that discretion. The court held that forcing defendant to remove his tattoos may actually hamper the intended rehabilitative goal of the court because it may be considered a humiliating, not to mention painful, procedure for the young defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted him of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a pro se motion for appointment of counsel other than the public defender who had been representing him but the motion was denied. On review, appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to appoint other counsel to represent him with respect to his posttrial allegation that his attorney suborned perjury and in failing to sufficiently examine the factual basis for appellant's other pro se posttrial claims. The court affirmed and found that the trial court had the discretion to determine that appellant's posttrial and post-sentencing allegations, made for the purpose of obtaining new counsel, were frivolous and were intended to delay the effective administrative of justice. The court also found that, because the matters complained of clearly lacked merit or simply involved questions of trial strategy, the trial judge did not err in failing to appoint new counsel to represent appellant. The court determined that the trial court was also not in error when it refused to grant appellant a second fitness hearing because appellant had failed to establish that he was entitled to such a hearing.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for first-degree murder was affirmed.

If, on remand, the court determined that defendant was fit to stand trial, his conviction was to be affirmed.

LaSalle Nat'l Bank, N.A. v. City of Lake Forest


No. 2-97-0535


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


297 Ill. App. 3d 36; 696 N.E.2d 1222; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 395; 231 Ill. Dec. 651


February 3, 1998, Submitted  
June 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 94--CH--12. Honorable Peter M. Trobe, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trustee and defendant city sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which declined to enjoin the city from imposing a covenant on future subdivisions or resubdivisions of property and any other property owned or hereafter acquired by any of the trustees or their heirs, beneficiaries, administrators, executors, and successors.


OVERVIEW: The trustee drew up a resubdivision of property in which two lots with single-family residences would remain essentially the same, and a third lot would be resubdivided into eight new lots. After the city's planning and development staff reviewed these documents, it was recommended that the final approval of the resubdivision of the property be subject to a condition that the trustee be required to place a covenant on the third lot that would prohibit the further subdivision. The trial court granted the trustee's motions for summary judgment and held that the issue of the covenant on further resubdivision of the third lot was moot. At the time that the trial court ruled on the motion for summary judgment, the final plat of resubdivision had been approved without a covenant not to resubdivide. Without the imposition of such a covenant, there was no longer a controversy before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal as moot.

People v. Chatman


No. 2-97-0672


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


297 Ill. App. 3d 57; 696 N.E.2d 1159; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 344; 231 Ill. Dec. 588



June 1, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 24, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 95--CF--2250. Honorable Judith M. Brawka, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed the indictment against defendant for possession of cocaine in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/402(c) (1994) on the grounds that the state could only prove that she had cocaine in her system so any conviction would have unconstitutionally punished her for being a drug user rather than for a wrongful act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with three counts of possession of cocaine in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/402(c) (1994). The state admitted that it could only prove that defendant had cocaine in her system. The trial court held the statute unconstitutional as applied because it would have cruelly and unusually punished defendant for being a drug user rather than for committing a wrongful act, and dismissed the indictment. The state appealed, contending that the dismissal was unauthorized by the statute and amounted to an improper pretrial adjudication of the sufficiency of the evidence. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that the trial court exceeded its authority in dismissing the indictment because the refusal to dismiss would not have effected a deprivation of due process or resulted in a miscarriage of justice. Due process required only that there be some evidence against defendant, it did not require the dismissal of a charge that could not be proved. The court noted that defendant did not lack recourse against a poorly founded prosecution: she could demand speedy trial under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/103--5 (1996).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the state's indictment of defendant for possession of cocaine, and remanded for trial.

Chicago Teachers Union v. Illinois Educ. Labor Rels. Bd.


No. 1-96-3551


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


296 Ill. App. 3d 785; 695 N.E.2d 1332; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 335; 231 Ill. Dec. 213



May 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Illinois Educational Labor Relations Board. Nos. 96 UC 0004 C, 96 RC 0006 C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, teachers union and assistant principals functional group, appealed from an order of respondent Illinois Educational Labor Relations Board (IELRB), which affirmed the administrative law judge's decision that found that assistant principals were managerial employees who were ineligible for membership in the teachers union and that dismissed petitioners' complaint.


OVERVIEW: The union's petitions sought to have the union declared the collective bargaining representative for assistant principals employed by respondent board of education (board). The administrative law judge (ALJ) dismissed the petitions and found that assistant principals were managerial employees, who were ineligible for membership in the teachers' union, based on the IELRB's interpretations of § 2(o) of the Educational Labor Relations Act, 115 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2(o) (1996). The IELRB affirmed the ALJ's recommended decision, and on appeal, the court affirmed the IELRB's decision. Section 2(b) of the Educational Labor Relations Act, 115 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2(b) (1996) excluded managerial employees from the definition of "educational employees," and assistant principals were managerial employees as defined by § 2(o) of the act, 115 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2(o) (1996). Assistant principals were responsible for directing the board's policies and practices and their professional interests could not be separated from those of their principals. Those assistant principals who taught full-time with no managerial functions were not managerial employees and could be represented by the union.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the IELRB, which adopted the ALJ's decision that assistant principals were managerial employees who could not be represented by the union.

Collection Prof'ls v. Logan


No. 4-97-0842


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


296 Ill. App. 3d 959; 695 N.E.2d 1344; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 337; 231 Ill. Dec. 225


March 10, 1998, Submitted  
May 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 10th Judicial Circuit Putnam County, Illinois. No. 96--LM--5. Honorable Robert J. Cashen, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee collection agency garnished appellant judgment-debtor's bank account. The Circuit Court for the 10th Judicial Circuit Putnam County (Illinois), issued an opinion which permitted execution of the nonwage garnishment. The judgment-debtor appealed contending that an agreed order executed by the collection agency constituted an accord and satisfaction of the entire judgment and precluded the garnishment of his accounts.


OVERVIEW: The collection agency sued the judgment-debtor and his wife to collect various outstanding medical bills incurred during their marriage. When the couple divorced the wife agreed she would assume responsibility for paying the bills. The collection agency obtained a judgment against the judgment-debtor by default and began non-wage garnishment proceedings against him. The judgment-debtor filed objections and a motion to quash contending that the collection agency's agreement with his ex-wife was an accord and satisfaction and the non-wage garnishment statute was unconstitutional because it failed to provide him with pre-seizure notice. The trial court found for the collection agency. On appeal, the court held that (1) where neither the judgment debtor nor his wife disputed the amount of the debt and the claim was certain and evidence of consideration and mutual intent to compromise was lacking, the facts did not support an accord and satisfaction, (2) there was no executory accord or compromise of the claim, and (3) it was not a violation of the judgment-debtor's due process rights to provide him with an opportunity to defend against the garnishment after his assets had been seized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court permitting the execution of a non-wage garnishment by the collection agency.

Stahl v. Village of Hoffman Estates


No. 1-97-3145


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


296 Ill. App. 3d 550; 694 N.E.2d 1102; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 303; 230 Ill. Dec. 824



May 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE DOROTHY KINNAIRD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their action against appellees, village and director. The property owners' challenged Village of Hoffman Estates, Ill., Ordinance 1884-1987 (Sept. 21, 1987) (amended 1993) under the Commerce, Privileges and Immunities, Due Process, and Equal Protection Clauses, the right to travel, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed an action against the village and director that requested legal and equitable relief from the village's enforcement and collection of a real estate transfer tax under the Village of Hoffman Estates, Ill., Ordinance 1884-1987 (Sept. 21, 1987) (amended 1993), on the grounds that the ordinance violated the Commerce, Privileges and Immunities, Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses, the right to travel, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2. The village filed a motion to dismiss the action pursuant to Section 2-615 of the Civil Practice Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-615(a) (1992). The trial court granted the motion to dismiss. The property owners appealed. The court held that: (1) the tax exemption provided by the ordinance did not violate the Commerce Clause because it served a legitimate local purpose; (2) the transfer tax was not violative of the Privileges and Immunities Clause because it applied equally to nonresidents and residents; (3) the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim was not applicable to the action; and (4) the transfer tax did not violate the right to travel, the right to uniformity, the Equal Protection Clause, or the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the property owners' action against the village and director that challenged the village's ordinance under the Commerce, Privileges and Immunities, Due Process, and Equal Protection Clauses, the right to travel, § 1983, and the Illinois Constitution was affirmed.

People v. Aaron


No. 2-96-0864


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


296 Ill. App. 3d 317; 694 N.E.2d 1093; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 300; 230 Ill. Dec. 815



May 11, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 12, 1998. Rehearing Denied June 15, 1998. Released for Publication June 15, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 94--CF--1890. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, reversed in part, and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which denied her motion to quash a search warrant, convicted her of unlawful possession of a controlled substance under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/402(c) (1994)), and acquitted her of armed violence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33A-2 (1994), and criminal fortification of a residence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/19-5 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on various criminal charges after the police executed a no-knock warrant pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/108-8(b)(4) (1992). The trial court denied defendant's motion to quash the warrant and convicted her of unlawful possession of a controlled substance. The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to quash. The no-knock warrant was issued based on existent circumstances, which were defined by § 5/108-8(b)(4) as wooden planking or other impediments to entry into the premises. Although § 5/108-8(b)(4) did not violate the federal constitution, it did violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 6's reasonableness requirement. Exigent circumstances did not exist based solely on the fortification of a dwelling with a barricade blocking the doors. Rather, evidence of an intent to prevent police access, to destroy evidence, or that a knock and announce would have been futile was required. The exclusionary rule of Ill. Const. art. I § 6 protected defendant from a search warrant executed pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. Good faith did not excuse the unreasonable search. Thus, the denial of defendant's motion to quash the warrant was improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to quash the search warrant and the trial court's acquittal of defendant of armed violence and criminal fortification. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial on the unlawful possession of a controlled substance charge.
