Van Breemen v. Department of Prof'l Regulation


No. 3-97-0414


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


296 Ill. App. 3d 363; 694 N.E.2d 688; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 287; 230 Ill. Dec. 719


January 20, 1998, Submitted  
May 6, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 96--MR--868. Honorable Robert E. Byrne, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff expert appealed the decision entered in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which affirmed the order of defendant, Department of Professional Regulation (Illinois) directing the expert to cease and desist the unlicensed practice of professional engineering in violation of 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 325/39 and 40. The expert contended that the order was void and should be vacated.


OVERVIEW: The department solicited a brochure from the expert, which advertised his services as an expert witness. The department's found that the expert was not licensed to practice as a professional engineer in the state, as indicated in his resume and a letter he sent to the department. The court concluded that the findings were adequate. The expert's cover letter and resume cited his experience in engineering, and he clearly held himself out as able to perform many services recognized as professional engineering practices, especially forensic engineering. The state had a legitimate interest in regulating the practice of professional engineering, which had been determined to affect public health, safety, and welfare, and the order issued pursuant to the Professional Engineering Practice Act of 1989, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 325/39 was in proportion to the state's interest. Anyone reading the expert's literature would be misled to believe that he was a licensed professional engineer. Therefore, the order was not an unconstitutional prohibition of protected speech, and was not vague in its prohibition of the use of the title engineer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in favor of the department.

People v. Douglas


NO. 4-97-0582


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


296 Ill. App. 3d 192; 694 N.E.2d 665; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 278; 230 Ill. Dec. 696


April 8, 1998, Submitted  
May 4, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 94CF783. Honorable John G. Townsend, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated child battery. He contended that because the trial court failed to rule upon his original post-conviction petition within 90 days of its filing, the trial court lacked authority to dismiss the petition under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-2.1 of the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: After pleading guilty to aggravated battery of a child, defendant was sentenced to 25 years in prison as a Class X offender pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (1992) of the Unified Code of Corrections. In an earlier action, his appeal was affirmed. Defendant filed a pro se petition for postconviction relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (1996), but amended the petition a month later, asserting that he had been subjected to double sentence enhancement, and alleging ineffective assistance of counsel. The trial court dismissed the petition as frivolous, and defendant appealed, claiming that the trial court lacked authority to dismiss by failing to timely rule. The court affirmed the dismissal, holding that, in order to give the trial court the full time the legislature deemed necessary for the trial court to consider the petitions under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-2.1, defendant's filing of the amended petition started the 90-day period review period anew, not only for the later-filed petition, but for the earlier petition, as well. The court examined defendant's claims and agreed that they were frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of defendant's post-conviction petition because the trial court had 90 days in which to examine defendant's petition, including the originally-filed petition, starting from the time of defendant's filing of the amended petition.

People v. Gooden


NO. 5-96-0746


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


296 Ill. App. 3d 205; 694 N.E.2d 215; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 274; 230 Ill. Dec. 584



April 30, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Washington County. No. 95-CF-74. Honorable Lloyd A. Karmeier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence by the Circuit Court of Washington County (Illinois) for home invasion and aggravated criminal sexual assault. He argued that his statutory right to a speedy trial, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/103-5 (1996), on the aggravated criminal sexual assault charge was violated; that his sentence was void because Ill. Public Act 89-404 (Act) was unconstitutional; and that his sentences of 12 years were excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with home invasion after he forced his way into his ex-wife's home and sexually assaulted her. His motion for a continuance to seek funds to hire an expert witness was granted. The state filed an amended information, adding charges of aggravated criminal sexual assault. Defendant's motion to dismiss the added counts was denied. He was convicted of home invasion and aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced to 12 years. Affirming the conviction and sentences, the court held that defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated. The sexual assault offense, known to the state at the time of the original prosecution and arising from the same set of facts, was subject to the speedy-trial limits that applied to the home invasion charge. However, the continuance was attributable to defendant and could not be used to justify dismissal of the sexual assault charge on the basis that 120 days had elapsed since he was arrested. The court ruled that defendant could not challenge in a direct appeal the constitutionality of the Act codifying the truth-in-sentencing laws because the application of those laws was outside the scope of the sentencing proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for home invasion and aggravated criminal sexual assault and his sentences of imprisonment for 12 years.

Meusel v. Ballard


No. 2-97-0884, No. 2-97-0711


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


296 Ill. App. 3d 377; 694 N.E.2d 610; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 266; 230 Ill. Dec. 641


February 11, 1998, Submitted  
April 24, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 12, 1998. Released for Publication June 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit Whiteside County, Illinois. No. 94--L--138, No. 95--L--109. Honorable Daniel A. Dunagan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Answered and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a municipal hospital and various physicians, challenged an order by the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit Whiteside County, Illinois, which denied their motions for summary judgment against plaintiff patients in medical malpractice actions that were consolidated on interlocutory appeal. The lower court issued a certified question in each case regarding which statute of limitations was applicable to the actions.


OVERVIEW: In separate cases, patients filed a medical malpractice action against a municipal hospital and various physicians more than one year, but less than two years, after the accrual of their respective causes of action. In a consolidated interlocutory appeal by the hospital and physicians from the trial court's denial of their motions for summary judgment, which alleged that the actions were filed beyond the one-year statute of limitations under 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/8-101, the court answered a certified question regarding which statute of limitations applied. The court held that the two-year statute of limitation set forth in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212(a) was applicable to medical malpractice cases brought against municipal hospitals rather than the one-year statute of limitation of 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/8-101 of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question and remanded for further proceedings.

Parker v. American Family Ins. Co.


NO. 3-97-0534


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


296 Ill. App. 3d 110; 694 N.E.2d 211; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 263; 230 Ill. Dec. 580


November 4, 1997, Submitted  
April 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 21, 1998. Released for Publication May 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 18th Judicial Circuit, DuPage County, Illinois. No. 97--L--574. Honorable Hollis Webster Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of the 18th Judicial Circuit, DuPage County (Illinois) confirmed an arbitration award in favor of plaintiff insured even though the award was in excess of the minimum liability set forth in the Illinois Safety and Family Financial Responsibility Law (Act), 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-100 et seq. (1996). Defendant insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insured was injured in a motor vehicle accident due to the negligence of an underinsured motorist (UIM). The insured settled his claim with the UIM for the policy limits of $ 20,000 and then filed for arbitration with his insurer as permitted by the arbitration provisions for UIM in his insurance policy. The arbitration provisions provided that if the award exceeded the minimum limits of the Act, then each party was entitled to a de novo trial on all issues. The arbitrator awarded the insured an amount in excess of the minimum under the Act but the trial court confirmed the award anyway, finding that the arbitration clause was one of adhesion, which violated public policy. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding the fact that both parties were bound to a low award, which the insurer was unlikely to appeal, but not bound by a high award, demonstrated that the clause only favored the insurer and was, thus, unconscionable. Therefore, the clause was unenforceable and the award was properly confirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the confirmation of the arbitration award in the insured's favor.

 

512 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Partin v. St. Francis Hosp.


No. 1-96-0270


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


296 Ill. App. 3d 220; 694 N.E.2d 574; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 243; 230 Ill. Dec. 605



April 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable JULIA M. NOWICKI, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed plaintiff's medical malpractice complaint against defendant health care providers and entered judgment in favor of defendants, on the basis that the complaint was time-barred by 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/13-212(b).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured party was born with severe brain and central nervous system damage at defendant hospital. Nineteen years later, plaintiff filed a medical malpractice complaint against defendant health care providers. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's complaint with prejudice and entered judgment for defendants, on the basis that the action was time-barred under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/13-212(b). On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that the statute bore a rational relationship to a legitimate government interest. The time limit selected was not arbitrary or unreasonable and there was a rational basis for different treatment of children subject to the dual disability of age and mental incompetence. Thus, under the rational basis test, the statute did not violate due process or equal protection. Ill. Const. art. I, § 12 did not apply to a statute that merely restricted the time for suit; thus plaintiff's right of access was not destroyed. Finally, the statute did not violate the constitutional ban on special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing plaintiff injured party's medical malpractice against defendant health care providers on the basis that it was time-barred. The statute of limitations did not violate plaintiff's right to due process, equal protection, or access to the courts, and it was not special legislation.

C.J. v. Department of Mental Health & Developmental Disabilities


No. 1-96-4142


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


296 Ill. App. 3d 17; 693 N.E.2d 1209; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 214; 230 Ill. Dec. 458



April 6, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CO 80. Honorable James F. Henry, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff criminal acquitees appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant department of mental health's motion to dismiss plaintiffs' claims for injunctive relief as the director of the mental health center where plaintiffs were confined was not permitted to recommend plaintiffs for unsupervised, on-grounds passes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, criminal acquitees, who were found not guilty by reason of insanity, sought injunctive relief against defendant mental health center and sought to permit the facility director to exercise professional judgment in determining whether plaintiffs could be recommended for unsupervised, on-grounds passes. The lower court granted defendant's motion to dismiss and the court reversed in part. The court found that dismissal of most of plaintiffs' allegations was proper as the Code of Corrections overruled the Mental Health Code when the two statutes conflicted. The court concluded that the U.S. Const. amend XIV due process clause allowed restriction on the freedom of bodily movement of involuntarily committed mental patients only pursuant to a professional judgment that restrictions are necessary for security or treatment reasons. The court remanded the matter for trial as there was a question of fact as to what constituted an unsupervised on-grounds pass so that it could be determined whether defendant violated the constitutional prohibition on freedom of movement.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court erred in dismissing plaintiff criminal acquitees' complaint on two of the counts as the court found that the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend XIV allows restriction on the freedom of bodily movement of involuntarily committed mental patients only pursuant to professional judgment that restrictions were necessary for treatment or security.

This Opinion Substituted for Withdrawn Opinion of May 2, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 239.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) convicting him of unlawful possession of less than 200 grams of a substance containing methamphetamine in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/402(c) (1992) and driving while his driver's license was revoked (DWR) in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-303(a) (1992). Defendant was sentenced to imprisonment and ordered to reimburse his appointed counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of less than 200 grams of a substance containing methamphetamine, and driving while his driver's license was revoked. After a jury trial, defendant was convicted and sentenced to consecutive terms of imprisonment. Defendant was also ordered to pay reimbursement for his appointed attorney. Defendant's motion to set aside the convictions was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of unlawful possession of less than 200 grams of a substance containing methamphetamine and driving while his driver's license was revoked. The court vacated the trial court's order directing defendant to pay reimbursement for his appointed counsel, and remanded the case for a hearing to determine defendant's ability to pay reimbursement.

People v. Tellez-Valencia


No. 2-97-0853


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


295 Ill. App. 3d 122; 692 N.E.2d 407; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 164; 229 Ill. Dec. 634



March 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 17, 1998. Released for Publication April 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 96--CF--2024. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois)of two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child in violation of Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12 - 14.1. He appealed and sought a summary reversal of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois Supreme Court found that the statute under which the defendant was convicted violated the Illinois Constitution. The defendant sought summary reversal of his convictions, claiming that the offense he was charged with, convicted of, and sentenced for did not exist at the time the offense allegedly occurred. The state argued that the court should deny the defendant any relief because the reenacting law should be applied retroactively. The court determined that when the supreme court invalidated the statute under which the defendant was convicted, the law became void ab initio and it was as if the law never existed. Because the reenacting law created new substantive law and became effective after the defendant was alleged to have committed the offense, it could not be applied retroactively to the defendant in this case. As a result, the defendant's conviction was invalid. The court further held, however, that since the law was void ab initio, the defendant did not have a claim of double jeopardy and the state could charge him with any other applicable offense that was in effect on the dates of the alleged acts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Wilson


NO. 5-97-0182


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


295 Ill. App. 3d 228; 692 N.E.2d 422; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 169; 229 Ill. Dec. 649


January 28, 1998, Oral Argument Held, Submitted  
March 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 20, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 96CF174. Honorable Jerry L. Patton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of first degree murder in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(a)(1) (Supp. 1995), appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea and applied the truth-in-sentencing provisions of § 3-6-3 of the Unified Code of Corrections, as codified at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3 (1994), as amended by Public Act 89-404, 1995 Ill. Laws 4306, 4323-27.


OVERVIEW: Three days after defendant's initial guilty plea hearing, the court reconvened the hearing to clarify its admonishment regarding the effect of his previous sentence on this new sentence. At the second hearing, defendant sought to withdraw his guilty plea, but the trial court refused to do so. The trial court also denied his motion to vacate the guilty plea. The trial court applied the amended truth-in-sentencing provisions, which no longer permitted day-for-day good time credit. The court held that the trial court did not err by denying defendant's request to withdraw his guilty plea at the second hearing and the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying the motion to withdraw the guilty plea. The court found defendant's plea to be knowing and voluntary and determined that the trial court's admonitions substantially complied with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402, 134 Ill. 2d R. 402. However, the court found that Public Act 89-404 violated the single subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) (1970) and thus its amendments to the truth-in-sentencing provisions were invalid. Defendant was therefore entitled to day-for-day good time credit under the unamended statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded the matter with directions that the trial court amend the sentencing order to reflect that defendant's eligibility for day-for-day good-time credit.

Northwest Airlines v. Department of Revenue


No. 1-96-4267


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


295 Ill. App. 3d 889; 692 N.E.2d 1264; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 149; 230 Ill. Dec. 98



March 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 93 L 50535. The Honorable Randye A. Kogan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Illinois Department of Revenue (department), challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held in favor of appellee taxpayers. The circuit court concluded that flyover miles were not properly included in the numerator of the apportionment fraction applicable to transportation services set forth in section 304(d) of the Illinois Income Tax Act, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/304(d) (1996).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers timely protested the department's tax adjustment based on its inclusion of flyover miles. The taxpayers argued that flyover miles were not in Illinois, but rather were in federal air space. The circuit court found that a nexus was required between overflights and the state of Illinois. The court affirmed the judgment and held that it was erroneous to conclude that flyover miles were excluded simply on the basis of an "in" versus "over" analysis. The court held that a nexus was required with the Illinois transaction by which the tax was measured. There had to be a sufficient connection with the flyover miles generated by the overflights. The court held that the record amply demonstrated that the nexus requirement could not be satisfied. There was a total absence of any nexus between the overflights and the state of Illinois.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that held in favor of the taxpayers and found that flyover miles were not properly included in the numerator of the apportionment fraction applicable to transportation services. The court held that a nexus was required with the Illinois transaction by which the department measured the tax.

Appeal denied by People v. Moore, 183 Ill. 2d 586, 712 N.E.2d 822, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 345, 238 Ill. Dec. 718 (1999)
Reversed by People v. Tellez-Valencia, 188 Ill. 2d 523, 723 N.E.2d 223, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 1473, 243 Ill. Dec. 191 (1999)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which sentenced him to 20 years in prison on each of three counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child and seven years in prison for aggravated criminal sexual abuse, with sentences to be served consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that mere touching of a victim's sex organ was not sufficient to prove predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. The court maintained that testimony of child witnesses was sufficient to prove defendant guilty of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and that the state was not required to provide corroboration for the testimony. The state contended that the court should simply change the name of the offense from predatory criminal sexual assault of a child to aggravated criminal sexual assault under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14. The court agreed finding that its focus was on the conduct defendant was convicted of engaging in rather than the section number of the statute that described that conduct. Therefore, the court granted the state's request to change the designation of defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

People v. Reedy


No. 2-96-0101


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


295 Ill. App. 3d 34; 692 N.E.2d 376; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 126; 229 Ill. Dec. 603


December 9, 1997, Submitted  
March 11, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 95-CF-2160. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) which sentenced him according to the "truth-in-sentencing" provisions of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3--6--3(a)(2)(ii) (1996) of the Unified Code of Corrections, under which he was eligible to receive no more than four and one half days of good conduct credit per month of his sentence, claiming that § 3--6--3(a)(2)(ii) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to 15 years in prison. Under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 6/3--6--3(a)(2)(ii) he was eligible to receive no more than four and one half days of good conduct credit per month of his sentence. He contended that § 6/3--6--3(a)(2)(ii) was unconstitutional insofar as it violated the single subject rule of the Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d). On appeal, the court held that the legislative enactment, Mich. Pub. Acts 89--404, that instituted § 6/3--6--3(a)(2)(ii) was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule, and held that defendant was entitled to the good conduct credit that he would have been eligible to receive prior to Mich. Pub. Acts 89--404's enactment. The court held that defendant could challenge the constitutionality of § 6/3--6--3(a)(2)(ii) on direct appeal because it had legal effect on the sentencing hearing and by its own terms it was not outside the scope of the sentencing proceedings. Mich. Pub. Acts 89--404 violated the single subject rule because it addressed five distinct subjects and amended nine different statutory codes, and there was no "natural and logical connection" uniting its various subjects.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as modified as to defendant's sentence under the "truth-in-sentencing" provisions of the Unified Code of Corrections.

Teachers Ins. & Annuity Ass'n of Am. v. La Salle Nat'l Bank


Nos. 2-96-1423, 2-97-1115, 2-97-1116, 3-97-0299 consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


295 Ill. App. 3d 61; 691 N.E.2d 881; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 121; 229 Ill. Dec. 408


February 3, 1998, Submitted

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 2, 1998. Released for Publication April 2, 1998.
Certiorari Denied February 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1139.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 95-CH-0829. Honorable John W. Darrah, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagor and others appealed from orders of the De Page County Circuit Court (Illinois) granting summary judgment to plaintiff mortgagee in plaintiff's foreclosure action, which appeals were consolidated. Summary judgment was granted to plaintiff, striking defendants' answers and affirmative defenses and on defendants' counterclaims. Plaintiff filed a motion to dismiss three of the four consolidated appeals.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mortgagee filed an action in the trial court against defendant mortgagor and others to foreclose a mortgage. The trial court granted summary judgments in favor of plaintiff on defendants' counterclaim and striking defendants' twice-filed answer and affirmative defenses. The court entered a judgment of foreclosure and sale. Defendants appealed the summary judgment orders and two other orders, which appeals were consolidated. Plaintiff filed a motion to dismiss three of the four consolidated appeals, which the court denied. Addressing only the appeals from the summary judgment orders, the court affirmed, holding that the Credit Agreements Act (Act), 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 160/0.01 et seq. (1996), barred defendants' affirmative defenses and counterclaims because such were actions as contemplated therein; that applying the Act did not violated defendants' equal protection rights and was not unconstitutional special legislation; that defendants failed to plead sufficient facts to show a breached fiduciary duty; and that defendants arguments regarding a duty of good faith and fair dealing and the single subject rule were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiff mortgagee's motion to dismiss three of the appeals and affirmed summary judgment for plaintiff on the counterclaims and affirmative defenses of defendant mortgagor and others, holding that the Credit Agreements Act barred the same. The court did not address defendants' appeals from other orders of the trial court, which were consolidated with these appeals.

People v. Nakajima


No. 4-97-0584


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


294 Ill. App. 3d 809; 691 N.E.2d 153; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 79; 229 Ill. Dec. 217


January 27, 1998, Oral Argument Held, Submitted  
February 19, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 19, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 95CF1107. Honorable Michael G. Prall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted him of stalking pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.3 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of stalking the victim pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.3 (West 1994). The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that a culpability requirement was to be read into 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.3(a)(2). The court held that the stalking legislation was constitutional. The court construed the stalking statute to require two separate instances where the victim was placed in reasonable apprehension of bodily harm, sexual assault, confinement, or restraint. The court concluded that the evidence adequately supported finding that the victim was placed in reasonable apprehension of bodily harm as a result of defendant's persistent and unwelcome conduct. The court held that the trial judge was not required to accept defendant's version of events and that defendant's knowledge could be inferred from the facts and circumstances of the case. The court found that defendant was explicitly told of the victim's concerns, ordered to stay away from her and her family, and sent a letter from the state's attorney's office detailing the effect of his actions on the victim and advising that he would be prosecuted if such conduct continued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of stalking. The court held that defendant had the requisite knowledge to be convicted of the crime.

West v. West


NO. 5-97-0108


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


294 Ill. App. 3d 356; 689 N.E.2d 1215; 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 46; 228 Ill. Dec. 794



January 27, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. No. 93-F-92. Honorable Terry H. Gamber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois), which granted visitation of her child to respondent grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents' son, who had been married to the mother, was the father of the child. The mother sought to end the visitation and argued that the grandparental visitation statute, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b) (1996), violated her fundamental parental liberty rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. 1, § 2. The reviewing court disagreed. The state had a wide range of power for limiting parental freedom and authority in things affecting the child's welfare. In assessing the best interest of the child in matters of visitation, appropriate matters to consider were: (1) the nature and length of the child's relationship with persons seeking visitation and (2) the effect of visitation on the emotional and psychological well-being of the child. The state had a compelling interest in maintaining and safeguarding an established grandparent-grandchild relationship where it has been proven that it is in the child's best interest. The statute was narrowly tailored and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Yap v. Zollar


No. 1-96-0141


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


294 Ill. App. 3d 71; 691 N.E.2d 18; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 917; 229 Ill. Dec. 82



December 31, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edwin M. Berman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Professional Regulation appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reversed the department's decision to deny plaintiff nurse licensure by endorsement as a professional registered nurse.


OVERVIEW: The department denied the nurse's application for licensure by endorsement as a professional registered nurse because she failed to meet the requirement of § 15 of the Illinois Nursing Act of 1987 (Act), 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 65/15 (1993), which required an applicant to pass the certifying exam within three years of the applicant's first attempt. At the time of the nurse's first attempt to pass the exam, the requirement was merely that the applicant pass the test within six attempts over an unlimited period of time. The trial court reversed the denial, and the court affirmed. The court held that the amendment to the statute could not be applied retroactively. To have denied the nurse's license by endorsement would have deprived her of a vested right because she reasonably relied on the former statute. Because the amendment significantly changed the time limit required to pass the exam, the change was substantive. The court held that the nurse was not on notice that she was required to pass the exam within three years of her first attempt after the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that reversed the department's decision to deny the nurse licensure by endorsement as a professional registered nurse.

People v. Reynolds


No. 1-95-3383


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


294 Ill. App. 3d 58; 689 N.E.2d 335; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 916; 228 Ill. Dec. 463



December 31, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 94 CR 23498. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant politician appealed the order from the trial court (Illinois), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of criminal sexual abuse, criminal sexual assault, child pornography, and obstruction of justice. Defendant contends he did not violate 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-13(a)(4) and that the judge erred in allowing general verdict forms for the separate counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant met a 16-year-old girl and had sex with her 2 to 3 times a week until she was 17 years old. Defendant gave her money almost every time they were together, arranged for her to go to a private school, paid her tuition, and arranged for her to volunteer on his political campaign. Defendant was convicted on, among other charges, criminal sexual assault under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-13(a)(4). On appeal, he contended that there was no evidence that he held a "position of trust, authority, or supervision" in relation to the girl, as required by § 12-13(a)(4). The court held that defendant's role as a public official did not alone create a position of trust, authority, or supervision in relation to the girl, but found that the evidence showed that he developed such a position in relation to the girl. The court noted that the girl worked on defendant's campaign, he arranged for her to go to private school and paid the tuition, and he even described himself as her "mentor." The court also held that the general verdict form was proper for the separate counts because the state proceeded on a theory of an ongoing sexual relationship between the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order convicting defendant of criminal sexual assault and found that the trial court did not err in allowing general verdict forms for the separate counts.

Benchwarmers, Inc. v. Daley


No. 1-96-0445


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


294 Ill. App. 3d 385; 690 N.E.2d 622; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 910; 228 Ill. Dec. 863



December 31, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 6, 1998. Released for Publication February 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 95-CH-0918, 95-CH-1344. Honorable Edwin M. Berman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, mayor and local liquor control commissioner, challenged the reversal by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of the local liquor control commission's (LLCC) suspension of appellee café's liquor license for violating Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 4-60-140 (1990). The cafe and appellee president contested the trial court's ruling that the license appeal commission (LAC) did not have the authority to modify the LLCC's decision.


OVERVIEW: A minor working undercover for the Chicago police was admitted to the café, requested a beer, and was served. The hearing officer determined that the defense of entrapment was inapplicable to the administrative proceeding and further found that there had been no entrapment. The LAC reduced the LLCC's five-day suspension of the cafe's liquor license for selling alcoholic liquor to a minor to a one-day suspension. The trial court found that the cafe had been entrapped and reversed the suspension entirely. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the LAC lacked authority to modify the LLCC's decision because the plain language of 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-5 (1992) enumerated the LAC's review powers to include sustaining or reversing an LLCC decision but not modifying a decision. Reversing the suspension judgment, the court ruled that the trial court erred in finding blatant entrapment. As evidentiary decisions were within the hearing officer's discretion, the entrapment defense was available when governmental misconduct was egregious. The hearing officer reasonably could determine that there was no evidence demonstrating that the cafe was induced to serve the minor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the trial court's judgment that held that the café's liquor license was wrongly suspended and affirmed that portion of the judgment that ruled that the LAC lacked authority to modify a decision rendered by the LLCC.

Archer Daniels Midland Co. v. City of Chicago


No. 1-96-3861


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


294 Ill. App. 3d 186; 689 N.E.2d 392; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 909; 228 Ill. Dec. 520



December 31, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ALEXANDER P. WHITE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, gas consumers, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County, which dismissed the consumers' action against defendant city. The consumers contended that the Chicago Gas Use Tax Ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 3-41-030(A) (1994), which imposed a tax on the use of natural gas purchased at retail, was an invalid occupational tax under the provisions of Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e).


OVERVIEW: The city entered into a contract with the gas company to collect taxes imposed under the ordinance. The consumers purchased natural gas at retail outside of Illinois for use in their businesses in the city. The gas was then delivered by pipeline to the gas company. According to the consumers, once their gas was in the pipeline, it was fungible and indistinguishable from gas being transported to gas company customers who purchased their gas in the city. The consumers contended that the ordinance was an unconstitutional occupation tax because it had not been authorized by the general assembly. The city countered that a tax could not be an occupation tax within the meaning of § 6(e) unless it was imposed on businesses engaged in the occupation of selling the commodities taxed. Instead, the city argued that the ordinance was a tax on tangible personal property. The court agreed and affirmed, holding that natural gas was a tangible personal property, and that the tax was on the consumer, not the provider of the gas. Because the tax was placed on the consumer, it was valid under § 6(e), and could not be construed as an unconstitutional service occupation tax upon a public utility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court denying reconsideration of its dismissal of the consumers' complaint against the city.

Turner v. Nama


No. 1-96-3317


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


294 Ill. App. 3d 19; 689 N.E.2d 303; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 921; 228 Ill. Dec. 431



December 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 1998. As Corrected February 25, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph Casciato, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the circuit court of Cook County affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedent's estate sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed plaintiffs' malpractice action against defendant doctor that was filed after defendant allegedly failed to notify decedent of test results. The action was dismissed on the ground that it had not been filed within the statute of repose under § 13-212(a) of the Limitations Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212(a) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff decedent's estate filed a malpractice action against defendant doctor, alleging defendant had failed to notify decedent of test results. Thereafter, the action was dismissed on the ground that it had not been filed within the statute of repose under § 13-212(a) of the Limitations Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-212(a) (1996). Accordingly, review was sought, and the court affirmed. After rejecting the contention that § 13-212(a) was unconstitutional, the court held defendant had not fraudulently concealed the decedent's cause of action, thus tolling § 13-212(a), because defendant's statements had not tended to conceal the cause of action, the decedent should have discovered the concealment through ordinary diligence, and reasonable time would have remained within the repose period upon discovery. In addition, the court held the ongoing course of continuous negligent medical treatment doctrine was inapplicable because defendant's failure to notify had not been an ongoing course of continuous negligent medical treatment. Finally, the court held the decedent's disability had not affected § 13-212(a) because the disability had occurred after the cause of action's accrual.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed a judgment dismissing a malpractice action brought by plaintiff decedent's estate against defendant doctor after defendant allegedly failed to notify decedent of test results because the statute of repose was not tolled by defendant's alleged fraudulent concealment, the ongoing course of continuous negligent medical treatment doctrine was inapplicable, and decedent's disability had not shortened the statute of repose.

Kavanagh v. County of Will


No. 3-97-0292


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 880; 689 N.E.2d 299; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 920; 228 Ill. Dec. 427



December 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit. Will County, Illinois. No. 96-MR-13498, No. 96-MR-13637, No. 96-MR-13638, No. 96-MR-13639. Honorable William R. Penn, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit (Illinois), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, attorneys who worked as lobbyists in the county (lobbyists). The county's declaratory judgment action, seeking to uphold the Will County, Ill., Lobbyist Registration Ordinance (June 1996), was dismissed because the ordinance violated the State Lobbyist Registration Act.


OVERVIEW: The State Lobbyist Registration Act, 25 Ill. Comp. Stat. 170/1 et seq. (1996), granted counties the power to enact lobbying ordinances that were required to be "similar," but not identical, to those imposed by the Act. The Will County, Ill., Lobbyist Registration Ordinance (June 1996) was challenged by a group of county attorneys, who worked as lobbyists. When the county filed an action for declaratory relief, the circuit court found that the county had exceeded its powers in enacting such an ordinance and granted the lobbyists' motion to dismiss. On the county's appeal, the court found substantial differences between the Act and the ordinance, which was much more intrusive than the requirements of the Act. The court affirmed the circuit court's decision and held that many of the ordinance's requirements were ultra vires and void. After the objectionable language had been excised, however, the court found that the remaining language was not void for vagueness merely because it did not contain definitions. Finally, the court disagreed with the lobbyists' contention that the ordinance could not regulate their activities because they were also lawyers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which dismissed the county's action for declaratory relief. The court held that some of the requirements of the ordinance exceeded the power delegated to the county in the state act and were void. Those parts of the ordinance in compliance with the statute were not void for vagueness, however, and the ordinance's regulation of the lobbyists, who were also attorneys, was not unconstitutional.

Aich-Sindino v. Department of Children & Family Servs. (In re A.S.B.)


No. 2-97-0305


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 836; 688 N.E.2d 1215; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 897; 228 Ill. Dec. 238


December 2, 1997, Submitted  
December 29, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. Nos. 95--J--93. 96--AD--72. Honorable Thomas E. Mueller, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner putative father appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted a motion of respondent, the Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS), to strike the putative father's petition for leave to intervene in the adoption proceeding.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of the adoption of the putative father's alleged child, the court held that DCFS used due diligence in trying to notify the putative father that it was seeking to terminate his parental rights because it made significant efforts to find the mother and published a notification. The putative father's parental rights were properly terminated because he had not shown an interest in the child. Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(1) (1994). The order of adoption was properly granted even after the trial court was aware of the putative father's identity because his rights were terminated. The putative father's constitutional right to equal protection was not violated by the Adoption Act because the definition of "unfit person" was reasonably related to a legitimate governmental interest. The putative father's equal protection rights were not violated by the Putative Father Registry because the registry was substantially related to important state interests in locating putative fathers. The putative father could not intervene because he was statutorily barred from bringing any action to assert any interest in the child because he failed to register with the Putative Father Registry.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

People v. Zamudio


No. 1-95-1246


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 976; 689 N.E.2d 254; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 883; 228 Ill. Dec. 382



December 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 CR 9690. Honorable James Schreier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of stalking in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-7.3(a) (1976). Defendant alleged that the statute applied to innocent conduct in violation of due process was unconstitutionally overbroad, was unconstitutionally vague because the term "follows" was not defined, and the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant followed the victim, a former friend, on three occasions. On one occasion, defendant parked his car so as to block the victims and banged on the victim's car window threatening to kill him. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that 5/12-7.3(a) punished assault, not innocent conduct. The court reasoned that the statute required proof of following and a threat that are a part of a course of conduct, not merely following. The court held that the stalking statute did not violate the Due Process Clauses of U.S. Const., amend XIV and Ill. Const., art I § 2 (1970), because its use of the terms "following" and "surveillance" were sufficiently definite to put the average person on notice as to what constituted a violation. Additionally, the court found that the requirement of two separate incidents accompanied by threat or assault were sufficient to inhibit arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement based on subjective standards. Because a rational jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant followed the victim without lawful justification and placed him in apprehension, the court held that there was sufficient evidence to convict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for stalking.

People v. Gallegos


No. 3-97-0247


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 873; 689 N.E.2d 223; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 885; 228 Ill. Dec. 351


November 5, 1997, Submitted  
December 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 3, 1998. Released for Publication February 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 18th Judicial Circuit, Du Page County, Illinois. No. 95--DT--4670. Honorable Kenneth W. Torluemke, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11--501 (1994) in the Circuit Court for the 18th Judicial Circuit, Du Page County (Illinois). On appeal, he contended that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1--6 (Supp. 1995), which provided that the state was no longer required to prove venue at trial, was unconstitutional and that his conviction had to be reversed.


OVERVIEW: The state asserted that the 1995 amendment to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1--6 (Supp. 1995) removed venue as an element of a criminal offense and that all objections to place of trial were waived unless raised prior to trial. Defendant argued that the amendment was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine. The trial court denied defendant's motion for directed verdict, finding that although the state had failed to prove venue beyond a reasonable doubt, it was not required to do so. The court concluded that the substantive element of venue was rooted in the common law and therefore it was unnecessary to address defendant's contention that the statute was invalid because of its failure to ensure defendant's knowing and intentional waiver of a constitutional right. Although venue was no longer an element of the offense, the county in which the crime was alleged to have taken place still had to be set forth in the charging instrument in order to confer jurisdiction on the trial court in a county, and an action filed in the wrong county remained subject to a motion to dismiss pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/114--1(a)(7) (1996).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that venue was not a constitutional requirement of proof in a criminal case of drunk driving, but one of the common law abrogated by legislative enactment.

People v. Kilpatrick


No. 3-96-0991


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 446; 688 N.E.2d 1202; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 873; 228 Ill. Dec. 225



December 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Knox County, Illinois. No. 95--CF--193. Honorable Harry C. Bulkeley, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Knox County, Illinois, entered on his guilty plea to attempted first degree murder and aggravated battery. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to conduct a fitness hearing as required by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. ILCS 5/104-21(a) (1994) prior to his guilty plea, despite evidence that he was taking psychotropic drugs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly stabbed two individuals and fought with a police officer; and pleaded guilty to attempted murder and aggravated battery. On appeal, defendant argued that he was statutorily entitled to a fitness hearing at the time of his plea because he was taking psychotropic drugs, and that the trial court's failure to conduct a fitness hearing required a new trial. The court held that: 1) the amendment to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. ILCS 5/104--21(a) (1994), which avoided the hearing requirement, was not retroactively applied because it was substantive and not procedural; 2) defendant was entitled to a fitness hearing pursuant to the original psychotropic drug statute; 3) although defendant was entitled to a fitness hearing, the remedy for the trial court's failure to conduct such was not necessarily a new trial; and 4) remand for a limited, retrospective fitness hearing was the proper remedy.


OUTCOME: On an appeal of the trial court's entering of defendant's guilty plea, the court remanded the case to the trial court for a limited hearing to determine defendant's fitness to stand trial.

 

537 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


City of Chicago v. Boulevard Bank Nat'l Ass'n


No. 1-96-2799


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 767; 688 N.E.2d 844; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 862; 228 Ill. Dec. 146



December 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 17, 1997. Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joanne L. Lanigan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied defendants' traverse and motion to dismiss a motion of plaintiff city's complaint for condemnation with respect to the quick take of defendants' building as part of a redevelopment financed under the Illinois Tax and Increment Allocation Redevelopment Act, 65 Ill. Cons. Stat. 5/11-74.4-1 et seq. (1994).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city filed an eminent domain action to acquire defendant property owner's property, and requested a "quick take" hearing pursuant to 735 Ill. Cons. Stat. 5/7-103(1994). Defendants filed an amended traverse and motion to dismiss. The court affirmed a denial of defendants' traverse and motion. The condemnation of defendants' property was consistent with and did not change the general land use or the nature of the redevelopment project as provided in the redevelopment plan as amended by subsequent ordinances. Defendants failed to show that the trial court's determination that plaintiff's acquisition of defendant's property was necessary and in conformance with the Illinois Tax and Increment Allocation Redevelopment Act, 65 Ill. Cons. Stat. 5/11-74.4-1 et seq. (1994), was contrary to the weight of the evidence. Ordinances establishing and amending the redevelopment plan were not vague or uncertain that an adjacent building was at risk of condemnation, justifying condemnation of defendants' property. The "quick take" statute was rationally based on plaintiff's greater population density than elsewhere in Illinois and was not unconstitutional special legislation.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant property owners' traverse and motion to dismiss a motion of plaintiff city's complaint for condemnation with respect to the quick take of defendants' building as part of a redevelopment financed under the Illinois Tax and Increment Allocation Redevelopment Act was affirmed.

People v. Watford


No. 3-96-0315


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


294 Ill. App. 3d 462; 690 N.E.2d 1009; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 826; 228 Ill. Dec. 934



December 12, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 25, 1998. Released for Publication February 25, 1998. As Modified Upon Denial of Petition for Rehearing February 25, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 95-CF-556. Honorable Gordon L. Lustfeldt, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted first-degree murder, aggravated battery with a firearm, and unlawful use of a weapon. The Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois) sentenced him to 10 years imprisonment for attempted first degree murder, and a concurrent three year term for the unlawful use of a weapon. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced. At his sentencing proceeding, the trial judge informed the public that defendant would have had to serve 85 percent of the sentence imposed because of truth-in-sentencing. The defendant argued on appeal that the Truth-in-Sentencing Act was unconstitutional and thus his sentence was void. The court held that defendant could not have challenged the constitutionality of the act that provided for truth-in-sentencing law in a direct appeal of his sentence because the application of those laws was outside the scope of the sentencing proceedings. The court further that the statement by the trial judge at sentencing had no legal effect on defendant's actual release and could not have been relief upon by defendant upon appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision.

 

539 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Palumbo Bros. v. Wagner


No. 1-95-4090


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 756; 688 N.E.2d 837; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 861; 228 Ill. Dec. 139



December 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE EARL ARKISS, ALEXANDER P. WHITE, JUDGES PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the dismissal of his complaint against defendant director of the state tax department by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The taxpayer argued that he was denied due process when the director assessed taxes due and attempted to collect them. He asserted that he had no liability to the director and that the director did not have a valid lien against his individual assets or those of the joint venture.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a member of a joint venture with a separate Illinois corporation. The director assigned the joint venture an Illinois Business Tax number that was different from the taxpayer's own. After an audit, the director issued to the taxpayer and to the joint venture notices of tax liability, including penalties and interest. The director placed tax liens on all property owned by the taxpayer. The taxpayer filed suit. The trial court granted the director's motion to dismiss. The taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that the taxpayer was not denied due process in either the assessment or the collection of taxes. Due process did not require that the taxpayer be given personal notice of the assessments on the joint venture. The joint venture was treated as a partnership, and under the Uniform Partnership Act such personal notice to the taxpayer was not required. The taxpayer was not denied due process by the department's liens on his property. A tax assessment was not a judgment under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 120/5, so appeal should have been taken to the director prior to suit. Also, relief from tax liability was by injunction not through declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the director's motion to dismiss the complaint for declaration brought by the taxpayer. The taxpayer's due process rights were not violated by either the assessment or the collection of taxes against him and against the joint venture. Notice to the joint venture was sufficient. The lien on the taxpayer's property was not a judgment, so appeal should have been taken to the director prior to suit.

Bachmann v. Kent


No. 1-96-0369


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 1078; 689 N.E.2d 171; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 859; 228 Ill. Dec. 299



December 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1998. Released for Publication February 10, 1998. Petition for Leave to Appeal Withdrawn March 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1927.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 94 M6 6531. The Honorable Edwin J. Richardson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a complaint against defendant alleging she was injured in a traffic accident as a result of defendant's negligence. An arbitration award was entered in favor of plaintiff. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) struck defendant's notice of rejection of the arbitration award and entered judgment for plaintiff. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the trial court properly struck defendant's rejection of the arbitration award. The court found that the trial court's debarring of defendant's rejection of the arbitration award was not an abuse of discretion because it had authority to do so under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 90(g), 145 Ill.2d R. 90(g), after defendant failed to appear at the arbitration hearing even though plaintiff served defendant with an Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 237 notice to appear. 166 Ill.2d R. 237. It was also not an abuse of discretion to strike defendant's notice of rejection because the notice was signed by a non-attorney in violation of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 137, 134 Ill.2d R. 137. The court found that the trial court's sanction was not excessive. The court held that the striking of the arbitration award was not in violation of Ill. Const. art. I, § 13 (1970) or the enabling act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1004A (1994). .


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order striking defendant's notice of rejection of the arbitration award in favor of plaintiff.

County of Cook v. Village of Rosemont


No. 1-97-2472


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 713; 688 N.E.2d 1192; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 852; 228 Ill. Dec. 215



December 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE LESTER BONAGURO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County, which denied appellee county's petition for preliminary injunction but which held that a village ordinance regarding an amusement tax was unconstitutional and enjoined the village from enforcing its ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The village enacted an ordinance whereby it declined to collect an amusement tax that was required pursuant to a county ordinance. The village enacted the ordinance to create a conflict with the county ordinance so that the village ordinance would prevail. The county filed suit seeking to compel the village to collect the tax and filed a petition seeking a preliminary injunction. The court denied the petition but found the ordinance unconstitutional. On appeal, the court vacated the trial court's order finding the village ordinance unconstitutional and granting a temporary injunction. In so doing, the court found that the court abused its discretion in finding the village ordinance unconstitutional because that issue was not before the trial court, nor was a constitutional determination necessary to the decision on the county's petition for a preliminary injunction that was before the court. The court further found that the order enjoining the village from enforcing its ordinance was a permanent injunction and should not have been ordered without a hearing on the matter.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order finding the village ordinance unconstitutional and granting a temporary injunction barring its enforcement. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

542 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


First Midwest v. Pogge


NO. 4-97-0393


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 359; 687 N.E.2d 1195; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 840; 227 Ill. Dec. 713


October 22, 1997, Oral Argument Held, SUBMITTED  
December 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 90CH62. Honorable Robert J. Eggers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by appellant lender against appellee bankruptcy trustee, and on cross motions, the lender appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to the bankruptcy trustee. The lender argued that the doctrine of lis pendens did not apply to its foreclosure action and that the bankruptcy trustee was estopped from contesting the lender's rights under the mortgage.


OVERVIEW: A wife filed a marital dissolution action. At the time, she and her husband jointly owned a house. They also owed money to the lender. Both the wife and her husband informed the lender of the dissolution. The lender loaned the husband more money. The marriage was dissolved, and the wife was awarded the house. The husband was ordered to assume the loans. The lender began to a foreclosure action on the house. Both the wife and her husband filed for bankruptcy. The husband was discharged in bankruptcy, and the bankruptcy trustee for the wife was substituted as a party. The trial court granted summary judgment to the bankruptcy trustee. The lender appealed. The court reversed and remanded and held that the bankruptcy trustee was estopped from contesting the loans that should have been litigated in the dissolution proceeding. The doctrine of lis pendens was inapplicable and did not prevent the encumbrance during the dissolution action. Equitable estoppel did not apply because the lender had actual notice of the pending divorce and was not a bona fide purchaser. The lender was bound to the judgment rendered in the underlying dissolution action as if it had been a party to that action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the grant of summary judgment to the bankruptcy trustee in a foreclosure action.

People v. Brownlee


NO. 4-96-0444


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 315; 687 N.E.2d 1174; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 841; 227 Ill. Dec. 692


April 25, 1997, SUBMITTED  
December 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 19, 1997. Released for Publication January 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 95CF1336. Honorable Harold L. Jensen, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the court's judgment, which reversed the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized during a vehicle search. The Illinois Supreme Court denied defendant's petition for leave to appeal, but vacated the court's judgment and remanded with directions for the court to consider defendant's argument regarding Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 (1970).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the passenger in a vehicle that was stopped for a minor traffic violation. After the officers decided not to issue any tickets, they asked to search the vehicle. The driver agreed. The officers discovered marijuana during the vehicle search, and they arrested all of the vehicle's occupants. A search of defendant's purse revealed the cocaine, and defendant was charged with possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the seized evidence. On appeal, the court reversed and held that: (1) the Fourth Amendment did not require a police officer to tell a stopped motorist that they were free to leave before the officer could ask the motorist to search the vehicle; (2) Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 (1970) provided no more protection to motorists than the Fourth Amendment; and (3) the consensual search of the vehicle did not violate defendant's Fourth Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the suppression order issued by the trial court and held that the evidence seized from defendant was admissible in her trial for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance.

People v. Karich


No. 2-95-1568


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 135; 687 N.E.2d 1169; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 821; 227 Ill. Dec. 687


October 27, 1997, Submitted  
December 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing December 29, 1997. Released for Publication December 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 95--DV--0726. Honorable Hollis L. Webster, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of violating an order of protection under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12--30(a)(1) for calling his ex-wife 6 to 12 times in one evening.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with telephone harassment and violating an order of protection after calling his ex-wife 6 to 12 times in an evening. The state argued the number of calls was per se proof that defendant was intending to harass the ex-wife. Defendant was acquitted of telephone harassment, but convicted of violating the order of protection. On appeal, defendant claimed that he was trying to talk to his children with the phone calls, but the ex-wife hung up without defendant being able to ask for his children, which was why he continued to call. The court found that there was no proof entered concerning the content of the calls. Without knowing the content of the calls, no rational trier of fact could have found defendant's purpose in making the calls was not reasonable under the circumstances, which was a required element of proof under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/103(7). Thus, the state failed to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for violating a protective order.

People v. Laughlin


No. 2-97-0125


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


293 Ill. App. 3d 194; 687 N.E.2d 1162; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 824; 227 Ill. Dec. 680



December 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 2, 1998. Released for Publication January 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 95--CF--918. Honorable Conrad F. Floeter and Ward S. Arnold, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which convicted him of indecent liberties with a child, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 11--4(a)(2) and 4(a)(3) (1979), and official misconduct, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33--3(b), for acts committed in the late 1970s. Defendant, who had lived in Nebraska since 1979, contended that the tolling provision of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3--7 (1996) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a high school teacher in Illinois in the late 1970s. In June 1979 he resigned his position and moved to Nebraska, where he remained. He was charged in 1995 with having sexual contact with three underage boys between August 1977 and June 1979. The trial court convicted him of two counts of indecent liberties with a child, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 11--4(a)(2) and 4(a)(3) (1979), and one count of official misconduct, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33--3(b) (1979). On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the tolling provision, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3--7 (1996), arguing that it created an impermissible distinction between Illinois residents and nonresidents in violation of the Equal Protection Clause under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. Finding no impingement of a fundamental constitutional right, the court concluded that the difficulty in investigating and bringing nonresidents to justice provided a rational basis for the classification created by the tolling provision. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, holding that the tolling provision did not violate his equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: Upholding the constitutionality of the tolling provision, the court affirmed defendant's convictions for indecent liberties with a child and official misconduct.

People v. Carlson


No. 1-96-0557


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 984; 691 N.E.2d 1156; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 815; 229 Ill. Dec. 433



November 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 27, 1998. Released for Publication February 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 94-CR-8731. THE HONORABLE JOHN J. MORAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of forgery and theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction of forgery and theft. On appeal, the court did not reverse the convictions but instead remanded the case for a determination of whether defendant was entitled to a competency hearing and for a factual investigation of defendant's use of psychotropic medication. The court found that the trial court was informed that defendant was taking psychotropic medication at a pretrial continuance, at defendant's appeal bond hearing, in defendant's physician's letter attached to the resentencing investigation report, and in defendant's statement during the sentencing hearing. The court ruled that this was sufficient to put the court on notice of the issue of defendant's competency. The court also found that the record lacked reliable evidence showing that defendant's receipt of lithium occurred during or near the time of the proceedings, and the record failed to show in what manner the drug may have influenced defendant's mental faculties, temperament, and behavior in the courtroom. Thus, the court ruled that a limited remand was necessary to make a factual determination of defendant's use of psychotropic drugs during the critical stages of the litigation.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case and directed the trial court to ascertain whether defendant was entitled to a competency hearing and to conduct a thorough factual investigation with respect to the circumstances surrounding defendant's use of psychotropic medication.
