McCullough v. Knight


No. 1-96-0775


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 591; 688 N.E.2d 1186; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 819; 228 Ill. Dec. 209



November 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 9, 1998. Released for Publication January 22, 1998. Petition for Rehearing Dismissed for Lack of Appellate Jurisdiction February 27, 1998. As Corrected March 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 CH 11220. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee challenged a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld a decision of appellee, department of revenue. The department had imposed a fine against the arrestee for an unregistered firearm recovered from his vehicle during an arrest. The arrestee's argument that because the firearm had been suppressed at his criminal trial that it should have been suppressed in the administrative hearing was rejected.


OVERVIEW: An arrestee brought suit to recover a fine imposed by the department for an unregistered firearm recovered from his vehicle during an arrest. The arrestee argued that the search of the vehicle violated U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970). A trial court affirmed the decision of the department and the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that despite its broad deterrent purpose, the exclusionary rule had never been interpreted to proscribe the use of illegally seized evidence in all proceedings or against all persons. The court found that the exclusionary rule did not apply to the case as advocated by the arrestee. The court found that in examining the costs of applying the exclusionary rule, the department would have been unable to consider valuable and relevant evidence that would have impeded the truth-finding function of the hearing officer, as was usually the case when the exclusionary rule was employed. The court ruled that the result would have interfered with the public policy behind the administrative proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that affirmed the decision of the department that imposed a fine upon the arrestee for an unregistered firearm recovered from his vehicle during an arrest.

People v. Van Brocklin

People v. Gibson


NO. 5-96-0716


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


292 Ill. App. 3d 842; 687 N.E.2d 1076; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 775; 227 Ill. Dec. 594



November 4, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rule 23 Order Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published November 4, 1997. Rehearing Denied November 4, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 774.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 95-CF-1623. Honorable Edward C. Ferguson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for attempted first-degree murder and the sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) on the ground that he was not fit to enter an Alford plea pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-21(a) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an Alford plea to the charge of attempted first-degree murder at the time he was taking sinequan, a psychotropic drug. The version of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-21(a) (1995) in effect at the time of his sentencing was found to be unconstitutional. Defendant argued that the previous version of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-21(a) (1994) governed his sentencing and required that he be granted a new trial because he was taking a psychotropic drug when he was sentenced. Section 104-21(a) was amended during the pendency of defendant's appeal following the declaration that it was unconstitutional, and the amended statute, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-21(a) (1996), stated that there was no presumption that a person was unfit to stand trial merely because that person was taking psychotropic drugs. The court held that the amended § 104-21(a) was procedural and could be applied to defendant's sentencing. Therefore, the matter was remanded to the lower court with directions to examine whether the sinequan had compromised defendant's ability to plead. On the remand, there was to be no presumption that the sinequan made defendant unfit to plead.


OUTCOME: The court applied the fitness statute as it had been amended during the pendency of defendant's appeal and remanded the matter to the lower court for a determination of whether the psychotropic drug taken by defendant had compromised his ability to plead.

Ardt v. State


No. 1-96-2064


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


292 Ill. App. 3d 1059; 687 N.E.2d 126; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 750; 227 Ill. Dec. 203



October 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 5, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ELLIS REID, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dentist sought attorney's fees incurred in successfully invalidating regulations of defendant Department of Professional Regulation under the provisions of 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 100/10-55(c) (1992). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) awarded attorney's fees in the full amount requested by the dentist. The Department of Professional Regulation asserted that the court should not have awarded the full amount requested.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff dentist was sanctioned by defendant Department of Professional Regulation for various advertising slogans. The dentist challenged the regulations and the sanction imposed and was successful in invalidating some of the regulations. The dentist then sought to recover attorney's fees incurred under the provisions of 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 100/10-55(c) (1992). The trial court awarded attorney's fees in the full amount requested by the dentist. The court affirmed the award of attorney's fees for the invalidation because it concluded that the action that went to the Illinois Supreme Court invalidated at least one administrative rule, and under 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 100/10-55(c) (1992) the dentist was entitled to reasonable fees incurred in the entire action culminating in the supreme court's decision. The court reversed and remanded the matter for an analysis of reasonableness of the fee because the trial court had accepted the invoice for the attorney's fees after it determined that there was entitlement to the fee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination that plaintiff dentist was entitled to fees incurred throughout the administrative action that resulted in the invalidation of the regulation against defendant Department of Professional Regulation but reversed and remanded the award of fees in the amount of $ 58,881 with instructions that the trial court conduct a more thorough reasonableness analysis because no analysis of the fee was made at trial.

In re Adopt O.J.M.


No. 1-96-2742


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


293 Ill. App. 3d 49; 687 N.E.2d 113; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 766; 227 Ill. Dec. 190



October 29, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 5, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE JAMES HENRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that entered an order of adoption in favor of appellee adoptive parents and dismissed appellant's parentage petition by reason of his failure to comply with the provisions of the Adoption Act regarding the timely registration with the Putative Father Registry, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/12.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant putative challenged the circuit court's dismissal of his petition to determine parentage by reason of his failure to comply with Adoption Act provisions requiring timely registration with the Putative Father Registry, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/12.1. Appellant claimed that his failure to register should have been excused because of the biological mother's misrepresentation concerning the identity of the child's father. Appellant also argued that he was denied equal protection because he was treated differently from fathers whose parental rights were regulated by the Illinois Juvenile Court Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1-1 et seq. The court held that because appellant failed to timely register and did not allege facts that would bring him within the exceptions to section 12.1(g) of the Adoption Act, he was barred from maintaining his parentage petition, which was properly dismissed. The court also held that a putative father who, like appellant, did not register and initiate paternity proceedings was not entitled to section 2-30 notice under the Juvenile Court Act; and the purported difference in the notice requirements of the two Acts argued by appellant did not exist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court judgment that dismissed appellant putative father's parentage petition because appellant failed to register with the Putative Father Registry as required by the Adoption Act, and thus, was not entitled to notice or opportunity to be heard in the adoption proceedings. The court also held that the birth mother's misrepresentation regarding the child's father did not excuse appellant's obligation to register.

 

552 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jamerson


No. 3-96-1020


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


292 Ill. App. 3d 944; 687 N.E.2d 329; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 742; 227 Ill. Dec. 255


May 20, 1997, Submitted  
October 23, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 16, 1997. Released for Publication December 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Knox County, Illinois, No. 95--CF--208. Honorable James B. Stewart, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction entered in the Circuit Court, Knox County (Illinois) following a bench trial, where she was found guilty but mentally ill of three counts of forgery and sentenced to a four-year prison term. She contended that the trial court failed to conduct a fitness hearing despite evidence she was taking psychotropic drugs under medical direction, and that her sentence was excessive given the mitigating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant knowingly delivered forged checks drawn on a bank that was not then in business. She testified that due to her mental state at the time of the offense, her ability to understand the criminality of her conduct was questionable. A licensed psychiatrist was called in rebuttal, and testified that she appeared coherent and was not delusional or acting oddly, and he did not believe that she lacked the ability to appreciate the criminality of her conduct at the time of the offense. The applicable statute was amended twice since the offense. The question presented was whether the Second Amendment was procedural and could be applied retroactively, or whether the original statute governed. In light of the importance the legislature placed on the right of an accused taking psychotropic medication to receive a fitness hearing under the original statute, the court found that the second amended statute effectuated a substantive change in the law and could not be applied retroactively, as it would deprive the defendant of the accrued right to a mandatory fitness hearing. Automatic reversal was not the appropriate remedy, as the facts were suitable for a case-specific fitness hearing.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the convictions with directions for a limited fitness hearing to determine defendant's fitness to stand trial.

 

553 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Slayton v. Strappe (In re Slayton)


NO. 4-97-0240


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


292 Ill. App. 3d 379; 685 N.E.2d 1038; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 710; 226 Ill. Dec. 583


August 20, 1997, Oral Argument Held, Submitted  
October 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 8, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Peoria County. Nos. 91D109, 91F253. Honorable Joe R. Vespa, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and father, were the minor child's biological parents. However, the child was born while the mother was married to appellee first husband. The Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) granted the first husband visitation with the child. The mother and father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father contended that because the first husband was not the child's biological father, he should not have been granted visitation absent a compelling reason why he should have been permitted to interfere with their constitutionally protected parental rights. The mother and father further contended that the trial court erred in finding that permanent visitation was in the child's best interests. The court held that § 607(a) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(a), governed the first husband's visitation rights and that the first husband was entitled to reasonable visitation. The court found that it was clear that the visitation did not endanger the child's physical, mental, moral, or emotional health. The mother and father did not raise their constitutional claim until the close of the custody hearing. At that time, they did not identify what constitutional provision afforded them protection against visitation; therefore, they waived the argument that a standard for nonbiological parents other that § 607(a) was constitutionally compelled.


OUTCOME: The order that granted the first husband visitation rights with the minor child was affirmed.

People v. Perry


No. 1-96-0037


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION

September 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 26, 1997.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Perry, 179 Ill. 2d 607, 702 N.E.2d 527, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 947, 234 Ill. Dec. 187 (1998)
Vacated by, Cause remanded by People v. Perry, 303 Ill. App. 3d 138, 707 N.E.2d 589, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 942, 236 Ill. Dec. 462 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1998)
Subsequent appeal at People v. Perry, 307 Ill. App. 3d 552, 718 N.E.2d 677, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 646, 241 Ill. Dec. 106 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Perry, 329 Ill. App. 3d 1232, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 3975 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Cathey v. Cox, 203 F. Supp. 2d 949, 2002 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 9107 (N.D. Ill., 2002)
Subsequent appeal at People v. Perry, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 5117 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Themis N. Karnezis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and two counts of armed robbery in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). He was sentenced to life without parole for the murder and appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and two counts of armed robbery. During the trial, defendant requested a jury instruction on second degree murder and involuntary manslaughter. The trial court allowed the instruction on involuntary manslaughter. The court held that the trial court did not have to give a jury instruction on second degree murder based on defendant's testimony which revealed he was unwilling to participate in a struggle with the victim and acted in self defense. The court reasoned that self defense did not entitle defendant to a provocation instruction based on mutual combat and the state presented evidence that defendant intended to rob the store and instigated the combat. The court determined that defendant did not preserve the issue of the trial court's response o the jury's question because the defense counsel agreed to the trial court's response and the issue was not included in defendant's posttrial motion. The court held that defendant failed to overcome the presumption that the was fit to stand trial solely because he was taking medication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction an sentence and remanded back to the trial court for sentencing on the two counts of armed robbery.

People v. Placek


No. 1-95-4398


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


292 Ill. App. 3d 521; 685 N.E.2d 1002; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 685; 226 Ill. Dec. 547



September 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 93-CR-19851. Honorable Joseph J. Urso, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance and sentenced him to a term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: After an undercover officer informed defendant that his boss needed a cocaine supplier, defendant informed the officer that he could obtain cocaine. Defendant was arrested as he was weighing a controlled substance in preparation to deliver it to the officer. An initial conviction of defendant for delivering a controlled substance and for theft was set aside because the theft statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed defendant's conviction at a second trial on charges of delivering a controlled substance. The second trial was not barred by federal or state constitutional guarantees against double jeopardy because defendant, not the state, was responsible for joining the charge of delivery with the theft charge in the first trial. The trial court gave a limiting instruction regarding the relevance of evidence of other crimes and did not abuse its discretion in admitting that evidence to rebut defendant's defense of entrapment. By failing to object at trial defendant waived error as to the introduction of other evidence. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's rejection of defendant's entrapment defense because defendant was predisposed to commit the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

556 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Straub


NO. 4-96-0340


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


292 Ill. App. 3d 193; 685 N.E.2d 429; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 675; 226 Ill. Dec. 326


August 20, 1997, Submitted  
September 25, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County. No. 92CF368. Honorable Richard E. Scott, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois) which, without having conducted a hearing to determine defendant's fitness to stand trial, convicted defendant of second degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant's entire argument rested on the claim that his use of Valium made him unfit to stand trial. The trial court did not conduct a fitness hearing, and the court affirmed. The court noted that under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/104-10 (1994) a defendant was presumed to be fit to stand trial, plead, and be sentenced, but he could be found unfit to stand trial if he was unable to understand the nature and purpose of the proceedings against him or to assist in his defense. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by not conducting a fitness hearing because defendant never informed it he was taking Valium at the time of the trial. Defendant's own examining psychologist did not find him unfit to stand trial. The trial court took great pains to assure that defendant's medication was not affecting his ability to understand the proceedings and cooperate in his defense. Because the trial court had a duty to order a fitness hearing sua sponte if there was a bona fide doubt of defendant's fitness and since defendant demonstrated no entitlement to a fitness hearing, defendant was not prejudiced by the failure of defense counsel to request a fitness hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which convicted defendant of second degree murder.

Marsh v. Illinois Racing Bd.


No. 1-95-4265


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


292 Ill. App. 3d 468; 685 N.E.2d 977; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 671; 226 Ill. Dec. 522



September 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Albert Green, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a racing board, its individual members, and two stewards of a racetrack, sought review of an order of the circuit court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted an injunction in favor of plaintiff racehorse rider that restrained defendants from enforcing a revocation of the racehorse rider's license to own and drive standardbred racehorses.


OVERVIEW: The racehorse rider's license was revoked and he was declared ineligible for future licensing when the stewards found that he had furthered an unlawful betting scheme by failing to give his best effort in two races. The racehorse rider sought and received an injunction that restrained defendants from enforcing the revocation. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the racehorse rider was barred from seeking injunctive relief from the circuit court because he did not exhaust any of his administrative remedies. The court held that the third exception to the exhaustion of remedies doctrine, that irreparable harm would result from further pursuit of administrative remedies, did not call for an injunction preempting any attempt at resolving the matter administratively. Further, the court held that the hearing was to be held only five days after the racehorse rider filed his complaint, and that the loss of income and future business for a brief period pending administrative proceedings did not constitute irreparable harm. Accordingly, the court held that the racehorse rider prematurely filed his complaint and that the trial court erred in granting the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court, which had granted an injunction in favor of the racehorse rider.

City of Chicago v. Roman


1-96-1957


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


292 Ill. App. 3d 546; 685 N.E.2d 967; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 658; 226 Ill. Dec. 512



September 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT COOK COUNTY. No. 94 MC1 351250. THE HONORABLE, WILLIAM O'MALLEY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of the sentence that was imposed by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), pursuant to defendant's conviction of assault of a person age 60 years or over in violation of Chicago, Ill, Municipal Code § 8-4-080 (1990), which was less than the mandatory minimum sentence provided for in the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of assault, in violation of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 8-4-080 (1990), the trial court twice denied defendant's motion to declare that the ordinance was unconstitutional, but ruled that the mandatory minimum sentence exceeded the city's home rule authority. The city sought review. On appeal, the court held that Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 8-4-080 (1990) was properly within the city's home rule authority and that state law did not preempt the authority of the city to set a mandatory minimum penalty of imprisonment for violation of its ordinance. The court held that reversal of the trial court's sentence would not subject defendant to another trial or to additional punishment. The court held that the trial court erred in failing to follow the penalty provision of the city's ordinance. The court held that the city's choice to have a sentencing scheme that was different from the state's was well within the city's constitutional powers as a home rule unit. Therefore, the court reversed the sentence that was imposed by the trial court and remanded the matter for sentencing only.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's sentence of defendant for his conviction for assault and remanded with directions for resentencing only.

Woodstock Hunt Club v. Hindi


Nos. 2-96-1288, 2-96-1342, 2-96-1343 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


291 Ill. App. 3d 1051; 684 N.E.2d 1089; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 640; 226 Ill. Dec. 93


April 22, 1997, Submitted  
September 11, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 9, 1997. Released for Publication October 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 96--CH--375. Honorable James C. Franz, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, anti-hunting activists, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) which granted the request of plaintiffs, hunting club and members, for an injunction enjoining them from violating the Hunter Interference Prohibition Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 125/0.01 et seq. (1996), and convicted one defendant of indirect criminal contempt of court and sentenced him to 180 days in jail.


OVERVIEW: The hunting club sought to enjoin the activists from violating the Hunter Interference Prohibition Act (Act), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 125/0.01 et seq. (1996), by scaring game away from the club by using sirens, bull-horns, and an engine-powered glider. The club obtained a temporary restraining order (TRO) against such practices. The circuit court issued a permanent injunction against the activists prohibiting any conduct violating the Act, found one activist in indirect criminal contempt for violating the TRO, and sentenced him to 180 days in jail. On appeal, the court affirmed the injunction, the contempt conviction, and sentence. The court held that the Act was not overly broad or unconstitutional because its criminal prohibitions were content-neutral: it did not single out any particular thought or opinion for prohibition. Its legitimate sweep was clear: to prevent intentional disturbance during the dangerous time of the hunt when loaded weapons were legally carried. The court further held that the circuit court's failure to recite the words "beyond a reasonable doubt" did not require reversal of the conviction. Finally, the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the circuit court granting the hunting club's request for an injunction restraining the anti-hunting activists from violating the Hunter Interference Prohibition Act and convicting one of the activists of indirect criminal contempt of court and sentencing him to 180 days in jail.

 

560 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Eggerman


No. 1-96-3846


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


292 Ill. App. 3d 644; 685 N.E.2d 948; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 631; 226 Ill. Dec. 493



September 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CR 11515. Honorable Michael Bolan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by indictment in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) with aggravated vehicular hijacking, vehicular hijacking, armed robbery, and robbery. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss because he had previously entered a guilty plea to the charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle based on the same incident. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle was a lesser included offense of the offenses of robbery, armed robbery, vehicular hijacking, and aggravated vehicular hijacking and that the state was barred by the doctrine of double jeopardy from pursuing them. The court held that double jeopardy applied. The court found that prosecution of a lesser included offense prevented the subsequent prosecution of the greater offense, and that the Fifth Amendment double jeopardy clause forbid successive prosecution and cumulative punishment for a greater and lesser included offense. Possession of a stolen motor vehicle was a lesser included offense of the charges because the taking of a motor vehicle as required in the vehicular hijacking offenses included unauthorized possession and knowledge that the vehicle was stolen, and the specific intent offense of theft was a lesser included offense of the general intent offense of armed robbery despite the differing mental states. The same facts that would prove the possession of a stolen motor vehicle would prove the other offenses and that prevented the state from pursuing successive prosecutions for the greater offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying defendant's motion to dismiss was reversed.

Reed v. Farmers Ins. Group


No. 3-96-0739


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


291 Ill. App. 3d 1068; 685 N.E.2d 385; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 643; 226 Ill. Dec. 282


May 14, 1997, Submitted  
September 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois, No. 95--L--298. Honorable Donald C. Courson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois, which granted defendant insurer's motion to dismiss the insured's complaint seeking to have a clause in her insurance policy declared void, to declare 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/143(a) (1996) unconstitutional, and to recover damages for injuries allegedly suffered as a result of the negligent driving of an uninsured motorist.


OVERVIEW: The insured filed a compliant against her insurer seeking a declaration that a clause in her insurance contract was void as against public policy and that 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/143(a) (1996) was an impairment of the right to contract. The complaint also sought to recover damages for injuries allegedly suffered as a result of the negligent driving of an uninsured motorist. The insurer filed a motion to dismiss the insured's complaint. The trial court dismissed the complaint, and the insured appealed, contending that an arbitration clause in the policy allowed the insurer to bind the insured to a low arbitration award and permitted the insurer to unilaterally reject a high award. On appeal, the court reversed, remanded, and held that the insured's complaint was ripe for adjudication, that the involuntary nature of the arbitration clause coupled with its structural inequality rendered it unconscionable and unenforceable, and that 5/143(a) was violative of the right to contract. The means adopted by the legislature were not rationally related to its goal of placing the injured insured in the same position she would have occupied had the uninsured motorist been minimally insured.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the insured's complaint against the insurer and remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Kershner


Nos. 2-95-0670, 2-95-0710 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


291 Ill. App. 3d 1024; 684 N.E.2d 1049; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 621; 226 Ill. Dec. 53



September 9, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 94--CF--1198, 94--CF--1199. Honorable Ronald B. Mehling, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of 11 counts of failing to file a sales tax transaction reporting return and one count of filing a fraudulent sales tax return. The trial court rejected defendant's argument that the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act (act), 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 120/1 et seq. (1994), was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him.


OVERVIEW: The state presented numerous witnesses to show that defendant was the person in charge of a car dealership and that he did all the business paperwork. The corporate dealership was involuntarily dissolved and became a sole proprietorship. On appeal, the court held that (1) the act provided that when the amount due was $ 300 or more, any person engaged in the business of selling tangible personal property at retail in the state who failed to file a return, or who filed a fraudulent return, was guilty of a Class 3 felony; (2) the act was presumed to be constitutional; (3) the act was not void for vagueness because it clearly defined the proscribed conduct in words that a person of ordinary intelligence could understand and provided definite standards for enforcement; (4) even if the act was unclear on who exactly was a "responsible person" in general, the evidence in the instant case clearly established that defendant was the responsible person at the car dealership; (5) the act applied to sole proprietorships, although it did not specifically enumerate them; and (6) the act was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of multiple violations of the act.

People v. T.W. (In re T.W.)


No. 1-96-2705


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


291 Ill. App. 3d 955; 685 N.E.2d 631; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 584; 226 Ill. Dec. 376



August 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Stuart F. Lubin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent minor, adjudicated delinquent, appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), contending that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-15(b) was unconstitutionally vague and violated due process because it contained no minimum objective standards to determine which of two minors who engaged in consensual sex was the accused and which was the victim.


OVERVIEW: Finding that relations between the two minors were consensual, the minor was found delinquent on two counts of criminal sexual abuse, and the circuit court ordered the case closed, but indicated that its adjudication of delinquency was to stand. The minor appealed, alleging that the statute was unconstitutional, but the court found that the statute was sufficiently clear. Once the minor victim filed her complaint alleging that the minor subjected her to an offense prohibited by the statute, the legislative definitions of the terms "accused" and "victim" were sufficient objective standards to guide law enforcement officials for purposes of prosecution. There was a rational relationship between the age classification created by the statute and the purpose behind the statute. Thus, the court rejected the minor's vagueness challenge. Further, the statutory schemes were constitutional. Thus, the judgment of the circuit court's finding of delinquency as to the two counts of criminal sexual abuse was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Finding no constitutional deficiencies in the criminal sexual abuse statute, the court affirmed the minor's adjudication of delinquency.

Lincoln Towers Ins. Agency v. Boozell


No. 1-95-4139


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


291 Ill. App. 3d 965; 684 N.E.2d 900; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 594; 225 Ill. Dec. 909



August 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 22, 1997. As Corrected September 26, 1997. Released for Publication October 9, 1997. As Corrected October 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 93 CH 11373. Honorable Ellis E. Reid, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a class of producers for defendant insolvent insurer, filed an action, seeking, inter alia, a declaration of their right to set off claims against insolvent insurer for commissions against premiums that were due. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment, and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted producers' motion in part. Insolvent insurer appealed, and producers filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Producers solicited clients for insolvent insurers, collecting the premiums and holding them in trust for insolvent insurer. In granting summary judgment for producers, the trial court held that the Contract Clause of the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, governed the parties' relationship and superseded the liquidation order and that producers were entitled to deduct their earned commissions from the premiums that they held in trust for insolvent insurer. The court held that the trial court erred in finding that the Contract Clause governed the parties' relationship, as § 206 of the Illinois Insurance Code, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/206 (1996), was in existence at the time the contract was formed and, thus, became an implied provision of the contract. Insolvent insurer argued that § 206 precluded the set off of the earned premiums that had not been credited prior to liquidation because there was no longer mutuality between the parties. The court held that the set off was improper, as there was no mutuality between the parties because producers acted as fiduciaries by holding the collected premiums in trust for insolvent insurer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, remanding the case.

People v. Elizonda (In re Daniel R.)


No. 1-96-4186


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


291 Ill. App. 3d 1003; 684 N.E.2d 891; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 595; 225 Ill. Dec. 900



August 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 24, 1997. The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court September 29, 1997. Released for Publication October 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Lynne Kawamoto, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee parents' motion for substitution of judge as of right pursuant to Ill. Code Civ. P. 2-1001(a)(2), 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1001(a)(2) (1994).


OVERVIEW: A minor by public guardian appealed the grant of his parents' motion for substitution of judge by right in the state's neglect petition on behalf of the minor. The parents argued that they would not receive an impartial hearing because the mother's other children were already before the trial court. On appeal, the court affirmed the grant of the motion for substitution of judge by right. The court rejected the minor's argument that allowing substitution would result in two or more judges hearing the same case and possibly reaching different conclusions. The court found that no party in the appeal adequately addressed the rights of the man who took care of one of the parents' other children. The court also found that 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-10-(10) (1994) applied to the instant proceeding and did not support the minor's attempt to extend the definition of "a case" to encompass all "cases" related to the same family. The court further found that the Juvenile Court Act's remedial purpose was not exclusive to the minor, but also recognized a parent's right to an impartial judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the parents' motion for substitution of judge as of right.

 

566 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mayhall


NO. 5-95-0359


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


291 Ill. App. 3d 650; 684 N.E.2d 174; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 581; 225 Ill. Dec. 699



August 18, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 94-CF-359. Honorable Phillip J. Kardis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which convicted him of the unlawful removal of a manufacturer's identification number in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-103(a)(2) (1994). Defendant was sentenced to two years' probation and ordered to pay court costs and restitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed as a mechanic by a car dealership. The owner directed him to replace the front clip of a wrecked car with the front clip from another car. Defendant welded the parts together. The front clip and the car contained different vehicle identification numbers (VIN). The owner directed him to attach the VIN from the car to the one stamped on the front clip, so that the VIN was consistent. The jury returned a guilty verdict, and the trial court concluded that the alteration of the VIN number was an attempt to defraud the public by hiding the fact that the car was a mixture of two cars that were welded together. On appeal, defendant asserted that § 5/1-103(a)(2) was unconstitutional because it did not require a criminal purpose and constituted a punishment of innocent conduct. The court distinguished case law presented by defendant because the offenses from the cases were based on a person's mere possession of an improper item. Defendant was knowingly responsible for the alteration of the VIN. The court rejected defendant's assertion that the punishment was disproportionate to the crime because defendant had knowledge that the car was to be sold to the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful removal of manufacturer's identification number and the sentence imposed.

Lacny v. Police Bd.


No. 1-94-3160


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


291 Ill. App. 3d 397; 683 N.E.2d 1265; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 541; 225 Ill. Dec. 602



August 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Albert Green, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered an order dismissing an administrative review action brought by plaintiff police officer following the officer's failure to comply with the relevant statutory requirements of the Administrative Review Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-103 et seq. (1994). The officer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent of police filed charges against an officer before the Police Board of the City of Chicago. The officer filed an action for administrative review within the 35 days required by the Act. The officer named the Police Board of the City of Chicago as a defendant, but failed to name the superintendent of police. The board filed a motion to dismiss that was granted. The lower court dismissed the case. The officer sought review, contending that the provision of the administrative review law, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-103 et seq. (1994), that limited its application to municipalities with a population of 500,000 or less was unconstitutional. The court agreed with this contention, finding that no rational difference of situation or condition existed between the complaints filed by plaintiffs in Chicago and complaints filed by plaintiffs outside Chicago, since both are allowed to file complaints for administrative review in the first instance. As a result, the court held that the lower court erred in dismissing the officer's complaint and denying leave to amend. The court held that the language of the act violated the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and granted the officer leave to amend his complaint.

Loop Mortg. Corp. v. County of Cook


No. 1-95-3830


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff deed filer, on behalf of itself and a class of others (deed filer), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant county and recorder of deeds' (recorder) motion to dismiss the deed filer's action that sought a declaration that an ordinance that provided for the recording of deeds was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance provided for the preparation and filing of a tax billing information form in order to have facilitated the distribution of real estate tax bills to the current owner of record. The deed filer alleged that the ordinance exceeded the powers granted to home rule counties by the Illinois constitution. The trial court dismissed the deed filer's amended complaint with prejudice because it found that the complaint failed to state a cause of action, there was no evidence of any deceptive practice or fraudulent concealment, and the home rule provisions of the Illinois constitution were not violated by the ordinance. The court affirmed the dismissal. The court held that the efficient operation of the collector's office pertained to county government and affairs and was therefore a proper subject of regulation under the home rule provision of the constitution. The court also determined that the ordinance did not change the process by which the taxes were collected and it did not impact or implicate the interests of other governmental taxing bodies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the deed filer's amended complaint that alleged that the ordinance was invalid.

People v. Tracy


No. 3-96-0997


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


291 Ill. App. 3d 145; 683 N.E.2d 182; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 506; 225 Ill. Dec. 238


June 11, 1997, SUBMITTED  
July 18, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 20, 1997. Released for Publication August 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, La Salle County, Illinois. No. 96--TR--4336. Honorable William Balestri, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, La Salle County (Illinois), which convicted her of passing a school bus that was stopped for the purpose of receiving or discharging pupils under § 11--1414(a) of the Rules of the Road, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11--1414(a) (1996). Plaintiff, the People of the State of Illinois, argued that it did not err when it failed to appoint a special prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appeared at a first return date for a charge against her daughter. She and her husband approached the state's attorney and told him that their daughter was not there because she lived in Chicago. Defendant voluntarily stated that it was not right that her daughter had been charged because she was the person who passed the school buses. Defendant argued that the circuit court should have granted her motion to suppress the statement because it was a part of plea negotiations and because she had not been informed of her Miranda rights. The circuit court noted that defendant had not been charged before she made her statement. It also found that the state's attorney did not elicit the statement. On appeal, the court found that defendant's voluntary and spontaneous statement regarding a charge against her daughter was clearly not part of a plea discussion. It also noted that entitlement to a Miranda warning is triggered only when a defendant is subjected to custodial interrogation or otherwise deprived of her freedom. Her statement, which was voluntarily, was admissible at trial. The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court. The circuit court did not abuse its discretion when it refused to appoint a special prosecutor because an assistant state's attorney testified as a prosecution witness.

People v. Stults


No. 2-96-0946


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


291 Ill. App. 3d 71; 683 N.E.2d 521; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 512; 225 Ill. Dec. 353



July 18, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 3, 1997. Released for Publication September 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 95--CM--636. Honorable George J. Bakalis, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) of practicing nursing without a license in violation of the Illinois Nursing Act of 1987 (act), 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 65/1 et seq. (1996). She challenged her conviction, alleging that the evidence was legally insufficient and that the trial court erred in excluding certain testimony.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in limiting her cross-examination of an expert witness upon the objection of the prosecution, that she was not proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, and that the provisions of the act prohibiting the unlicensed practice of nursing were unconstitutional. The appellate court determined that appellant's attempt to cross-examine the expert was properly prohibited because the witness indicated only expertise with regard to the requirements of the act, not any knowledge as to the permissible duties of a medical assistant, which was the nature of the testimony sought by appellant. The court further determined that there was sufficient evidence of appellant's guilt because there was testimony that she performed the duties of a nurse without being licensed and asserted no basis for authority to perform those functions under any statute. The court further held that the act was not unconstitutionally overly broad as asserted by appellant because the prohibitions were clearly spelled out in the act's provisions, but permitted the nursing functions to be performed by properly licensed persons.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed.

People v. Rand


No. 1-95-2451


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


291 Ill. App. 3d 431; 683 N.E.2d 1243; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 500; 225 Ill. Dec. 580



July 7, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dennis Porter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which after a jury trial, convicted him of stalking, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-7.3 (1994).


OVERVIEW: In challenging the judgment which convicted him of stalking, defendant claimed that: (1) the trial court erred in refusing his waiver of a jury trial; (2) the stalking statute, 720 Ill. Gen. Stat. 5/12-7.3 (1994), was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad; (3) the trial court erred in not holding an evidentiary hearing on defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of trial counsel; and (4) the stalking instruction was improper because it did not include language on defendant's claim of self-defense. The court found that because defendant's attempted jury waiver was made after the jury was impaneled and sworn, whether to accept it was within the trial court's discretion, which it did not abuse. The court found that the stalking statute adequately set forth what conduct was and was not lawful, and was sufficiently narrow to prevent arbitrary enforcement; hence, the court rejected the vagueness and overbreadth claims. The court found that an evidentiary hearing was not required on the ineffective assistance of counsel claim, and that defendant did not show plain error with respect to the jury instruction, which was necessary because he had waived the issue by not objecting at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of stalking.

 

572 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nwosu


No. 1-94-3623


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


289 Ill. App. 3d 487; 683 N.E.2d 148; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 448; 225 Ill. Dec. 204



June 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 5, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 92 CR 14394. Honorable Marcus R. Salone, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, the court was instructed to reconsider its prior decision affirming defendant's conviction for controlled substance trafficking from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) based on a subsequent case, which held that the good faith exception did not apply to a search based on a statute later found to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of controlled substance trafficking. He appealed, claiming that the cocaine found in his apartment was inadmissible because the search was based on an anticipatory search warrant not then authorized by statute. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that the good faith exception applied. Based on a subsequent case, the state supreme court vacated the court's decision and remanded the case for reconsideration. The court again affirmed the conviction. The case upon which the supreme court relied held that the good faith exception did not apply to a search pursuant to a warrant issued under a statute later found to be unconstitutional. In the instant case, the statute providing for anticipatory warrants, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/108-3 (1992), was not determined to be unconstitutional. Rather, the statute was found to be ambiguous. Thus, the case relied upon by the supreme court did not prohibit application of the good faith exception to the instant case. Assessing the credibility of witnesses was a function reserved to the trier of fact. Thus, the trial court's decision to believe the testimony of the officers over that of defendant was not disturbed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Presley v. P&S Grain Co.


NO. 5-96-0400


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


289 Ill. App. 3d 453; 683 N.E.2d 901; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 430; 225 Ill. Dec. 398



June 25, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 94-L-103. Honorable William H. Wilson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant agriculture center challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of WIlliamson County, Illinois, which ordered it to pay damages to plaintiff association, for indemnification of breach of warranty under the Uniform Commercial Code, 810 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-607(5) (1994). Association as defendant challenged the same judgment ordering it to pay damages to plaintiff grain company, pursuant to § 2-607(5) of the UCC.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff buyer who contracted with defendant seller to buy seeds filed suit against seller for breach of express and implied warranties when seeds did not germinate. Seller purchased the seeds from defendant association, which had a limited liability provision. Association purchased seeds from center and delivered them directly to buyer. Seller counterclaimed against buyer and association. Association filed a third party claim for indemnification against center. The trial court awarded damages: to buyer from seller; to seller from association; and to association from center. Association and center appealed. The court found center participated only after it had no further recourse. The contract between association and center was between two Missouri residents and, therefore, there was no making or performance of a contract substantially connected with Illinois. The delivery of the seeds to seller was not sufficient contact. Thus, the court found that center was not subject to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-209(a)(7) (1994), of the long-arm statute. Further, mutuality of agreement to limit liability to the purchase price of the seeds was not present between seller and association.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and vacated in part.

People v. Robles


No. 2-95-0527


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


288 Ill. App. 3d 935; 682 N.E.2d 194; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 411; 224 Ill. Dec. 633


February 11, 1997, SUBMITTED  
June 20, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 93--CF--0805. Honorable John J. Nelligan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied his motion for a new trial after he was convicted of murder and the solicitation of murder for hire when the jury found him guilty but mentally ill on all counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the Illinois guilty but mentally ill (GBMI) statute, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115--4(j) (1992), violated state and federal guarantees of due process. The court held that: (1) the GBMI statute violated defendant's due process rights by encouraging compromise verdicts because the GBMI verdict misled and confused jurors into believing they could assign a lower level of culpability, and a correspondingly lower level of punishment, to a mentally ill defendant; and (2) the allocation of the burden of proof under the current version of the GBMI statute resulted in defendant being required to prove something that was fundamentally at odds with his defense of insanity because in order to obtain a GBMI conviction, defendant had to prove the existence of a culpable state of mind which he had maintained throughout the trial did not exist. The imposition of conflicting burdens upon defendant was fundamentally unfair and placed him in an untenable position, depriving him of his due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that denied defendant's motion for a new trial and remanded the cause for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

People v. Electronic Plating Co.


No. 1-96-1064


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


291 Ill. App. 3d 328; 683 N.E.2d 465; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 408; 225 Ill. Dec. 297



June 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 20, 1997. As Modified On Denial Of Rehearing August 21, 1997. Rehearing Denied August 18, 1997. Released for Publication August 21, 1997. Certiorari Denied March 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2172.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94--CR--10434. Honorable Eugene Campion, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted a motion to suppress filed by defendants, a company and its officials, on grounds that the Metropolitan Water Reclamation District (district) agents obtained evidence in violation of the Fourth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The district obtained samples from a manhole station at the company. The district installed a surreptitious probe 24 feet down from the sewer line. The district did not obtain permission to install this second probe. The district found evidence of contamination, and defendants were charged with conspiracy and hazardous waste violations. Prior to trial, defendants filed a motion to suppress evidence, contending that the evidence recovered by the district was illegally obtained in violation of the Fourth Amendment. The trial court granted the motion to suppress. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court concluded that the company did not have an objectively reasonable expectation of privacy in the wastewaters contained in the sewer connection that was searched, and, therefore, there was no search subject to a search warrant. Because there was no Fourth Amendment search or seizure, the court did not consider the administrative inspection exception of the warrant clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision granting defendants' motion to suppress evidence obtained by the district's agents in a trial against defendants on conspiracy and hazardous waste charges.

Chicago Southshore & S. Bend R.R. v. Northern Ind. Commuter Transp. Dist.


No. 1-96-0358, Cons. 1-96-2757


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


289 Ill. App. 3d 533; 682 N.E.2d 156; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 399; 224 Ill. Dec. 595



June 18, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 15, 1997. Released for Publication August 5, 1997.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Indiana transportation district sought review of the judgments of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the Indiana transportation district's jurisdictional argument, confirmed the arbitration award between the Indiana transportation district and plaintiff partnership, and denied the Indiana transportation district's motion to modify or vacate the judgment confirming the award.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana transportation district (district) and the partnership, located in Illinois, entered into a contract to purchase the assets of a railroad. A dispute arose between the parties, and the district invoked the arbitration provisions in the contract. The arbitration took place in Illinois. The district challenged a portion of the award in Indiana. The Indiana court held that it did not have jurisdiction. The partnership filed a motion to confirm the award in the Illinois trial court. The trial court confirmed the award. Subsequently, the Indiana court of appeals reversed the Indiana trial court and held that Indiana courts did have jurisdiction. Based on the Indiana court of appeals decision, the district filed a petition to vacate or modify the order, which was denied. If the Illinois court had not accepted jurisdiction, the partnership would then have had no forum for enforcing the award. The decision of the trial court to confirm the award was not in derogation of any Indiana decision and thus, it did not abridge the Full Faith and Credit Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's confirmation of the arbitration award and denial of the district's motion to modify or vacate the award.

Du Page County Collector for the Year 1993 v. 1212 Associates-MB Mgmt. Co. (In re Du Page County Collector for the Year 1993)


No. 2-96-1250


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


288 Ill. App. 3d 480; 681 N.E.2d 135; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 381; 224 Ill. Dec. 153



June 11, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 94--TX--10028. Honorable John W. Darrah, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county collector challenged the judgment on the pleadings in favor of appellee objectors granted by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) in a tax objection case challenging the validity of taxes levied for building and equipment for a public library.


OVERVIEW: A public library district levied a building and equipment tax. The objectors paid the tax under protest and filed a timely objection. The trial court held that the levy violated § 18-190(a) of the Tax Cap Act, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 200/18-190(a) (1994) because it had not been approved by direct referendum. The county collector appealed. The court reversed the judgment. Section 18-190(a) applied only to rates which were newly authorized by statute or rate limits that where increased by statute. For years, public library districts were authorized to levy a building and maintenance tax at a rate of 0.02 percent. Because the tax was authorized prior to the levy at issue herein, the tax was not a new rate. Moreover, the tax rate was not increased. Thus, § 18-190 did not apply. The public library district's authority to impose taxes did not expire annually merely because it was required to pass an ordinance each year a tax was levied. The tax was not an additional tax because § 18-190 had a different purpose than taxes levied under the Public Library Act, 75 Ill. Comp. Stat. 16/35-5(a) (1994).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for the objectors and remanded the case with directions for the entry of an order overruling the objections to the public library's tax levy.

Steward v. Crissell


No. 1-96-2444


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


289 Ill. App. 3d 66; 681 N.E.2d 1040; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 374; 224 Ill. Dec. 419

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Philip Fleischman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator sought review of the order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted judgment to appellees, truck driver and truck owner, in appellant's action for negligence in the death of her husband.


OVERVIEW: Appellant administrator's husband died after striking the tractor-trailer of appellees, driver and owner, which was partially blocking the roadway. A toxicology report showed a .162 alcohol concentration in appellant's husband's blood. Appellant filed an action alleging that appellees were negligent and sought to bar the admission of the toxicology report. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment on the jury's verdict for appellees. The court held that because appellees provided a certified record, which the medical examiner kept in the ordinary course of business, and the preparer of the record was available to both parties, they had met the foundational requirements to admit the toxicology report. The court found that appellant failed to establish a violation of those statutory requirements; thus the toxicology report was properly admitted as a public record. Finally, the court held that comments made by appellees' attorney were not inappropriate, did not grossly mischaracterize appellant's arguments and did not amount to a personal attack on appellant's attorney.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellees, truck driver and owner, holding that the toxicology report was properly admitted as a public record and that appellees laid a complete foundation for the introduction of that report.

Heidenhain Corp. v. Doherty


No. 1-96-1781


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


288 Ill. App. 3d 852; 681 N.E.2d 59; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 333; 224 Ill. Dec. 77



May 29, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 2, 1997. As Corrected July 7, 1997. Released for Publication July 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE DOROTHY KIRIE KINNAIRD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the employer's action against defendant Director of the Illinois Department of Employment Security seeking a refund of overpayments of unemployment insurance assessments.


OVERVIEW: The employer overpaid unemployment insurance assessments. The employer had received credit for the overpayments, but the credit was later removed. The employer complained to the director, but the director would not hear the claim because the employer had waited too long. The employer sued the director in a class action suit. It contended that the director had improperly refused to return to it and other class members credits which had previously been given. The trial court dismissed the suit because the employer did not pursue its administrative remedies. The court affirmed. The director stopped giving and rolling over credits when the law changed, requiring the director to pay interest on refunds of erroneously paid contributions, under 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2201.1 (1992). The employer did not file a claim within the three-year limit of § 2201. The employer did not have an independent lawsuit for damages. Stripped of excess verbiage, the employer's lawsuit was an attempt to obtain a refund of the employer's overpayments. Failure to exhaust administrative remedies was fatal to the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the employer's lawsuit against the director seeking a refund of overpayments of unemployment insurance assessments.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. Nos. 96--MH--285, 96--MH--287. Honorable James C. Hallock, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant incompetent sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted respondent state's motion to involuntarily admit the incompetent to a mental facility, pursuant to Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-100 et seq. (1994), and granted the state's motion to administer psychotropic medication pursuant to 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. para. 5/2-107.1 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The state filed a motion to involuntarily admit the incompetent to a mental facility, pursuant to the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-100 et seq. (1994). The state also filed a motion to administer psychotropic medication pursuant to 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. para. 5/2-107.1 (1994). Without the incompetent being present, the trial court granted both motions, and the incompetent sought review. The court determined that the incompetent's procedural due process rights were violated because she was not allowed to attend the hearing determining her civil commitment, a deprivation of her life and liberty. The court held that 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-806(a) was unconstitutional because it allowed a hearing to take place without the incompetent being present. The court further found that 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-806(b) was unconstitutional because, although it allowed the incompetent to refuse to attend the hearing, it failed to ensure that such refusal was made knowingly or intelligently by the individual, who was aware of her due process rights. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment of the trial court, which, without the presence of the incompetent, granted the state's motions to admit the incompetent to a mental facility, pursuant to the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, and to administer psychotropic medication to the incompetent.
