State Farm Ins. Co. v. Gebbie


No. 1-96-2774


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


288 Ill. App. 3d 640; 681 N.E.2d 595; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 299; 224 Ill. Dec. 280



May 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Sidney A. Jones, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County Plaintiff insurance company, as subrogee of plaintiff subrogor filed a complaint against defendant driver seeking recovery of property damage to the subrogor's vehicle. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted a motion by the insurance company to bar the driver from rejecting an arbitration award after he failed to appear and the driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver contended on appeal that he was barred from presenting any evidence at the arbitration, and the insurance company stated that the driver had failed to complete discovery or seek to vacate the court's order barring him from presenting evidence. The driver was represented by counsel at the arbitration hearing but did not attend personally. The driver contended that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 90(g) which allowed the sanction of a bar to rejecting an arbitration award for failure to participate in mandatory arbitration 45 Ill. 2d R. 90(g). The court disagreed, finding that Rule 90(g) was not unconstitutional and not violative of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1004A. The circuit court's order, which gave notice that the driver's evidence would be barred if he did not comply with discovery, therefore was within its province and the circuit court did not abuse its discretion by imposing a sanction that was allowed under the Supreme Court Rules.


OUTCOME: The circuit court judgment was affirmed.

 

583 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Caterpillar Fin. Servs. Corp. v. Whitley


No. 3-94-0830


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


288 Ill. App. 3d 389; 680 N.E.2d 1082; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 306; 223 Ill. Dec. 879


December 12, 1995, SUBMITTED  
May 19, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 92-CH-42. Honorable John A. Barra, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the judgment of Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) in favor of appellee department of revenue in appellant's action to recover taxes paid under protest. Appellant argued that appellee's "water's edge" combined reporting method of apportioning income unconstitutionally discriminated against interest and royalty payments from foreign subsidiaries of domestic parent corporations doing business in the state.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer challenged the decision of the trial court in favor of appellee department of revenue in appellant's action to recover taxes paid under protest. The court held that it had jurisdiction over appellant's appeal. A taxpayer was entitled to pay under protest into the protest fund and subsequently raise any legitimate claim to establish its right to refund. The court held that appellee's "water's edge" combined reporting method did not unconstitutionally discriminate against royalties and interest payments received by appellant's domestic entities from its foreign subsidiaries. Under the "water's edge" method of combined reporting, royalty and interest paying foreign subsidiaries were similar to non-related domestic third-party customers of the taxpayer in that none of the income of the foreign subsidiary or the non-related third-party was included in the income allocable to the state. Therefore, the foreign subsidiaries were similar to domestic entities and no discrimination resulted. Accordingly, the judgment of the lower court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court in favor of appellee department of revenue was affirmed. Under the "water's edge" method of combined reporting, royalty and interest paying foreign subsidiaries were treated similarly to domestic entities in that no income of the foreign subsidiary or non-related third-party was included in the income allocated to the state. Accordingly, no discrimination occurred.

 

584 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brackett


No. 2-95-0524


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


288 Ill. App. 3d 12; 679 N.E.2d 1285; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 284; 223 Ill. Dec. 512


April 17, 1997, SUBMITTED  
May 13, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 17, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 94--CF--1370. Honorable Ronald B. Mehling, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted her of aggravated robbery, pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-5 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery, and she filed a timely notice of appeal. Defendant contended that the aggravated robbery statute, § 5/18-5, was unconstitutionally vague and that she was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and held that § 5/18-5 provided sufficiently definite standards to guide officers and fact finders and to minimize the danger of arbitrary enforcement. The court ruled that § 5/18-5 did not give the police inordinate discretion in determining whether to make an arrest because the statute defined criminal conduct in terms of the acts' effects upon the victim's state of mind. The court held that the totality of the circumstances demonstrated that the showup identification was sufficiently reliable because the witness had an opportunity to observe defendant during the robbery, defendant closely matched the witness's description, and the identification procedures occurred approximately two hours after the offense. The evidence, taken as a whole, was sufficient to establish defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery.

 

585 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cavins


NO. 5-95-0711


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


288 Ill. App. 3d 173; 679 N.E.2d 1276; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 274; 223 Ill. Dec. 503



May 9, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 94-CF-237. Honorable Sherri L.E. Tungate, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois), in which he was sentenced to an extended term of 10 years imprisonment after he entered a plea of guilty to the charge of burglary. Defendant filed a motion to reconsider his sentence and the trial court denied the motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to the charge of burglary in reliance on an admonishment by the trial court that in doing so, he could receive a sentence of six to thirty years imprisonment. At defendant's sentencing hearing, the state introduced a certified copy of defendant's conviction for a class C felony in Iowa, to which defendant did not object. Based upon that and other evidence, the trial court determined that defendant was a candidate for an extended-term sentence and imposed a 10 year term of imprisonment. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed, holding that because defendant was advised upon entering his guilty plea that he was subject to the range of penalty within which he was ultimately sentenced and he did not thereafter file a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, defendant was not entitled to relief from his sentence. The court found that defendant was given the opportunity to withdraw his plea and was not precluded from doing so within the required 30-day period. The court concluded that defendant failed to show how the extended-term statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him, but found that the trial court's interpretation was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence and affirmed the judgment of the trial court in sentencing defendant to an extended term of 10 years imprisonment after he entered a plea of guilty to the charge of burglary.

Best Bus Joint Venture v. Board of Educ.


No. 1-96-2927


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


288 Ill. App. 3d 770; 681 N.E.2d 570; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 278; 224 Ill. Dec. 255



May 9, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN MADDEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, unsuccessful bidders, sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in favor of defendants, the Board of Education for the City of Chicago and successful bidders, in their action challenging the Board of Education's award of bus contracts for the 1996-97 through 1998-99 school years.


OVERVIEW: After the Board of Education of the City of Chicago applied a two-percent local business preference (LBP) to award bus contracts for the 1996-97 and 1998-99 school years, the unsuccessful bidders, whose bid as a joint venture was the lowest bid but for application of the LBP, filed an action to compel the Board of Education to apply the LBP to their bid or, in the alternative, to invalidate the LBP. The court ruled that the two-percent LBP had no proper legislative authority, was an arbitrary and capricious delegation of power to a municipal unit, and was therefore unconstitutional. The court further ruled that the unsuccessful bidders were estopped from challenging the validity of the two-percent LBP because they did not so within a reasonable time where they were aware of the adoption of the LPB in March 1996, knew that they did not qualify for the LBP, and did not seek to invalidate the LBP until July 1996, when the awards were made, and also where the Board of Education as well as the successful bidders who had been awarded the contracts had incurred obligations in reliance on the award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the Board of Education of the City of Chicago and the successful bidders in the action brought by the unsuccessful bidders to challenge the award of bus contracts for the 1996-97 and 1998-99 school years, ruling that the unsuccessful bidders were estopped from challenging the validity of a two-percent local business preference.

People v. Carlson

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which ordered evidence suppressed that had been recovered during a search of defendant's vehicle pursuant to an anticipatory search warrant.


OVERVIEW: Anticipatory search warrants were held to be invalid in Illinois and, therefore, the trial court excluded the evidence obtained from defendant's apartment. The state argued that the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule should have been applied. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the good-faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied when the police relied on an anticipatory search warrant that was issued before such warrants were declared to be statutorily invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order suppressing the evidence and remanded the cause back to the trial court.

People v. Beard


1-95-3682


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


287 Ill. App. 3d 935; 679 N.E.2d 456; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 213; 223 Ill. Dec. 271



April 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court Cook County. Honorable John E. Morrisey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which sentenced him to concurrent 15 year terms for aggravated vehicular hijacking, armed violence predicated on vehicular hijacking, armed robbery, and armed violence predicated on robbery.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction for aggravated vehicular hijacking, armed violence predicated on vehicular hijacking, armed robbery, and armed violence predicated on robbery, the court sentenced defendant to concurrent 15 year terms for each offense. On appeal, defendant argued that the sentences for armed violence were unconstitutionally disproportionate. The court reversed defendant's convictions and sentences for armed violence, holding that the elements of aggravated vehicular hijacking, which carried a minimum sentence of seven years, were identical to those of armed violence predicated on vehicular hijacking, which carried a minimum sentence of 15 years. Furthermore, the elements of armed robbery, which carried a minimum sentence of six years, were identical to those of armed violence predicated on robbery, which carried a minimum sentence of 15 years. The court found that the disparities in the penalties for armed violence predicated on both the robbery and vehicular hijacking while armed with a category 1 weapon were unconstitutionally disproportionate. The court also ruled that under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a) the state had no right to challenge the sentences imposed.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions and sentences for armed violence, vacated the sentences imposed for the remaining offenses, and remanded for resentencing.

People v. Koger


No. 3-96-0334


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


287 Ill. App. 3d 764; 679 N.E.2d 105; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 211; 223 Ill. Dec. 161


March 5, 1997, SUBMITTED  
April 16, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] THIS OPINION UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23 ORDER.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 30, 1997.
Appeal denied by People v. Koger, 174 Ill. 2d 580, 686 N.E.2d 1168, 1997 Ill. LEXIS 1301, 227 Ill. Dec. 12 (1997)
Related proceeding at People v. Koger, 2016 IL App (3d) 130661-U, 2016 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 718 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 95-CF-696. Honorable Robert Adcock, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois), after a jury found him guilty of two counts of first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to natural life in prison for the murders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two accomplices committed an armed robbery of two men. One of the accomplices killed the victims while defendant stood nearby with a shotgun. A jury convicted defendant of armed robbery and two counts of first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to natural life in prison for the two murders. He sought review of the murder convictions and his sentence. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's argument that the mandatory life imprisonment provision contained in § 5-8-1(a)(1)(c) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1994), violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 because it did not consider his rehabilitative potential. It noted that similar constitutional challenges had been rejected in those situations where the defendant was either the actual killer or an accomplice to the killer. Furthermore, the focus of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1994) was the nature of the homicides, not the defendant's role in them. Therefore, the court found that Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 was not violated when 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1994) was applied to those defendants found guilty by accountability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' murder convictions and sentence.

State Bank of Countryside v. City of Chicago


No. 1-96-2185


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


287 Ill. App. 3d 904; 679 N.E.2d 435; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 219; 223 Ill. Dec. 250



April 15, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 94 CH 9861. The Honorable Dorothy Kirie Kinnaird, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Chicago), which entered judgment for appellant city on the landowner's request for a declaration that the city's zoning ordinance containing manufacturing classifications was unconstitutional as it applied to their property.


OVERVIEW: Landowners sought to have their property reclassified from restricted manufacturing to general residence. The city refused. On appeal, the landowners claimed, inter alia, that the manufacturing classification on their property did not bear any substantial relation to the public health, comfort, morals, safety, or general welfare. The court disagreed, holding that to successfully attack the validity of a zoning ordinance, it was not enough to show that the property could reasonably have been zoned differently. Additionally, although plaintiffs might have shown that the subject property could reasonably have been zoned R-4, that was not enough to prove that the property's existing classification was arbitrary and unreasonable. Instead, their concession that the M1-1 restriction was consistent with other uses in the area supported a conclusion that the existing zoning was valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying landowners a change in the classification of their property was affirmed.

Vernon Hills III Ltd. Pshp. v. St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co.


No. 2-96-0724


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


287 Ill. App. 3d 303; 678 N.E.2d 374; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 188; 222 Ill. Dec. 762


November 19, 1996, SUBMITTED  
April 3, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. Nos. 95--CH--587, 95--CH--628, 95--CH--903. Honorable Peter M. Trobe, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lienholder challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff property owner on its claim for a declaratory judgment and ruled that defendant forfeited its mechanic's lien by failing to commence an action to foreclose the lien within 30 days after receipt of plaintiff's written demand to sue, as required by section 34 of the Mechanics Lien Act, 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/34.


OVERVIEW: After defendant lienholder filed a mechanic's lien against plaintiff's shopping center, it received a certified letter from plaintiff stating that filing the lien constituted a breach of the construction contract and demanding that defendant either immediately release the lien or bring suit to enforce it. Plaintiff then sought a declaratory judgment that defendant forfeited its mechanic's lien by failing to commence an action to foreclose its lien within 30 days after receipt of plaintiff's written demand to sue, as required by section 34 of the Mechanic's Lien Act (act), 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/34. The trial court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and declared the lien null and void. On appeal, the court affirmed. Plaintiff's letter was a written demand to sue under the act, even though it did not reference the act or the requirement that defendant file a lien enforcement suit within 30 days. Plaintiff was not estopped by reason of the fact that it participated in settlement negotiations and requested defendant's help with paper work after sending out the demand letter. The time limitations in the act were jurisdictional and not subject to waiver or estoppel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiff property owner because plaintiff's letter to defendant lienholder satisfied the written demand requirements of the mechanics' lien statute and triggered the tolling of the 30-day limitation period.

ZUBATY v. BEAR


No. 1-95-3757


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


288 Ill. App. 3d 284; 681 N.E.2d 1; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 180; 224 Ill. Dec. 19



March 31, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1997. Released for Publication June 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable R. Morgan Hamilton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied his motions to stay an agreed upon child support order issued under the Revised Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act (RURESA), 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 15/11 (1994), and for injunctive relief to require petitioner mother to provide full access to their children. The father also challenged the constitutionality of 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 20/23 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The mother's petition for child support, which was filed in Florida, was submitted to the trial court in Illinois, whereupon the parties consented to an agreed order requiring the father to pay weekly child support for their children. The father sought to stay the agreed RURESA support order until the mother allowed him full access to his children. In the alternative, he requested that the trial court declare 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 20/23 (1994) unconstitutional. The trial court denied the requested relief, holding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the father alleged that the trial court improperly denied his motion seeking injunctive and other relief and improperly denied him an evidentiary hearing on the issues. In affirming the trial court's order, the court held that the trial court properly determined Florida, rather than Illinois, was the appropriate forum in which to raise the father's claims regarding visitation rights. 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 20/23, 20/32 (1994) specifically provided a limitation on subject matter and personal jurisdiction, and those limitations were rationally related to a legitimate state interest in enforcing child support obligations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied the father his requested relief and established a payment plan for child support arrearages owed to the mother.

People ex rel. Schacht v. Prestige Cas. Co.


No. 1-95-3058


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


287 Ill. App. 3d 577; 678 N.E.2d 785; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 178; 222 Ill. Dec. 913



March 31, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 12, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 CH 3504. Honorable Thomas P. Durkin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law firm sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found § 205 of the Insurance Code, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/205(1) (1994), to be constitutional. The law firm, who represented the insurance company, had filed a petition for attorneys' fees in the liquidation action brought against the insurance company by appellees, the Director of Insurance and the Illinois Insurance Guaranty Fund.


OVERVIEW: On the eve of trial in the liquidation action, the law firm filed a petition for attorneys' fees for trial preparation. The law firm challenged the constitutionality of § 205 of the Insurance Code, which governed the way assets of an insurance company were distributed after liquidation. General creditors were listed fifth in priority and included claims for attorneys' fees incurred by the insurance company in a liquidation action. The trial court found the scheme under § 205 to be constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that § 205 was not unconstitutional. The law firm had standing to bring the appeal because the law firm's injury-in-fact was clear; the law firm claimed over $ 50,000 worth of pre-trial work, and there was a possibility that it would not be paid. On the constitutionality issue, the court found that, although the insurance company had a constitutional right to obtain counsel, § 205's impediment to attorneys' fees was not an unconstitutional infringement of the right to counsel. Because the right to pay attorneys first was not a constitutionally protected right, the state could properly enact a scheme that ranked attorneys with other creditors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found that a provision of the Insurance Code, which governed the distribution of assets of an insurance company after liquidation, was not unconstitutional.

 

594 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Simester


Nos. 1-94-4064, 1-94-4065, Cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


287 Ill. App. 3d 420; 678 N.E.2d 710; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 159; 222 Ill. Dec. 838



March 27, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 12, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Paul J. Nealis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant husband and wife of two counts of criminal neglect of an elderly person in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-21-a(2) and (3) (1992). Defendants were thereafter sentenced to 30 months' probation and 1,000 hours of community service. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was the wife's elderly uncle and he resided in a room in defendants' home. Paramedics found the victim in a coma in a fetal position in his room, covered with feces and urine. The medical evidence established that the victim had no nutritional intake for at least one week, that his rigid fetal position took at least two weeks to develop, and that his deep coma had to have existed for several days before his hospitalization. The court upheld the convictions. First, defendants waived their right to argue that the statute under which they were prosecuted was unconstitutionally vague because they failed to sufficiently develop their argument or provide authority. Second, the statute did not violate equal protection because it exempted professionally licensed caregivers. Such caregivers were already regulated by the state. Thus, there existed a rational basis for exempting them. Third, the evidence overwhelmingly demonstrated that defendants were guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Finally, the statute specifically precluded as a defense a defendant's alleged mistake of fact as to whether the victim was disabled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences.

597 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Link by Link v. Venture Stores


NO. 5-96-0123


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


286 Ill. App. 3d 977; 677 N.E.2d 486; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 103; 222 Ill. Dec. 283



March 7, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 94-L-485. Honorable Randall Bono, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant store sought review of a judgment entered in favor of appellee infant by the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois). The trial court denied the store's motion to dismiss the infant's negligence action that sought to recover for injuries received while seated in a defective car seat sold by the store. The store contended that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-621, as amended, applied retroactively; thus, dismissal was required.


OVERVIEW: The court found that infant had a vested right in her negligence cause of action against store. Store conceded in its brief that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-621, prior to its amendment in 1995, did not affect infant's right to sue store on a negligence theory. The court recognized, prior to the enactment of the amendment at issue, the existence of a common law right for a plaintiff to maintain an action against a non-manufacturer under theories other than strict liability. The court found it was compelled to apply § 2-621 prospectively in order to avoid the unconstitutional result posed by retroactive application of the statute as amended. It was immaterial whether the legislature intended retroactive application of the amendment. The legislature lacked constitutional authority to retroactively enact a law that purported to impair vested rights, despite any expressed legislative intent. The court concluded that § 2-621 as amended did not apply retroactively. Store was not entitled to dismissal of the negligence count based upon § 2-621.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

Walsh v. Property Tax Appeal Bd.


No. 3-95-0813


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


286 Ill. App. 3d 895; 677 N.E.2d 489; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 104; 222 Ill. Dec. 286


September 3, 1996, SUBMITTED  
March 7, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 95-MR-1. Honorable Donald Courson Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County (Illinois), which upheld the decision of defendant State Property Tax Appeal Board, which decided that defendant Tazewell County Board of Review had properly appraised the landowners' property and had not violated Ill. Const. art. IX, § 4 (1970).


OVERVIEW: The townships in Tazewell County had not conducted a true fair market assessment of property within the county for over 20 years. Instead, the townships conducted yearly mass appraisals wherein the increase in value of the property within the whole county was ascertained and every parcel of property was given a proportionate increase based upon that property's historical value as of the last fair market assessment. Thus, many parcels of land were undervalued, including the landowners' property. Following complaints about undervalued land, a small number of parcels, including that of the landowners' were appraised at their true market value. The Board of Review, the Appeal Board, and the lower court upheld the assessment on the landowners' property. The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, holding that § 4 required uniformity in the application of taxes. The court ruled that the fact that the landowners' property was undervalued was irrelevant because the landowners were taxed by the use of a radically different method of assessment than most other township property owners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which held that the landowners' property was correctly assessed. The matter was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

599 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Jost v. Bailey


Nos. 2-96-0695, 2-96-0916 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


286 Ill. App. 3d 872; 676 N.E.2d 1033; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 78; 222 Ill. Dec. 69



February 26, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 28, 1997. Released for Publication March 28, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 95--L--1612. Honorable Stephen E. Walter, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, deceased's parents, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed their wrongful death and survival actions against defendants, county and forest preserve, finding they were immunized by § 5--1(N) of the Snowmobile Registration and Safety Act, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 40/5--1(N) (1994), and § 3--109 of the Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/3--109 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The deceased was a passenger on a snowmobile that was struck by an oncoming snowmobile. The operator of the deceased's mobile crossed lanes in front of the approaching mobile as the marked signs directed. Such a route was expressly prohibited under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 40/5--2(B) (1994). The bridge where the collision occurred was owned and maintained by the county. The parents' second amended complaint alleged that the county and the forest preserve were negligent and wilful and wanton in their approval of a dangerous and unsafe snowmobile trail. The trial court granted the county and forest preserves' motion to dismiss. The parent's appealed. The court concluded that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 40/5--1(N) completely immunized the county and the forest preserve from the allegations contained in the parents' complaint. Further, the court found that the parents failed to allege that the forest preserve had contractually waived the immunities provided under the Snowmobile Act when it purchased insurance. And finally, the court rejected the contention that the purchase of an insurance policy was not a waiver of immunity, absent specific contractual waiver.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the judgment of the trial court granting immunity to the county and forest preserve.

 

600 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Tully v. Edgar


No. 1-95-2426


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


286 Ill. App. 3d 838; 676 N.E.2d 1361; 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 76; 222 Ill. Dec. 157



February 21, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Albert Green, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general sought interlocutory review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied reconsideration of the circuit court's appointment of a private attorney as special attorney general to represent defendant trustee in an action by plaintiff citizen against defendants, public officials and trustees, challenging the University Act, Pub. Act 89-5 (effective Jan. 1, 1996).


OVERVIEW: The University Act (Act), Pub. Act 89-5 (effective Jan. 1, 1996), terminated the unexpired terms of existing elected university trustees and replaced them with appointed trustees. The citizen brought a declaratory action against defendants to challenge the Act. At the request of the trustee, the circuit court appointed a private attorney as special attorney general to represent her and denied appellant's motion for reconsideration. Appellant sought interlocutory review of the order. The court held that (1) under the State Employee Indemnification Act, 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 350/2(b) (1996), elected officials were entitled to retain their own attorneys to represent them without interference from appellant, (2) under 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 350/2(e)(i) (1996), the costs of providing a defense were to be reimbursed, and (3) because appellant had a conflict with the trustee's desire to challenge the constitutionality of the Act, it was proper to appoint private counsel to abate that conflict.


OUTCOME: The order denying the motion for reconsideration was affirmed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.
